Prophethood
beginner
6 min
Sensory Miracles Outside the Prophet's Person
Enumerates sensory miracles external to the Prophet's person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various sensory miracles that occurred externally around the Prophet (peace be upon him) as evidence of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Sensory miracles outside the Prophet's person demonstrate Allah's power through creation.

After discussing miracles within the Prophet's own being, the author now turns to those that occurred outside his body. These events, witnessed by others, serve as clear signs of his prophethood. The following passage enumerates several such miracles, from the splitting of the moon to the testimony of a roasted sheep.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the list of miracles and try to recall their basic details.
Each item in the list is a distinct miracle.
2
Identify categories of miracles
Group the miracles into natural phenomena (moon, water), inanimate objects (tree, stone, wood), animals (camel, sheep, goat), and historical incidents (cloud, Abu Jahl, Umm Ma'bad).
This shows the diversity of miracles.
3
Reflect on literal vs symbolic interpretation
The author presents these as literal events. Consider why some might view them symbolically and how the passage refutes that.
The common misunderstanding is addressed here.
4
Understand the purpose
The number and variety of miracles strengthen the proof of prophethood, as they surpass ordinary human capability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما ما كان خارج ذاته فمن نحو انشقاق القمر، واجتذاب الشجرة، وتسليم الحجر عليه، وشُرب الكثير من الشَّرْب القليل من الماء، ونبع الماء من بين أصابعه، وحنين الخشب، وشكاية الناقة وشهادة الشاة المصلَيَّة، وما كان من السحاب الذي كان يظله قبل مبعثه، وما كان من حال أبي جهل عليه اللعنة وصخرته حين هوى بها إلى رأسه، وما كان من شأن الشاه الحابل ودَرِّها حين مسح بيده الكريمة على ضرعها على ما ذكر في حديث أم معبد.
As for what was outside his being, it includes such things as the splitting of the moon, the drawing of the tree, the greeting of the stone to him, the drinking of many from a small drink of water, the flowing of water from between his fingers, the yearning of the wood, the complaint of the she-camel, the testimony of the roasted sheep, what was of the cloud that shaded him before his mission, what was of the case of Abu Jahl—may the curse be upon him—and his rock when he hurled it at his head, and what was of the affair of the goat of Habal and its milk when he wiped his noble hand on its udder as mentioned in the hadith of Umm Ma'bad.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage enumerates examples of sensory miracles that occurred outside the Prophet's own body. The author lists: the splitting of the moon (inqishāq al-qamar), the tree being drawn to him (ijtidhāb al-shajara), the stone greeting him (taslīm al-hajar), a large number drinking from a small amount of water (shurb al-kathir min al-sharb al-qalil), water flowing from between his fingers (nab' al-mā' min bayn asābi'ihi), the yearning of a piece of wood (hanīn al-khashab), a camel complaining (shikāyat al-nāqa), a roasted sheep testifying (shahādat al-shāt al-musalliya), a cloud that shaded him before his mission, the incident of Abu Jahl's rock, and the goat of Habal that gave milk when the Prophet wiped his hand on its udder, as mentioned in the hadith of Umm Ma'bad. Each of these events is presented as a genuine sensory miracle, clearly different from natural phenomena and beyond human capability.

Key Terms
انشقاق القمر
اجتذاب الشجرة
تسليم الحجر
نبع الماء
حنين الخشب
شكاية الناقة
شهادة الشاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these miracles are symbolic or metaphorical rather than literal physical events.
Correction: The author presents each event as a literal occurrence, supported by hadith, to serve as undeniable evidence of prophethood.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as a miracle outside the Prophet's person in this passage?
A) Splitting of the moon
B) Tree drawing near
C) The Prophet's body radiating light
D) Water flowing from fingers

Key Takeaway
The multiplicity of sensory miracles outside the Prophet's person affirms his prophethood through diverse, witnessed events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage lists ten miracles outside the Prophet's person. Do you believe each one literally happened as described? If so, how does that belief affect the way you treat the natural world around you—do you see it as a sign of Allah's power at every moment?
?
Consider the miracle of the roasted sheep testifying. That sheep was dead and cooked, yet it spoke by Allah's permission. If a dead animal can be brought to testimony, what excuse do you have for not living every moment as if your deeds are witnessed by the One who created even the sheep?
?
The cloud shaded the Prophet before his mission. Allah was caring for him even before he was sent. When you think about your own life before guidance, can you see Allah's hidden care? How will you now consciously rely on that care, especially in moments of difficulty?

Division of Prophetic Signs: Sensory and Rational
The author divides prophetic signs into sensory and rational, and states the three types of sensory signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the twofold division of prophetic signs into sensory and rational, and the three subtypes of sensory miracles.

Core Idea
Prophetic signs are either seen or reasoned; sensory miracles come in three forms.

This passage from Imam Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla presents a foundational classification of the miracles proving prophethood. Before examining the evidence, the author clarifies the types: some are physical wonders, others are rational arguments. The sensory miracles themselves are further categorized, showing the breadth of the Prophet's signs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style; each sentence carries a key idea.
2
Identify the overall division
The author splits prophetic signs into two: sensory and rational. This is the primary division. Underline or note these two terms.
3
Focus on the definition of sensory
Sensory signs are defined as visible wonders that break natural laws and customs, and they were countless for the Prophet. Understand the key features: visible, miraculous, abundant.
The term 'حسية' refers to what is perceived by the senses.
4
Find the three subtypes
Sensory miracles are further divided into three categories: outside his essence, in his essence, and in his character. Locate these three in the text.
These categories cover external events, personal attributes, and moral conduct.
5
Reflect on the classification
Consider why this classification matters for proving prophethood. It shows that miracles encompass all aspects of the Prophet's life, reinforcing his truthfulness comprehensively.
This connects to the broader argument for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آیات رسالته لا تنقسم أولا إلى قسمين حسية وعقلية.
أما الحسية منها : وهي ما يظهره الله تعالى للأعين من العجائب المباينة لمجرى الطبائع والبدائع المفارقة للمعهود من العادة وكان له من ذلك ما لا يحصى كثرة.
وهي أقسام ثلاثة : فمنها ما كان خارج ذاته، ومنها ما كان في ذاته ومنها ما كان في أخلاقه.
The signs of his prophethood are divided first into two categories: sensory and rational. As for the sensory: they are what Allah the Exalted makes appear to the eyes of wonders that are contrary to the course of natural laws and marvels that differ from what is customary, and he had of that an uncountable multitude. They are three divisions: some of them are outside his essence, some of them are in his essence, and some of them are in his character.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies the miracles (ayat) of prophethood. The author begins by stating that these signs are divided into two types: sensory (hissiyya) and rational (aqliyya). He then defines sensory miracles as those visible phenomena that Allah causes to appear to the eyes, which are extraordinary, breaking natural laws and customs. The Prophet had countless such miracles. Then he divides sensory miracles into three categories: first, miracles occurring outside his person (kharij dhatihi) like the splitting of the moon; second, miracles in his person (fi dhatihi) like the seal of prophethood; and third, miracles in his character (fi akhlaqihi) like his perfect manners. This classification shows the comprehensiveness of the Prophet's miracles.

Key Terms
آیات رسالته
حسية
عقلية
خارج ذاته
في ذاته
في أخلاقه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that sensory miracles are the only type of prophetic sign, ignoring rational miracles.
Correction: The author explicitly divides signs into sensory and rational; both are valid and important proofs.

Checkpoint
According to the author, into how many categories are sensory miracles divided?
A) 1
B) 2
C) 3
D) 4

Key Takeaway
The signs of prophethood are divided into sensory and rational, and sensory miracles themselves are of three types: external, personal, and moral.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet’s character is counted as a sensory miracle. Which of your own character traits is furthest from his example, and what specific step will you take this week to begin correcting it?
?
You have seen many sensory signs of God’s power, but the author also mentions rational signs. Are you more convinced by what you see or what you reason? How can you strengthen the aspect you neglect?
?
The Prophet had countless miracles, yet how many have you truly pondered? Name one miracle that has impacted your faith today, and commit to studying one more before the week ends.

Miracles in the Prophet's Essence
Enumeration of sensory miracles in the Prophet's body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various sensory miracles associated with the Prophet's physical being and how they serve as signs of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's very body was a living sign of prophethood.

This passage from Tabsirat al-Adilla presents a series of miraculous phenomena directly connected to the Prophet's person. These are not abstract proofs but tangible, sensory experiences reported by his companions. From the light that preceded his birth to the fragrance of his skin, each miracle reinforces the truth of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own enumeration come through before you interpret.
Notice the sequential listing of miracles.
2
Identify each miracle
The passage lists six distinct miracles: the transmitted light, the seal, the height, the beauty, the fragrance, and the blessed sweat. Find each one and note what is said.
These are sensory, not abstract.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why each of these details is considered a proof of prophethood. What does each miracle tell us about the Prophet's status?
Consider the epistemological weight of sensory evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما كان في ذاته فنحو النور الذي كان ينتقل من ظهر إلى بطن إلى ظهر إلى أن خرج، وما كان من الخاتم بين كتفيه، وما وصف أنه كان ربعة ثم كان لا يزاحم طويلين إلا فاقهما، وما روى أنه نظر إلى وجهه وإلى البدر فكان هو أحسن، وأنه كان أطيب ريحًا من المسك وألين من الحرير، وكان يؤخذ عرقه فينتفع به في الطيب، وقد وصفت خلقته بما لا يعرف أحد يوصف بمثله حسنًا وجمالاً، وروى في وصفه على التفصيل أنه عليه السلام كان أطول من المربوع()، وأقصر من المشذب (٢) عظيم الهامة (٣) رجل (٤) الشعر ، أزهر (٥) اللون، واسع الجبين، أزج (١) الحواجب، أقنى العرنين()، يحسبه من لم يتأمله أشم ()، في عينيه دبح()، وفي سطع، وفي لحيته كثافة، سهل الخدين، ضليع (١١) الفم، مفلج الأسنان، ظاهر الوضاءة، عظيم الصدر، سواء (١٢) البطن، ضخم الكراديس، بعيد ما بين المنكبين، دقيق المسبوبة، طويل الزندين رحب الراحة، شثن (١٣) الكفين سائل الأطراف بادن متماسك، وسيم قسيم فخم مفخم ليس بالجافي ولا المهين وصفه بهذا هند ابن أبي هالة عليه السلام - إذ هو كان ابن خديجة رضي الله عنها من أبي هالة بناس بن زرارة التميمي بين يدي المهاجرين والأنصار بهذه الحلية - وكان وصافًا - فصدق بها. وكذا وصفته أم معبد لزوجها بما يضاهي هذا فلم ينكر عليها.
As for what was in his essence, such as the light that was transmitted from back to womb to back until he emerged, and the seal between his shoulder blades, and what was described that he was of medium height and then he would not be surpassed by tall people except that he surpassed them, and what was narrated that he looked at his face and at the moon and he was more beautiful, and that he had a better fragrance than musk and was softer than silk, and his sweat was taken and used as perfume. His creation was described in such a way that no one is known to be described with similar beauty and handsomeness. And it was narrated in detail that he, peace be upon him, was taller than the medium-height but shorter than the markedly tall, large-headed, with thick hair, fair-skinned with a reddish tint, broad forehead, arched eyebrows, a fine nose bridge such that one who did not examine him would think it was prominent, a slight bow in his eyes, a slight leanness in his nostrils?, thick beard, smooth cheeks, wide mouth, spaced teeth, bright complexion, broad chest, equal belly, large joints, wide between the shoulders, fine fingers, long forearms, broad palms, thick-fingered but soft hands, thick limbs (?), balanced and firm, handsome and dignified, not rough nor contemptible. Hind ibn Abi Hala described him thus, and Umm Ma'bad described him similarly without objection.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage covers the second category of sensory miracles: those in the Prophet's essence (fi dhatihi). First, the author lists miraculous events directly related to his body: the transmission of light through his lineage, the seal of prophethood on his back, his height being perfect, his beauty surpassing the moon, his fragrance better than musk, his softness, and the blessedness of his sweat. Then he provides an elaborate physical description, citing the report of Hind ibn Abi Hala (the son of Khadija from her first marriage) and Umm Ma'bad. This description is extremely detailed, covering his stature, head, hair, complexion, forehead, eyebrows, nose, eyes, cheeks, mouth, teeth, chest, belly, shoulders, fingers, hands, and overall bearing. The purpose is to show that even his physical form was a sign of prophethood, being perfect and without fault, captivating all who saw him.

Key Terms
النور المنتقل
الخاتم بين كتفيه
ربعة
أطيب ريحاً من المسك
ألين من الحرير
عرقه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet's sweat used as?
A) Medicine
B) Perfume
C) Food
D) Water

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's body itself was filled with signs of divine favor and prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that the Prophet's beauty surpassed the moon. When was the last time you truly pondered on his appearance while sending blessings upon him? How can you incorporate that visual into your daily salawat?
?
The Prophet's sweat was used as perfume—a detail that shows his entire being was blessed. What 'ordinary' things of the Prophet do you overlook? Choose one sunnah this week to revive with the intention of connecting to his physical example.

The Prophet's Detailed Physical Description
Detailed physical description of the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed physical description of the Prophet as a sign of his prophethood and a testimony to his perfection.

Core Idea
The Prophet's physical beauty and perfection reflected his inner perfection and prophethood.

This passage provides an extremely detailed description of the Prophet's appearance, based on the testimony of Hind ibn Abi Hala and Umm Ma'bad. Such detailed descriptions serve not only as historical records but also as evidences of his prophethood, as his features were perfectly balanced and captivating.

Guided Path
1
Read the description carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the rich detail sink in.
This is a very detailed account.
2
Identify the main features
The description covers height, head, hair, complexion, forehead, eyebrows, nose, eyes, cheeks, mouth, teeth, chest, belly, shoulders, fingers, hands, and overall bearing. Pick out a few and note how they are described.
Consider the precision of the language.
3
Consider the sources
The passage cites Hind ibn Abi Hala and Umm Ma'bad. Why are these sources considered reliable?
Hint: Hind was a stepson, and Umm Ma'bad was a contemporary.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Why is such a detailed description included in a theological work on prophethood? What does it prove?
Think about the perfection of the Prophet's creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما كان في ذاته فنحو النور الذي كان ينتقل من ظهر إلى بطن إلى ظهر إلى أن خرج، وما كان من الخاتم بين كتفيه، وما وصف أنه كان ربعة ثم كان لا يزاحم طويلين إلا فاقهما، وما روى أنه نظر إلى وجهه وإلى البدر فكان هو أحسن، وأنه كان أطيب ريحًا من المسك وألين من الحرير، وكان يؤخذ عرقه فينتفع به في الطيب، وقد وصفت خلقته بما لا يعرف أحد يوصف بمثله حسنًا وجمالاً، وروى في وصفه على التفصيل أنه عليه السلام كان أطول من المربوع()، وأقصر من المشذب (٢) عظيم الهامة (٣) رجل (٤) الشعر ، أزهر (٥) اللون، واسع الجبين، أزج (١) الحواجب، أقنى العرنين()، يحسبه من لم يتأمله أشم ()، في عينيه دبح()، وفي سطع، وفي لحيته كثافة، سهل الخدين، ضليع (١١) الفم، مفلج الأسنان، ظاهر الوضاءة، عظيم الصدر، سواء (١٢) البطن، ضخم الكراديس، بعيد ما بين المنكبين، دقيق المسبوبة، طويل الزندين رحب الراحة، شثن (١٣) الكفين سائل الأطراف بادن متماسك، وسيم قسيم فخم مفخم ليس بالجافي ولا المهين وصفه بهذا هند ابن أبي هالة عليه السلام - إذ هو كان ابن خديجة رضي الله عنها من أبي هالة بناس بن زرارة التميمي بين يدي المهاجرين والأنصار بهذه الحلية - وكان وصافًا - فصدق بها. وكذا وصفته أم معبد لزوجها بما يضاهي هذا فلم ينكر عليها.
As for what was in his essence, such as the light that was transmitted from back to womb to back until he emerged, and the seal between his shoulder blades, and what was described that he was of medium height and then he would not be surpassed by tall people except that he surpassed them, and what was narrated that he looked at his face and at the moon and he was more beautiful, and that he had a better fragrance than musk and was softer than silk, and his sweat was taken and used as perfume. His creation was described in such a way that no one is known to be described with similar beauty and handsomeness. And it was narrated in detail that he, peace be upon him, was taller than the medium-height but shorter than the markedly tall, large-headed, with thick hair, fair-skinned with a reddish tint, broad forehead, arched eyebrows, a fine nose bridge such that one who did not examine him would think it was prominent, a slight bow in his eyes, a slight leanness in his nostrils?, thick beard, smooth cheeks, wide mouth, spaced teeth, bright complexion, broad chest, equal belly, large joints, wide between the shoulders, fine fingers, long forearms, broad palms, thick-fingered but soft hands, thick limbs (?), balanced and firm, handsome and dignified, not rough nor contemptible. Hind ibn Abi Hala described him thus, and Umm Ma'bad described him similarly without objection.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage covers the second category of sensory miracles: those in the Prophet's essence (fi dhatihi). First, the author lists miraculous events directly related to his body: the transmission of light through his lineage, the seal of prophethood on his back, his height being perfect, his beauty surpassing the moon, his fragrance better than musk, his softness, and the blessedness of his sweat. Then he provides an elaborate physical description, citing the report of Hind ibn Abi Hala (the son of Khadija from her first marriage) and Umm Ma'bad. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The narrators Hind and Umm Ma'bad treasured every detail of the Prophet's appearance. Do you truly treasure knowing about him? What is one concrete step you will take this week to increase your knowledge of his life and character?
?
When you read about his beautiful features — his fair skin, arched eyebrows, and dignified bearing — does your heart feel closer to him? If not, why? What is blocking that connection, and how can you remove it?
?
The Prophet was 'not rough nor contemptible' (laysa bi l-jāfi wa lā al-mahīn). How often do you treat others with roughness or contempt? Identify one relationship where you can embody his gentle and dignified manner, starting today.

Proof of Prophethood from Physical Perfection and Physiognomy
Description of Prophet's physical traits and physiognomy argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's physical perfection, combined with the science of physiognomy, serves as evidence for his prophethood, and how witnesses and scholars corroborated this.

Core Idea
The Prophet's flawless physique and physiognomy reveal his truthful soul.

This passage presents a unique proof of prophethood: the Prophet's physical attributes themselves are so rare and perfect that they indicate a noble soul, as confirmed by the science of physiognomy (firasa). The author cites eyewitness descriptions and scholarly opinions to show that the Prophet's appearance was a sign of his truthfulness, not merely biographical detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the detailed physical description
Read the Arabic passage describing the Prophet's physical traits carefully. Notice how the description is precise and comprehensive, covering many aspects of his appearance.
This description is attributed to Hind ibn Abi Hala and confirmed by Umm Ma'bad.
2
Understand the physiognomy argument
The author argues that the rare combination of perfect traits in one body indicates the noblest soul. Grasp how the science of physiognomy (firasa) is used as evidence for truthfulness.
Physiognomy was a recognized science in that era.
3
Examine the testimonies
Read the quotes from Shaykh Abu Mansur, Abdullah ibn Rawaha, and Abdullah ibn Salam. See how each supports the argument from appearance or demeanor.
Abdullah ibn Salam recognized the Prophet's truthful face instantly.
4
Note the transition to character
The passage ends by introducing the Prophet's character, which is vast and will be partially covered later. Recognize that the physical proof is just one aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفه على التفصيل أنه عليه السلام كان أطول من المربوع، وأقصر من المشذب، عظيم الهامة، رجل الشعر، أزهر اللون، واسع الجبين، أزج الحواجب، أقنى العرنين، يحسبه من لم يتأمله أشم، في عينيه دبح، وفي سطع، وفي لحيته كثافة، سهل الخدين، ضليع الفم، مفلج الأسنان، ظاهر الوضاءة، عظيم الصدر، سواء البطن، ضخم الكراديس، بعيد ما بين المنكبين، دقيق المسبوبة، طويل الزندين رحب الراحة، شثن الكفين سائل الأطراف بادن متماسك، وسيم قسيم فخم مفخم ليس بالجافي ولا المهين. وصفه بهذا هند ابن أبي هالة إذ هو كان ابن خديجة من أبي هالة بناس بن زرارة التميمي بين يدي المهاجرين والأنصار بهذه الحلية وكان وصافاً فصدق بها. وكذا وصفته أم معهد لزوجها بما يضاهي هذا فلم ينكر عليها.

ثم إن أصحاب علم الفراسة يجمعون معترفون أن اجتماع هذه الصفات في البدن الواحد مما يقل وجوده، ويعز اتفاقه، وهو مع ذلك دال على أن النفس المختصة بمثل هذا التركيب تكون لا محالة أشرف النفوس وأتمها، فتكون دلالة صادقة بشهادة علم الفراسة أنه صادق خير غير شرير ولا كاذب.

والشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله عبر عن هذا المعنى فقال بعدما وصفه عليه السلام بهذه المعاني المختصة ببدنه : وجل الفتن تراها تهيج في الخبرة بذي الآفات في الخلقة، فدلت براءته عن كل الآفات، وزينه بكل زين على استيجابه أعلى الدرجات في الخلق وأفضل الأقدار. ولهذا قال عبد الله بن رواحة له: لو لم تكن فيه آيات مبينة كانت بديهته تنبيك بالخير. وروى عن عبد الله بن سلام أنه قال: لما قدم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المدينة فقال الناس قدم رسول الله، فخرجت إليه فلما نظرت إليه عرفت أن وجهه ليس بوجه كذاب، وكان أول ما سمعته من كلامه أنه قال: أيها الناس أفشوا السلام، وصلوا الأرحام، وأطعموا الطعام، وصلوا بالليل والناس نيام تدخلوا الجنة بسلام.

ثالثًا: ما كان من أخلاقه عليه السلام: وأما ما كان من أخلاقه عليه السلام فكثير جدًا يتعذر إحصاؤه ويفوت الوسع والطرف تعداده فنذكر بعضًا من ذلك.
He described him in detail: he (peace be upon him) was taller than the moderately tall and shorter than the excessively tall, large-headed, with flowing hair, white with a reddish tinge, broad forehead, arched eyebrows, a thin and high-bridged nose, so that one who did not examine him would think it aquiline, with a slight protrusion in his eyes, and with fullness in his beard, smooth cheeks, wide mouth, spaced teeth, apparent brightness, large chest, flat belly, large joints, wide between the shoulders, slender upper arms, long forearms, broad palms, coarse hands and feet, full but compact, handsome, noble, majestic, magnificent, neither coarse nor contemptible. Hind ibn Abi Hala described him with this – for he was the son of Khadija from Abu Hala – before the emigrants and the helpers with this description, and he was a describer, so they attested to it. Likewise, Umm Ma'bad described him to her husband with something similar, and he did not deny it.

Then the experts in physiognomy agree and acknowledge that the combination of these qualities in a single body is rare in existence and difficult to coincide, and yet it indicates that the soul specific to such a composition is necessarily the noblest and most complete of souls. Thus it is a truthful indication, by the testimony of the science of physiognomy, that he is truthful, good, not evil nor a liar.

Sheikh Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) expressed this meaning, saying after describing him (peace be upon him) with these specific physical qualities: "And you see most of the seditions erupt in the one who has defects in creation. So his being free from all defects and adorned with every adornment indicates his deserving the highest degrees in character and the best of statuses." For this reason, Abdullah ibn Rawaha said to him: "If there were no clear signs in you, your intuitive disposition would tell you of goodness." And it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Salam that he said: "When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) arrived in Medina, the people said: 'The Messenger of Allah has arrived.' So I went out to him, and when I looked at him, I knew that his face was not the face of a liar. And the first thing I heard from his speech was that he said: 'O people, spread the greeting of peace, maintain family ties, feed food, and pray at night while people sleep, you will enter Paradise in peace.'"

Third: Regarding his character (peace be upon him): As for his character, it is very much, impossible to enumerate and beyond capacity and scope to count, so we will mention some of that.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood from the Prophet's physical attributes and the science of physiognomy (firasa). The author first provides a detailed description of the Prophet's appearance, citing two witnesses: Hind ibn Abi Hala and Umm Ma'bad. Then he argues that the rare combination of these perfect traits in one body indicates a noble and complete soul, as physiognomy confirms. He quotes Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, who notes that defects in creation lead to sedition, so the Prophet's freedom from defects and complete adornment prove he deserves the highest rank. The author then cites two testimonies: Abdullah ibn Rawaha's statement that even without miracles, the Prophet's demeanor would indicate goodness, and Abdullah ibn Salam's recognition of his truthful face and his first words calling to good deeds. The passage ends with an introduction to the Prophet's character, which is vast and impossible to fully enumerate.

Key Terms

أم معبد
عبد الله بن رواحة
عبد الله بن سلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think this is mere biographical detail without theological significance.
Correction: The passage presents the physical description as evidence for prophethood through the science of physiognomy, not just personal anecdote.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the science of physiognomy (firasa) indicate about the Prophet?
A) He is wealthy and powerful.
B) He is truthful, good, and not evil or a liar.
C) He is tall and handsome.
D) He is a poet and orator.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's physical perfection, rare and complete, is a sign of his truthful soul and prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Abdullah ibn Salam knew by looking at the Prophet that his face was not the face of a liar. When you read this description, does your heart recognize the truth of the Prophet? If not, what barrier in you prevents that recognition?
?
The Prophet's perfect physique pointed to a perfect soul. What imperfect aspects of your own character are you hiding behind a pleasant appearance? How can you align your outer self with the inner truth of your faith?

The Proof from Physiognomy of Prophethood
Nasafi presents a proof of prophethood from the science of physiognomy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the science of physiognomy provides a rational proof for the truthfulness of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and the nobility of his soul.

Core Idea
Physiognomy confirms prophethood: a rare combination of traits reveals a noble soul.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi presents an argument for prophethood that does not rely solely on transmitted miracles. He appeals to the science of physiognomy (علم الفراسة), which reads character from physical appearance. The unanimous agreement of physiognomists that the Prophet's unique physical and moral attributes point to a soul of the highest rank provides a compelling rational proof. This lesson will walk you through the argument and its supporting evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Familiarize yourself with the flow of the argument and the supporting quotes.
This is a continuous argument; note how each part builds on the last.
2
Identify the core claim
What is the main claim of the physiognomists? Look for the statement about the rarity of the combination of attributes and what it indicates about the soul.
3
Examine the supporting testimonies
Three pieces of support: Shaykh Abu Mansur's quote, Abdullah ibn Rawahah's saying, and Abdullah ibn Salam's narration. Understand how each reinforces the argument.
These testimonies anchor the rational proof in lived experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن أصحاب علم الفراسة يجمعون معترفون أن اجتماع هذه الصفات في البدن الواحد مما يقل وجوده، ويعز اتفاقه، وهو مع ذلك دال على أن النفس المختصة بمثل هذا التركيب تكون لا محالة أشرف النفوس وأتمها، فتكون دلالة صادقة بشهادة علم الفراسة أنه صادق خير غير شرير ولا كاذب. والشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله عبر عن هذا المعنى فقال بعدما وصفه عليه السلام بهذه المعاني المختصة ببدنه : وجل الفتن تراها تهيج في الخبرة بذي الآفات في الخلقة، فدلت براءته عن كل الآفات، وزينه بكل زين على استيجابه أعلى الدرجات في الخلق وأفضل الأقدار ، ولهذا قال عبد الله بن رواحة له: لو لم تكن فيه آيات مبينة كانت بديهته تنبيك بالخير. وروى عن عبد الله بن سلام أنه قال : لما قدم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المدينة فقال الناس قدم رسول الله، فخرجت إليه فلما نظرت إليه عرفت أن وجهه ليس بوجه كذاب، وكان أول ما سمعته من كلامه أنه قال: أيها الناس أفشوا السلام، وصلوا الأرحام، وأطعموا الطعام، وصلوا بالليل والناس نيام تدخلوا الجنة بسلام.
Then the practitioners of physiognomy unanimously agree that the combination of these attributes in one body is rare in its existence and uncommon in its concurrence, and nevertheless it indicates that the soul specific to such a composition is without doubt the noblest of souls and the most complete; thus it is a truthful indication by the testimony of physiognomy that he is truthful, good, not evil, nor a liar. And Shaykh Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, expressed this meaning and said after describing him, peace be upon him, with these meanings particular to his body: 'Most tribulations are seen to arise in association with one having defects in constitution, so his innocence from all defects and his adornment with every adornment indicated that he deserved the highest ranks in creation and the best of destinies.' For this reason Abdullah ibn Rawahah said to him: 'If there were no clear signs in him, his natural disposition would inform you of goodness.' And it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Salam that he said: 'When the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, arrived in Medina, the people said: The Messenger of Allah has arrived. So I went out to him, and when I looked at him I knew that his face was not the face of a liar. The first thing I heard from his speech was that he said: O people, spread peace, maintain kinship ties, feed food, and pray at night while people sleep, you will enter Paradise in peace.'
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents a proof of prophethood from the science of physiognomy (علم الفراسة). The author states that practitioners of this science agree that the combination of specific physical traits in one body is extremely rare, and when it occurs, it indicates that the soul in that body is the noblest and most complete. Therefore, the physiognomic evidence truthfully indicates that the Prophet was truthful and good, not evil or a liar. The author then quotes Shaykh Abu Mansur (Imam al-Maturidi), who explains that the Prophet's freedom from all physical defects and his adornment with every good quality proves that he deserves the highest ranks in creation. This is supported by the statement of Abdullah ibn Rawahah, who said that even without explicit miracles, the Prophet's appearance would indicate goodness. Finally, a narration from Abdullah ibn Salam is given: when he first saw the Prophet, he knew from his face that he was not a liar, and the first saying he heard from him was about spreading peace, maintaining kinship, feeding food, and praying at night—a summary of excellent moral teachings.

النفس
التركيب
الشيخ أبو منصور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophethood can only be proven through transmitted miracles.
Correction: Natural signs like physiognomy also serve as valid proofs, as this passage demonstrates.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the science of physiognomy indicate about the Prophet?
A) That he was fortunate.
B) That his soul is the noblest and most complete, and he is truthful and good.
C) That he was a great military leader.
D) That he was wealthy.

Key Takeaway
The science of physiognomy provides a rational proof that the Prophet's unique physical and moral traits indicate a noble soul and truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Look at your own face in the mirror. If someone with the gift of physiognomy saw you, what would they conclude about your character? What traits of truthfulness or deceit might they see? What does that reveal about the state of your soul?
?
The Prophet's face was not the face of a liar. Do you live as though you truly believe every word he said? In what area of your life are you acting as if you doubt his teaching? What will you change today to align your actions with your belief?
?
Abdullah ibn Salam knew from the Prophet's face that he was truthful. If your friends or family looked at your face and demeanor, would they conclude that you are a truthful person? What would they see that contradicts your claim to faith?

The Prophet's Truthfulness and Bravery
Nasafi enumerates the Prophet's truthfulness and bravery with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's complete truthfulness and unmatched bravery, grounded in divine protection, are key evidences of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet never lied or fled; his courage came from Allah's promise, not human strength.

Nasafi begins his account of the Prophet's moral excellences by highlighting two fundamental qualities: truthfulness and bravery. The Prophet was never known to lie, even before his mission, and he never fled from battle despite severe hardships. This lesson examines these qualities and shows how they are linked to his trust in Allah's promise of protection, making them supernatural proofs of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on truthfulness and bravery
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the emphasis on 'never' (قط) to indicate absolute consistency.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
Find the verse 'والله يعصمك من الناس' and understand how it supports the Prophet's fearlessness.
3
Contrast with normal human behavior
Think about how even the bravest people can be forced to retreat; the Prophet never did, showing supernatural support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثًا: ما كان من أخلاقه عليه السلام فأما ما كان من أخلاقه عليه السلام فكثير جدًا يتعذر إحصاؤه ويفوت الوسع والطرف تعداده فنذكر بعضًا من ذلك. فمنه أنه لا يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة ولا منه عن فرار، بل كان في الشجاعة بمحل، ما ولى دبره قط في حرب على ما أصاب أتباعه من النكبات والشدائد، ولذلك أمكنه الركون إلى وعد الله تعالى بقوله: وَاللَّهُ يَعْصِمُكَ مِنَ النَّاسِ فلم يخف أعداءه بعد ذلك، ولم يعرف في أخلاقه سوء. كان على وصفه لا يداري ولا يماري، ولا يعرف فحاشا ولا صخابا، وكان لا ينتصر لنفسه، وكان في الإشفاق بالمحل الذي عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَتٍ وقوله تعالى: فَلَعَلَّكَ بَخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ وفي التحزن عما به هلاك الخلق كما وصفه الله تعالى بقوله: وَلَا تَحْزَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ وقال: عَزِيزُ عَلَيْهِ مَا عَنِتُّمْ وكان في السخاء والكرم بحيث عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسَط وقيل : إنه عليه السلام لم يدخر شيئًا لغد وقد عرض عليه أعلى يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بأن يداهن قليلاً فما أجاب، بل عادى الله تعالى الأقرباء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله تعالى بالرعب في قلوب الخلق. وفي الجملة كان عليه الصلاة والسلام في حلمه ووفائه وزهده وسخائه وأمانته وسداده، وشجاعته، وعفافه، وصادق في صبره، وذكاء فهمه وقلة تلونه، وبارع حفظه، وقوله بجوامع الكلم إذا قال، ومراعاته لشرائط الصمت إذا.
Third: What pertains to his morals, peace be upon him. As for his morals, peace be upon him, they are very many, impossible to enumerate, beyond capacity and scope. So we mention some of that. Among them is that he was never taken for a liar at all, nor was a fault known from him, nor flight from him. Rather, he was in bravery at a station: he never turned his back in battle, despite what befell his followers of calamities and hardships. Therefore he was able to rely on the promise of Allah Almighty in His saying: 'And Allah will protect you from the people' (Quran 5:67), so he did not fear his enemies after that, and evil was not known in his morals. He was, in his description, neither flattering nor disputatious, nor known as obscene or clamorous, and he did not seek revenge for himself. He was in compassion at a station where he was reproached by the saying of Allah: 'Then would you destroy yourself with grief over them?' (Quran 35:8) and His saying: 'Perhaps you would kill yourself with grief' (Quran 18:6), and in grief over what causes the destruction of creation as Allah described him: 'And do not grieve over them' (Quran 16:127), and He said: 'Your suffering is grievous to him' (Quran 9:128). And he was in generosity and liberality to the extent that he was reproached by the saying of Allah: 'And do not stretch it forth to the utmost' (Quran 17:29). And it is said that he, peace be upon him, did not store anything for the next day. The highest desires of worldly goods and leadership were presented to him to compromise a little, but he did not respond. Rather, he opposed for Allah the relatives, kings, and leaders, until Allah honored him with awe in the hearts of people. In summary, he, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was in his forbearance, loyalty, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, bravery, chastity, truthful in his patience, intelligence, stability (lit. little change), excellent memory, speech with comprehensive words when he spoke, and his observance of the conditions of silence when [he was silent].
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the Prophet's moral excellences. The author begins by noting that his morals are too many to fully enumerate and that only a partial listing is possible. The first quality mentioned is his truthfulness: he was never accused of lying, and no fault or flight was known from him. His bravery is highlighted by the fact that he never fled from battle despite severe trials, allowing him to rely on God's promise of protection. The second quality is his forgiveness and lack of retaliation for personal wrongs. Third, his compassion is so intense that God reproached him for excessive grief over people's disbelief. Fourth, his generosity was so extreme that God advised moderation. The author narrates that he did not save for the future and refused worldly offers even when asked to compromise. Finally, a comprehensive list of virtues is given: forbearance, loyalty, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, bravery, chastity, truthfulness, intelligence, stability, excellent memory, speech that is comprehensive, and proper observance of silence. The passage is a testimony to the perfection of his character, supported by Quranic verses that both praise and gently correct him.

Key Terms
صدق
شجاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet's courage was merely human courage like any other brave person.
Correction: The passage shows his bravery was based on divine trust, making it a supernatural quality.

Checkpoint
What is the Quranic verse referenced to support the Prophet's fearlessness?
A) 'And Allah will protect you from the people'
B) 'Your suffering is grievous to him'
C) 'Then would you destroy yourself with grief'
D) 'And do not stretch it forth to the utmost'

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's absolute truthfulness and unconquerable bravery, rooted in divine protection, are clear signs that he was supported by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you been in a situation where telling the truth would have cost you dearly? Did you follow the Prophet's example of absolute truthfulness, or did you compromise? What held you back, and what can you change starting today?
?
The Prophet never fled from battle, even when his companions suffered. In what areas of your life have you been running—spiritually, morally, or in relationships—instead of standing firm? How does knowing that his courage came from Allah's promise inspire you to face your own battles with reliance on Him?
?
The passage says 'evil was not known in his morals.' Compare your own character to this standard: what one moral fault do you most struggle with? Will you repent and strive to rid yourself of it today, knowing that the Prophet's example is attainable through divine help?

The Prophet's Forbearance and Compassion
Nasafi lists the Prophet's forbearance and compassion with Quranic reproaches.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's forbearance, lack of retaliation, and intense compassion, even when reproached by Allah, exemplify his perfect character.

Core Idea
The Prophet never sought revenge and grieved so deeply for others that Allah had to console him.

After establishing his truthfulness and bravery, Nasafi describes the Prophet's manner of dealing with people: he was not flattering, not disputatious, not obscene, not clamorous, and never sought revenge for himself. Then he highlights his extreme compassion and grief over the disbelief of his people, which was so intense that Allah reproached him. This lesson covers these beautiful qualities and the Quranic verses that both praise and gently correct him.

Guided Path
1
Read about his forbearance
Notice the positive qualities: not flattering, not disputing, not obscene, not clamorous, not seeking revenge.
2
Read about his compassion
Focus on the Quranic verses that show how deeply he cared, even to the point of grief.
3
Understand the reproaches
The reproaches from Allah are not criticisms but affirmations of his high station.

ثالثًا: ما كان من أخلاقه عليه السلام فأما ما كان من أخلاقه عليه السلام فكثير جدًا يتعذر إحصاؤه ويفوت الوسع والطرف تعداده فنذكر بعضًا من ذلك. فمنه أنه لا يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة ولا منه عن فرار، بل كان في الشجاعة بمحل، ما ولى دبره قط في حرب على ما أصاب أتباعه من النكبات والشدائد، ولذلك أمكنه الركون إلى وعد الله تعالى بقوله: وَاللَّهُ يَعْصِمُكَ مِنَ النَّاسِ فلم يخف أعداءه بعد ذلك، ولم يعرف في أخلاقه سوء. كان على وصفه لا يداري ولا يماري، ولا يعرف فحاشا ولا صخابا، وكان لا ينتصر لنفسه، وكان في الإشفاق بالمحل الذي عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَتٍ وقوله تعالى: فَلَعَلَّكَ بَخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ وفي التحزن عما به هلاك الخلق كما وصفه الله تعالى بقوله: وَلَا تَحْزَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ وقال: عَزِيزُ عَلَيْهِ مَا عَنِتُّمْ وكان في السخاء والكرم بحيث عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسَط وقيل : إنه عليه السلام لم يدخر شيئًا لغد وقد عرض عليه أعلى يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بأن يداهن قليلاً فما أجاب، بل عادى الله تعالى الأقرباء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله تعالى بالرعب في قلوب الخلق. وفي الجملة كان عليه الصلاة والسلام في حلمه ووفائه وزهده وسخائه وأمانته وسداده، وشجاعته، وعفافه، وصادق في صبره، وذكاء فهمه وقلة تلونه، وبارع حفظه، وقوله بجوامع الكلم إذا قال، ومراعاته لشرائط الصمت إذا.
Third: What pertains to his morals, peace be upon him. As for his morals, peace be upon him, they are very many, impossible to enumerate, beyond capacity and scope. So we mention some of that. Among them is that he was never taken for a liar at all, nor was a fault known from him, nor flight from him. Rather, he was in bravery at a station: he never turned his back in battle, despite what befell his followers of calamities and hardships. Therefore he was able to rely on the promise of Allah Almighty in His saying: 'And Allah will protect you from the people' (Quran 5:67), so he did not fear his enemies after that, and evil was not known in his morals. He was, in his description, neither flattering nor disputatious, nor known as obscene or clamorous, and he did not seek revenge for himself. He was in compassion at a station where he was reproached by the saying of Allah: 'Then would you destroy yourself with grief over them?' (Quran 35:8) and His saying: 'Perhaps you would kill yourself with grief' (Quran 18:6), and in grief over what causes the destruction of creation as Allah described him: 'And do not grieve over them' (Quran 16:127), and He said: 'Your suffering is grievous to him' (Quran 9:128). And he was in generosity and liberality to the extent that he was reproached by the saying of Allah: 'And do not stretch it forth to the utmost' (Quran 17:29). And it is said that he, peace be upon him, did not store anything for the next day. The highest desires of worldly goods and leadership were presented to him to compromise a little, but he did not respond. Rather, he opposed for Allah the relatives, kings, and leaders, until Allah honored him with awe in the hearts of people. In summary, he, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was in his forbearance, loyalty, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, bravery, chastity, truthful in his patience, intelligence, stability (lit. little change), excellent memory, speech with comprehensive words when he spoke, and his observance of the conditions of silence when [he was silent].
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the Prophet's moral excellences. The author begins by noting that his morals are too many to fully enumerate and that only a partial listing is possible. The first quality mentioned is his truthfulness: he was never accused of lying, and no fault or flight was known from him. His bravery is highlighted by the fact that he never fled from battle despite severe trials, allowing him to rely on God's promise of protection. The second quality is his forgiveness and lack of retaliation for personal wrongs. Third, his compassion is so intense that God reproached him for excessive grief over people's disbelief. Fourth, his generosity was so extreme that God advised moderation. The author narrates that he did not save for the future and refused worldly offers even when asked to compromise. Finally, a comprehensive list of virtues is given: forbearance, loyalty, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, bravery, chastity, truthfulness, intelligence, stability, excellent memory, speech that is comprehensive, and proper observance of silence. The passage is a testimony to the perfection of his character, supported by Quranic verses that both praise and gently correct him.

Key Terms
حلم
إشفاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the reproaches mean the Prophet was wrong.
Correction: The reproaches are signs of his high rank; Allah gently corrected him to moderate his compassion, not to condemn it.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as part of the Prophet's forbearance?
A) Not flattering
B) Not disputing
C) Not being generous
D) Not seeking revenge

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's forbearance and compassion show his complete selflessness and concern for others, to the extent that Allah consoled him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone wrongs you, do you naturally seek revenge or do you follow the Prophet's example of not seeking revenge for himself? What holds you back from that? Commit to one specific situation this week where you will forgive instead of retaliate.
?
The Prophet grieved so deeply for disbelievers that Allah had to console him. When was the last time you felt genuine grief for someone who rejects the truth? Are you more concerned about your own comfort or the salvation of others? Identify one person you know who is far from faith and make a specific dua for them today.
?
The Prophet was not known as obscene or clamorous. In your conversations, especially online, do you avoid harsh words and loud arguments? What one change will you make to your speech to reflect his forbearance?

The Prophet's Generosity and Comprehensive Virtues
Nasafi describes the Prophet's generosity and lists his comprehensive virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's extreme generosity, combined with a comprehensive list of virtues, forms a complete model of moral perfection.

Core Idea
The Prophet's generosity was so great that Allah advised moderation, and his virtues encompass all aspects of character.

Nasafi continues with the Prophet's generosity, noting that he was so generous that he did not store for the next day, and was offered worldly wealth to compromise but refused. The passage concludes with a comprehensive summary of his virtues, including forbearance, loyalty, asceticism, trustworthiness, and many others. This lesson highlights how these qualities together show that the Prophet was the perfect moral exemplar.

Guided Path
1
Read about his generosity
Notice the extent: he did not save anything for the future, and he refused worldly offers.
2
Read the Quranic reproach
Allah said 'Do not stretch forth your hand to the utmost' to moderate his giving.
3
Study the summary list
Go through each virtue in the summary and reflect on how they complement each other.

?

?

The Prophet's Courage and Truthfulness
Nasafi lists the Prophet's truthfulness and courage as signs of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unwavering courage and truthfulness point to divine support.

Core Idea
Flawless courage and honesty are signs of prophethood.

Nasafi begins his proof by highlighting two critical virtues of the Prophet: he never lied and never fled from battle. These qualities, despite immense hardships, reveal a character beyond ordinary human capacity. Let's examine these specific traits and the Quranic support for them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Nasafi uses definitive statements: 'never taken lying', 'never turned his back'.
These are absolute claims meant to establish complete reliability.
2
Identify the virtues mentioned
List the virtues explicitly stated: truthfulness (no lie), no slip, no flight, courage, and then the negative qualities absent (no dissimulation, no foul speech).
3
Connect to divine support
Note that the Prophet's reliance on Allah's promise of protection (Quran 5:67) made him fearless. This shows his courage stems from faith, not natural disposition alone.
Nasafi uses this to argue the virtues are divinely sustained.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمنه أنه لا لو لم يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة ولا منه عن فرار، بل كان في الشجاعة بمحل، ما ولى دبره قط في حرب على ما أصاب أتباعه من النكبات والشدائد، ولذلك أمكنه الركون إلى وعد الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿ وَاللَّهُ يَعْصِمُكَ مِنَ النَّاسِ ﴾ فلم يخف أعداءه بعد ذلك، ولم يعرف في أخلاقه سوء. كان على وصفه لا يداري ولا يماري، ولا يعرف فحاشا ولا صخابا، وكان لا ينتصر لنفسه، وكان في الإشفاق بالمحل الذي عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَاتٍ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَعَلَّكَ بَاخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ ﴾ وفي التحزن عما به هلاك الخلق كما وصفه الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿ وَلَا تَحْزَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ ﴾ وقال: ﴿ عَزِيزٌ عَلَيْهِ مَا عَنِتُّمْ ﴾ وكان في السخاء والكرم بحيث عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسْطِ ﴾ وقيل: إنه عليه السلام لم يدخر شيئًا لغد وقد عرض عليه أعلى يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بأن يداهن قليلاً فما أجاب، بل عادى الله تعالى ما الأقرباء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله تعالى بالرعب في قلوب الخلق. وفي الجملة كان عليه الصلاة والسلام في حلمه ووفائه وزهده وسخائه وأمانته وسداده، وشجاعته، وعفافه، وصادق في صبره، وذكاء فهمه وقلة تلونه، وبارع حفظه، وقوله بجوامع الكلم إذا قال، ومراعاته لشرائط الصمت إذا صمت، وتصديقه المواعيد إذا وعد وطهارة أخلاقه كلها صبيًّا وناشئًا وكهلاً، بحيث تتبع آثاره أعداؤه الذين تأمروا على معاداته، وتجانبوا عن مسالمته ومداراته، بل ناصبوه الحرب، وداوموا على قصد إطفاء نوره وطمس آثاره وإبادة أتباعه وأشياعه بالطمس والضرب. كانت هذه الأخلاق الفاضلة والشمائل الشريفة موجودة فيه على طول الأيام وتصاريف الأحوال لم تتغير عن شيء منها في حالة، ولا وجد منه ضد من أضدادها طول عمره البتة، فكان ذلك دليلاً أن شيئًا منها لم يكن عن تكلف، إذ المتكلف لما ليس في طباعه لا يستمر على ما يتكلفه بل لابد أن يرجع في كثير من الأحايين إلى ما جبل عليه من الخلق ولهذا قيل: إن التخلق يأتي دونه الخلق. وقال بعض الشعراء: ن يتخلق بغير خلق يرجع بصفر إلى الطبيعة. وما أحسن ما قال المتنبي: وأسرع مفعول صنعت تغيرا تكلف شيء في طباعك ضده. فكان جريه على السلام على طريقة واحدة في تساوي الأخلاق على امتداد الأزمنة والدهور، واختلاف الأحوال والأمور دليلاً أنها مواهب من مواهب الله تعالى؛ ليكون اجتماعها كلها وانتفاء أضدادها التي هي رذائل بأسرها عنه دلالة صادقة، أنه المؤيد بقوة سماوية، والمكرم بمعونة إلهية، ليشتغل بالقيام بما فرض إليه، وتحمل أعباء ما حمل عليه من أمور الرسالة إلى أصناف الخليقة والأمة والرياسة على جميع طبقات البرية.
From it: that he was never taken lying, nor was any slip known from him, nor did he flee; rather, he was in courage at a level: he never turned his back in battle despite what befell his followers of calamities and hardships. Therefore, he was able to rely on the promise of Allah Almighty, saying: 'And Allah will protect you from the people' (5:67), so he did not fear his enemies after that, and no evil was known in his character. He was of such description: he did not dissimulate nor dispute, and was not known to be foul-mouthed or clamorous. He did not seek revenge for himself. He was in compassion at the level for which he was reproached by Allah's saying: 'So do not let your soul go out in regret over them' (35:8) and His saying: 'Perhaps you would kill yourself with grief' (18:6), and in grief over what would destroy creation as Allah described him: 'And do not grieve over them' (16:127) and said: 'Grievous to him is your suffering' (9:128). He was in generosity and liberality to the extent that he was reproached by Allah's saying: 'And do not stretch it forth all the stretching' (17:29). And it is said that he, peace be upon him, did not store anything for tomorrow, though he was offered higher things desirable from the goods of this world and leadership if he would compromise a little, but he did not accept. Rather, he enmified for Allah's sake even relatives, kings, and chiefs, until Allah honored him with terror in the hearts of creation. In summary, he, peace and blessings be upon him, was in his forbearance, faithfulness, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, courage, chastity, truthful in his patience, sharpness of understanding, lack of inconsistency, excellent memory, his speech with comprehensive words when he spoke, his observance of the conditions of silence when he was silent, his fulfillment of promises when he promised, and the purity of his entire character as a child, youth, and adult, such that his enemies pursued his traces, those who conspired to oppose him and avoided making peace with him or placating him, but rather waged war against him and persisted in aiming to extinguish his light, obliterate his traces, and destroy his followers and partisans by obliteration and striking. These noble qualities and honorable traits existed in him over the length of days and changes of states, not changing from any of them in any state, nor was any opposite of their opposites found from him throughout his entire life at all. That was evidence that none of them was by affectation, for one who affects what is not in his nature does not continue in what he affects, but inevitably returns in many moments to what he was created upon of character. Hence it is said: 'Pretending to have a trait falls short of the trait itself.' Some poet said: 'Whoever pretends to have a trait not his own returns empty-handed to nature.' How excellent is what al-Mutanabbi said: 'The quickest thing to change is a manufactured act; to affect something while it is your opposite is against nature.' Thus, his proceeding upon one way in equality of character over the extension of times and ages and the variation of states and matters was evidence that they were gifts from Allah Almighty, so that their complete gathering together and the absence of their opposites, which are all vices from him, would be a truthful indication that he is supported by a heavenly power and honored with divine assistance, to occupy himself with performing what was imposed upon him and bearing the burdens of what he was charged with from the affairs of the message to all kinds of creation, the community, and leadership over all levels of humankind.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood based on the Prophet Muhammad's perfect character. Nasafi begins by listing specific virtues: never lying, never fleeing in battle despite hardships, relying on God's promise of protection, courage, absence of evil traits, straightforwardness without deceit, no foul language or clamor, not seeking revenge, extreme compassion as reflected in Quranic verses that rebuke him for excessive grief, generosity to the point of being warned not to be wasteful, and rejection of worldly offers even from relatives. He then summarizes the Prophet's virtues: forbearance, faithfulness, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, courage, chastity, patience, intelligence, consistency, memory, eloquence, proper silence, keeping promises, and pure character from childhood to adulthood. Notably, his enemies themselves acknowledged these virtues despite their hostility. Nasafi then argues that these virtues persisted unchanged throughout his entire life, never deviating nor showing their opposites. This consistency is evidence that they were not affectation (takalluf), because someone who affects a trait not natural to him cannot maintain it; he will revert to his innate character. He quotes a poet and al-Mutanabbi to support this: affectation is unstable. Therefore, the uniformity of his virtues over time proves they are divine gifts (mawahib), not acquired. The combination of all virtues and absence of all vices indicates he is supported by heavenly power and divine assistance for his mission of prophethood and leadership over all creation.

Key Terms
الكذب
الفرار
الشجاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi claim the Prophet never did in battle?
A) He never gave orders.
B) He never turned his back.
C) He never killed anyone.
D) He never used weapons.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's absolute truthfulness and courage, sustained by divine trust, are early indicators of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you told a small lie to avoid embarrassment? How does knowing that the Prophet was 'never taken lying'—not even once—make you feel about that excuse? What will you do differently starting today?
?
The Prophet never fled from battle despite calamities that shook his followers. Think of a situation where you ran away from a difficult duty (e.g., helping a family member, standing up for truth) because you were afraid of the outcome. What promise of Allah could you have relied on instead?
?
The passage says 'no evil was known in his character.' Is there a single character flaw you have been tolerating in yourself—like a sharp tongue, holding grudges, or avoiding responsibility—that would never be found in the Prophet? Are you willing to confront it today and seek Allah's help to remove it?

Compassion, Generosity, and Rejecting the World
Nasafi details the Prophet's remarkable compassion and generosity as evidence of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's extreme compassion and generosity, even when reproached, indicate divine assistance.

Core Idea
Prophetic compassion and generosity surpass human limits.

Nasafi continues his listing by focusing on qualities that were so intense that Allah gently reproached the Prophet: his compassion for others caused him grief, and his generosity bordered on waste. These traits, combined with his rejection of worldly offers, demonstrate a character not driven by personal gain but by divine mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the Quranic verses mentioned. Each verse comments on the Prophet's excessive grief or generosity.
2
Identify the two main qualities
Look for compassion (ishfaq) and generosity (sakha' wa karam). Note how they are described as so extreme that Allah 'reproached' him.
The reproach is loving, not harsh.
3
Understand the rejection of worldly offers
The Prophet refused offers of wealth and leadership if he would compromise even slightly. This shows his sincerity and independence from worldly motives.
This strengthens the proof that his character is not for personal benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمنه أنه لا لو لم يؤخذ عليه كذب قط، ولا عرفت منه هفوة ولا منه عن فرار، بل كان في الشجاعة بمحل، ما ولى دبره قط في حرب على ما أصاب أتباعه من النكبات والشدائد، ولذلك أمكنه الركون إلى وعد الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿ وَاللَّهُ يَعْصِمُكَ مِنَ النَّاسِ ﴾ فلم يخف أعداءه بعد ذلك، ولم يعرف في أخلاقه سوء. كان على وصفه لا يداري ولا يماري، ولا يعرف فحاشا ولا صخابا، وكان لا ينتصر لنفسه، وكان في الإشفاق بالمحل الذي عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَا تَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَاتٍ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَعَلَّكَ بَاخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ ﴾ وفي التحزن عما به هلاك الخلق كما وصفه الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿ وَلَا تَحْزَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ ﴾ وقال: ﴿ عَزِيزٌ عَلَيْهِ مَا عَنِتُّمْ ﴾ وكان في السخاء والكرم بحيث عوتب عليه بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسْطِ ﴾ وقيل: إنه عليه السلام لم يدخر شيئًا لغد وقد عرض عليه أعلى يرغب فيه من متاع الدنيا والرياسة بأن يداهن قليلاً فما أجاب، بل عادى الله تعالى ما الأقرباء والملوك والسادات حتى أكرمه الله تعالى بالرعب في قلوب الخلق. وفي الجملة كان عليه الصلاة والسلام في حلمه ووفائه وزهده وسخائه وأمانته وسداده، وشجاعته، وعفافه، وصادق في صبره، وذكاء فهمه وقلة تلونه، وبارع حفظه، وقوله بجوامع الكلم إذا قال، ومراعاته لشرائط الصمت إذا صمت، وتصديقه المواعيد إذا وعد وطهارة أخلاقه كلها صبيًّا وناشئًا وكهلاً، بحيث تتبع آثاره أعداؤه الذين تأمروا على معاداته، وتجانبوا عن مسالمته ومداراته، بل ناصبوه الحرب، وداوموا على قصد إطفاء نوره وطمس آثاره وإبادة أتباعه وأشياعه بالطمس والضرب. كانت هذه الأخلاق الفاضلة والشمائل الشريفة موجودة فيه على طول الأيام وتصاريف الأحوال لم تتغير عن شيء منها في حالة، ولا وجد منه ضد من أضدادها طول عمره البتة، فكان ذلك دليلاً أن شيئًا منها لم يكن عن تكلف، إذ المتكلف لما ليس في طباعه لا يستمر على ما يتكلفه بل لابد أن يرجع في كثير من الأحايين إلى ما جبل عليه من الخلق ولهذا قيل: إن التخلق يأتي دونه الخلق. وقال بعض الشعراء: ن يتخلق بغير خلق يرجع بصفر إلى الطبيعة. وما أحسن ما قال المتنبي: وأسرع مفعول صنعت تغيرا تكلف شيء في طباعك ضده. فكان جريه على السلام على طريقة واحدة في تساوي الأخلاق على امتداد الأزمنة والدهور، واختلاف الأحوال والأمور دليلاً أنها مواهب من مواهب الله تعالى؛ ليكون اجتماعها كلها وانتفاء أضدادها التي هي رذائل بأسرها عنه دلالة صادقة، أنه المؤيد بقوة سماوية، والمكرم بمعونة إلهية، ليشتغل بالقيام بما فرض إليه، وتحمل أعباء ما حمل عليه من أمور الرسالة إلى أصناف الخليقة والأمة والرياسة على جميع طبقات البرية.
From it: that he was never taken lying, nor was any slip known from him, nor did he flee; rather, he was in courage at a level: he never turned his back in battle despite what befell his followers of calamities and hardships. Therefore, he was able to rely on the promise of Allah Almighty, saying: 'And Allah will protect you from the people' (5:67), so he did not fear his enemies after that, and no evil was known in his character. He was of such description: he did not dissimulate nor dispute, and was not known to be foul-mouthed or clamorous. He did not seek revenge for himself. He was in compassion at the level for which he was reproached by Allah's saying: 'So do not let your soul go out in regret over them' (35:8) and His saying: 'Perhaps you would kill yourself with grief' (18:6), and in grief over what would destroy creation as Allah described him: 'And do not grieve over them' (16:127) and said: 'Grievous to him is your suffering' (9:128). He was in generosity and liberality to the extent that he was reproached by Allah's saying: 'And do not stretch it forth all the stretching' (17:29). And it is said that he, peace be upon him, did not store anything for tomorrow, though he was offered higher things desirable from the goods of this world and leadership if he would compromise a little, but he did not accept. Rather, he enmified for Allah's sake even relatives, kings, and chiefs, until Allah honored him with terror in the hearts of creation. In summary, he, peace and blessings be upon him, was in his forbearance, faithfulness, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, courage, chastity, truthful in his patience, sharpness of understanding, lack of inconsistency, excellent memory, his speech with comprehensive words when he spoke, his observance of the conditions of silence when he was silent, his fulfillment of promises when he promised, and the purity of his entire character as a child, youth, and adult, such that his enemies pursued his traces, those who conspired to oppose him and avoided making peace with him or placating him, but rather waged war against him and persisted in aiming to extinguish his light, obliterate his traces, and destroy his followers and partisans by obliteration and striking. These noble qualities and honorable traits existed in him over the length of days and changes of states, not changing from any of them in any state, nor was any opposite of their opposites found from him throughout his entire life at all. That was evidence that none of them was by affectation, for one who affects what is not in his nature does not continue in what he affects, but inevitably returns in many moments to what he was created upon of character. Hence it is said: 'Pretending to have a trait falls short of the trait itself.' Some poet said: 'Whoever pretends to have a trait not his own returns empty-handed to nature.' How excellent is what al-Mutanabbi said: 'The quickest thing to change is a manufactured act; to affect something while it is your opposite is against nature.' Thus, his proceeding upon one way in equality of character over the extension of times and ages and the variation of states and matters was evidence that they were gifts from Allah Almighty, so that their complete gathering together and the absence of their opposites, which are all vices from him, would be a truthful indication that he is supported by a heavenly power and honored with divine assistance, to occupy himself with performing what was imposed upon him and bearing the burdens of what he was charged with from the affairs of the message to all kinds of creation, the community, and leadership over all levels of humankind.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood based on the Prophet Muhammad's perfect character. Nasafi begins by listing specific virtues: never lying, never fleeing in battle despite hardships, relying on God's promise of protection, courage, absence of evil traits, straightforwardness without deceit, no foul language or clamor, not seeking revenge, extreme compassion as reflected in Quranic verses that rebuke him for excessive grief, generosity to the point of being warned not to be wasteful, and rejection of worldly offers even from relatives. He then summarizes the Prophet's virtues: forbearance, faithfulness, asceticism, generosity, trustworthiness, rectitude, courage, chastity, patience, intelligence, consistency, memory, eloquence, proper silence, keeping promises, and pure character from childhood to adulthood. Notably, his enemies themselves acknowledged these virtues despite their hostility. Nasafi then argues that these virtues persisted unchanged throughout his entire life, never deviating nor showing their opposites. This consistency is evidence that they were not affectation (takalluf), because someone who affects a trait not natural to him cannot maintain it; he will revert to his innate character. He quotes a poet and al-Mutanabbi to support this: affectation is unstable. Therefore, the uniformity of his virtues over time proves they are divine gifts (mawahib), not acquired. The combination of all virtues and absence of all vices indicates he is supported by heavenly power and divine assistance for his mission of prophethood and leadership over all creation.

Key Terms
الإشفاق
السخاء
الكرم
العتاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did the Prophet refuse to do even when offered worldly goods and leadership?
A) To pray for his enemies.
B) To compromise (mudāhana) even a little.
C) To accept gifts from non-Muslims.
D) To store food for his family.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's extreme compassion and generosity, even when reproached, and his rejection of worldly compromise show his character is divinely guided.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see people rejecting the truth, does your heart ache for them as the Prophet's did? Or have you become indifferent? Ask yourself: when was the last time you sincerely prayed for someone's guidance out of compassion, not obligation?
?
Examine your spending: are you holding back because you fear poverty, or do you truly trust Allah's provision? The Prophet stored nothing for tomorrow. What is one thing you can give away today that you normally would keep 'just in case'?
?
Think of a relative, colleague, or leader you avoid opposing because it might cost you status or comfort. Are you willing to enmify for Allah's sake, as the Prophet did? What step of uncompromising truth are you avoiding right now?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
Consistency of Virtues Proves Divine Gift
Nasafi argues the Prophet's unchanging virtues are divine gifts, not human affectation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the lifelong consistency of the Prophet's virtues proves they are divine gifts, not affectation.

Core Idea
Unaffected virtues that never change are from Allah.

Nasafi now builds the central argument: the Prophet's virtues were present from childhood to old age, never changing. This constancy cannot be explained by affectation (takalluf), because human nature always reverts. Therefore, these virtues are divine gifts (mawahib), proving he is supported by Allah for prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the comprehensive list of virtues and the statement that they never changed over entire life.
The phrase 'لم تتغير عن شيء منها' is key.
2
Understand the argument against affectation
Identify the logical move: consistency over time implies no affectation, because affectation cannot be sustained. Nasafi quotes a poet and al-Mutanabbi.
3
Grasp the conclusion
The uniformity and completeness of virtues (all present, none absent) indicate they are divine gifts, proving he is aided by heavenly power for his prophetic mission.
This is the final proof of prophethood from character.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's virtuous character was merely a result of his excellent upbringing and personal effort.
Correction: Nasafi argues that lifelong consistency without change or lapse proves these virtues are divinely bestowed, not humanly acquired.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence that the Prophet's virtues were not affectation?
A) They were praised by everyone.
B) They never changed over his entire life.
C) They were taught by the Quran.
D) They were unlike his ancestors.

The lifelong invariability of the Prophet's complete virtues proves they are divine gifts, confirming his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of one virtue you attempt to maintain in your daily life. How often do you find yourself acting contrary to it? The Prophet's virtues never changed because they were divine gifts. Where are you relying on your own affectation instead of seeking Allah's gift of consistency? What will you ask Allah for tonight in your du'a to transform this area of your character?
?
Nasafi uses the proverb 'Pretending to have a trait falls short of the trait itself.' In what specific relationship or responsibility are you merely pretending to be patient, generous, or truthful? Why do you keep pretending rather than turning to Allah for real change? What would happen if you honestly admitted your weakness to Allah and asked Him to give you the virtue as a gift?
?
The proof of prophethood here is that the Prophet's complete, unwavering character can only come from Allah. How does your own inconsistency—your repeated failures in character despite good intentions—serve as a reminder that true virtue must come from Him? Will you stop trusting your own efforts and instead beg Allah to grant you a share of the prophetic character? Write down one concrete step you will take tonight to seek His help.
