Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
The Prophet's Consistent Character as Divine Gift
Nasafi argues that the Prophet's unwavering virtues prove they were divinely gifted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the unwavering consistency of the Prophet's character serves as a proof of prophethood, demonstrating that his virtues were divine gifts rather than affectation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's lifelong consistency proves his virtues were divinely gifted, not affected.

Nasafi presents a unique argument for prophethood based on the absolute constancy of the Prophet's character. Even his enemies, who fought against him, could not deny that his virtues never changed or showed their opposites. This lesson explores how this consistency rules out affectation and points to divine support.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Pay attention to the list of virtues and the overall flow of the argument.
Notice the vivid description of the enemies' hostility.
2
Identify the core claim about constancy
Find the sentence that states the virtues never changed and no opposite ever appeared. This is the key evidence.
3
Understand the refutation of affectation
Read the section on takalluf (affectation) and the poetic quotes. See how the author contrasts affected behavior with natural character.
The quotes from the poet and al-Mutanabbi reinforce the point.
4
Trace the conclusion about divine gifts
Note how the argument concludes that the Prophet's unwavering conduct is a sign that his virtues are divine gifts, enabling his mission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صمت، وتصديقه المواعيد إذا وعد وطهارة أخلاقه كلها صبيًّا وناشئًا وكهلاً، بحيث تتبع آثاره أعداؤه الذين تأمروا على معاداته، وتجانبوا عن مسالمته ومداراته، بل ناصبوه الحرب، وداوموا على قصد إطفاء نوره وطمس آثاره وإبادة أتباعه وأشياعه بالطمس والضرب. كانت هذه الأخلاق الفاضلة والشمائل الشريفة موجودة فيه على طول الأيام وتصاريف الأحوال لم تتغير عن شيء منها في حالة، ولا وجد منه ضد من أضدادها طول عمره البتة، فكان ذلك دليلاً أن شيئًا منها لم يكن عن تكلف، إذ المتكلف لما ليس في طباعه لا يستمر على ما يتكلفه بل لابد أن يرجع في كثير من الأحايين إلى ما جبل عليه من الخلق ولهذا قيل: إن التخلق يأتي دونه الخلق. وقال بعض الشعراء: من يتخلق بغير خلق يرجع بصفر إلى الطبيعة. وما أحسن ما قال المتنبي: وأسرع مفعول صنعت تغيرا تكلف شيء في طباعك ضده. فكان جريه على السواء على طريقة واحدة في تساوي الأخلاق على امتداد الأزمنة والدهور، واختلاف الأحوال والأمور دليلاً أنها مواهب من مواهب الله تعالى؛ ليكون اجتماعها كلها وانتفاء أضدادها التي هي رذائل بأسرها عنه دلالة صادقة، أنه المؤيد بقوة سماوية، والمكرم بمعونة إلهية، ليشتغل بالقيام بما فرض إليه، وتحمل أعباء ما حمل عليه من أمور الرسالة إلى أصناف الخليقة والأمة والرياسة على جميع طبقات البرية.
His silence, and his fulfillment of promises when he promised, and the purity of all his manners as a child, a youth, and an adult, such that his enemies – those who conspired against him in hostility, shunned peace and diplomacy with him, but rather waged war against him and persisted in trying to extinguish his light, obliterate his traces, and destroy his followers and partisans by erasure and striking – followed his traces. These noble manners and excellent traits existed in him over the length of days and the vicissitudes of circumstances, not changing from any of them in any state, nor was any opposite of these opposites ever found from him throughout his entire life. That was proof that none of them was from affectation, because the one who affects what is not in his nature does not persist in his affectation; he must in many cases revert to the disposition he was created with. For this reason it was said: 'Affectation comes short of natural character.' And one of the poets said: 'He who affects a character not his own returns empty to his natural disposition.' And how excellent is what al-Mutanabbi said: 'The quickest thing to change is an affectation of something opposite to your nature.' His conduct, then, being upon the same pattern in the equality of his virtues over the extension of times and ages and the variation of states and affairs, was proof that they are gifts from among the gifts of Allah the Exalted, so that their complete gathering together and the absence of their opposites, which are vices entirely from him, might be a true indication that he is supported by a heavenly power and honored with divine assistance, to occupy himself with discharging what was imposed upon him and bearing the burdens of what he was charged with of the affairs of the message to the classes of creation and the community, and leadership over all levels of humanity.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood based on the consistency of the Prophet's (s) character. It begins by listing some of his noble traits: silence (perhaps meaning restraint in speech), fulfillment of promises, and purity of character from childhood to adulthood. It notes that even his enemies, who actively opposed and fought him, could not deny these traits. Then it argues that these virtues remained constant throughout his life without any change, and he never exhibited their opposites. This constancy proves they were not affected (takalluf), because a person who forces himself to act against his nature cannot maintain it and will eventually revert to his innate character. The author quotes a poet and al-Mutanabbi to illustrate that affectation is unstable. Therefore, the Prophet's unvarying conduct over time indicates that these virtues were divine gifts (mawahib). The purpose of gathering all these virtues and excluding every vice in him is to provide a truthful sign that he is supported by Allah, so that he may carry out his mission and leadership.

Key Terms
تكلف (affectation)
تخلق (affectation of character)
خلق (natural character)
مواهب (divine gifts)
نقض العادة (breach of custom)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that good character alone proves prophethood, but the key is the consistency and absence of opposites over a lifetime, not just any good character.
Correction: The passage argues that the Prophet's virtues never changed and no opposite ever appeared, which distinguishes them from ordinary good character that may fluctuate.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what proves that the Prophet's (s) noble character was not due to affectation (takalluf)?
A) His enemies praised him.
B) The virtues remained constant throughout his entire life without change.
C) He was known for his silence.
D) He never made any mistakes.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unwavering character over his entire life, without any opposite ever appearing, proves his virtues were divine gifts, not human affectation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of one area in your life where you try to maintain a good character trait that doesn't come naturally to you. How long can you keep it up before your true nature shows? What does that struggle reveal about the Prophet's lifelong consistency—and what does it demand of you in admitting that such virtue must be a gift, not your own achievement?
?
The Prophet's enemies still followed his traces. Who in your life—someone who disagrees with you or even opposes you—can see consistency in your behavior? Or do you find yourself changing your character depending on the audience? If your character shifted with circumstances, what does that imply about your reliance on Allah versus your own image management?
?
If you had to live the rest of your life without ever showing a single vice opposite to the virtues you claim, could you? What would that impossibility force you to confess about your own need for divine assistance—and about the Prophet, who did precisely that? Will you, after today, stop attributing your occasional good behavior to your own strength and start thanking Allah for any consistency you have?

The Gathering of Miraculous Traits as a Breach of Custom
Nasafi argues that the Prophet's unique combination of qualities is a breach of custom, refuting the possibility of a false prophet possessing them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unique combination of perfect qualities serves as a miracle (breach of custom) that distinguishes true prophethood from false claims.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unmatched virtues are a divine proof no false prophet can replicate.

In this passage, Nasafi builds on the earlier discussion of the Prophet not seeking reward. He argues that the extraordinary combination of perfect qualities in the Prophet's character and body is itself a breach of custom, and thus a miracle. He then refutes the potential objection that God might grant such qualities to a false prophet, showing that would lead to the absurdity of false prophets performing real miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Let the argument's flow become familiar before you interpret.
Notice the reference to Quran 26:180 and the logical progression.
2
Identify the key claims
Find where Nasafi states that the gathering of qualities is a breach of custom, and then the hypothetical objection about a false prophet. Understand how he refutes it.
The refutation relies on the impossibility of miracles for false prophets.
3
Analyze the logical structure
Break down the argument into premise, objection, and refutation. See how the impossibility of false prophets performing miracles is used to prove that they cannot possess such perfect qualities.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this argument strengthens the proof of prophethood by showing that the Prophet's very character is a miracle.
Connect this to the broader concept of miracles as signs of truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: وإلى هذا المعنى يرجع قوله تعالى فيما أمر نبيه عليه السلام بمخاطبة قومه به على سبيل الاحتجاج لنفسه: ﴿ وَمَا أَسْأَلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَجْرٍ ﴾ الآية - وهذا تأويل حسن، والله أعلم. ثم اجتماع هذه المعاني التي اجتمعت في بدنه وأخلاقه خارج عن العادة المستمرة وإن كان وجود أفرادها على ما عليه العادة جائز من أفراد الأشخاص وأعيان الخلق، فكان ذلك من باب نقض العادة، ولن يظن أن الله تعالى مع كمال يجمع هذا كله فيمن يعلم أنه يتقول عليه ويدعي أنه أرسله إلى عباده إفكا منه وتحرصا، ولو كان هذا جائزاً لكان إظهار المعجزة الناقضة للعادة على يدي المتنبئ الكاذب في دعواه أجوز، وقد مر امتناع ذلك، فكذا هذا.
They said: And to this meaning refers the saying of Allah the Exalted, in what He commanded His Prophet, peace be upon him, to address his people with by way of argument for himself: 'And I do not ask you for any reward for it' – the verse. And this is a good interpretation, and Allah knows best. Then the gathering of these qualities that were gathered in his body and his character is outside the continuous custom, even if the existence of their individuals according to custom is possible from individual persons and individuals of creation. So that was of the category of breach of custom (naqd al-ʿāda). And it is not to be thought that Allah the Exalted, despite His perfection, would gather all this in one whom He knows to be fabricating against Him and claiming that He sent him to His servants – a lie and a display of affectation from him. And if this were permissible, then the manifestation of a miracle breaking the custom at the hands of a false claimant to prophethood in his claim would be even more permissible. And the impossibility of that has already passed, so likewise this.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer style argument. It first references a Quranic verse (26:180) as supporting the earlier point about the Prophet not seeking reward. Then it presents the core argument: the gathering of all these perfect qualities in the Prophet's body and character is a breach of normal custom (naqd al-ʿāda). Although individual qualities might exist in others, their combination is unprecedented. It then refutes a potential objection: one might think that God could gather these qualities in a false prophet. The author argues that this is impossible because if it were possible, then it would be even more plausible for a false prophet to perform a real miracle (breaking custom), but that has already been proven impossible. Therefore, the gathering of these qualities is a true sign of prophethood.

Key Terms
اجتماع المعاني (gathering of qualities)
نقض العادة (breach of custom)
معجزة (miracle)
متنبئ كاذب (false prophet)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Prophet's qualities could be ordinary and not miraculous, or that a false prophet could also possess such qualities.
Correction: The combination of all these perfect qualities in one person is unprecedented and beyond normal custom, making it a genuine miracle. Moreover, the argument shows that if a false prophet could possess them, he could also perform miracles, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
Why is it impossible that a false prophet could possess all the perfect qualities mentioned?
A) Because he would not want them.
B) Because if it were possible, then he could also perform real miracles, which is impossible.
C) Because the qualities are only for the true Prophet.
D) Because the qualities are beyond human capacity.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unprecedented combination of perfect qualities is a divine miracle, and any claim that a false prophet could match it is self-defeating because it would imply false prophets can perform miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet's unparalleled combination of qualities is a divine proof from Allah, why do you still find it easy to pick and choose which parts of his example to follow? What would you need to change starting today to treat his character as a clear sign demanding complete obedience?
?
The argument shows that if a false prophet could possess these virtues, miracles would lose their meaning. In your own life, have you ever watered down the uniqueness of the Prophet by claiming that others can be just as good, thereby erasing the divine evidence? Repent from that attitude specifically today.
?
You have been given the knowledge that the gathering of these qualities is a breach of custom. But do you live as if this knowledge should revolutionize your relationship with the Prophet? Name one specific quality from his character that you have not taken seriously, and commit to embodying it this week as a response to this truth.

The Collective Certainty of Ahad Miracle Reports
Nasafi explains how accumulated ahad reports about miracles can yield certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how multiple ahad (individual) reports can collectively produce certainty about the occurrence of miracles, even if each report alone is not definitive.

Core Idea
Many ahad reports together can yield certainty.

Imam Nasafi addresses a common objection: many miracle reports are transmitted as isolated narrations (āḥād). How can such reports be trusted? He explains that when they are numerous and from sources impossible to collude in falsehood, they yield general certainty. This lesson examines his argument and its parallels in everyday knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the full Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the flow from stating the abundance of miracles to discussing their transmission.
Pay attention to the condition set by the phrase 'unless they are numerous...'
2
Identify the key condition
The passage states that ahad reports do not yield certainty for each individual event, unless they are numerous from people who cannot collude in lying. Identify this condition and understand its significance.
3
Reflect on the analogy
Nasafi compares the collective certainty to the widespread knowledge of legendary generous figures like Hatim al-Ta'i. Consider how this analogy illustrates the principle.
This shows that cumulative evidence can establish a general truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنبينا محمد عليه السلام من المعجزات الحسية ما لا يحصى كثرة، ذكرها نقلة الحديث وخلدوها في كتبهم وأعرضت عن ذلك مخافة التطويل. ثم وإن كان فيما ذكر أصحاب التواريخ ونقلة الأخبار والآثار أشياء نقلت على طريق الآحاد، وذلك لا يوجب العلم لكل فرد أنه حق لا محالة إلا أن ترادفها من أناس لا يتصور عليهم التواطؤ على الكذب، يكون دليلاً على ظهور ما هو الناقض للعادة في الجملة على يديه، وإن لم يقع العلم بكل فرد كحكاية الأفراد عن [؟] وجود حاتم [؟] وكعب بن مامة وأبي داوود الإيادي وهرم بن سنان المري.
And for our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, there are from the sensory miracles what cannot be counted due to multitude; the transmitters of hadith mentioned them and recorded them in their books, and I turned away from that for fear of prolongation. Then, even if among what the historians and transmitters of reports and traditions mentioned are things transmitted by way of individual reports (āḥād), and that does not necessitate knowledge for every individual that it is certainly true, unless they are numerous from people concerning whom collusion in lying is inconceivable, it becomes evidence for the appearance of what breaks the custom in general at his hands, even if knowledge of every individual does not occur – like the reporting of individuals about [؟] the existence of Hatim [؟] and Ka'b ibn Mamah and Abu Dawud al-Iyadi and Hirm ibn Sinan al-Murri.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage addresses the epistemological status of reports about the Prophet's miracles. It first notes that the sensory miracles (mu'jizāt ḥissiyya) of the Prophet are countless, but the author refrains from detailing them to avoid length. Then it discusses that many of these reports are transmitted as individual (āḥād) narrations. Such reports do not yield certain knowledge for each individual event by itself. However, when these narrations are numerous (mutarādifa) and come from people who cannot be imagined to collude in a lie, they provide certainty that in general miracles breaking custom did occur at his hands, even if one does not have certainty about every specific event. The author compares this to the widespread knowledge of legendary generosity of figures like Hatim al-Ta'i, Ka'b ibn Mamah, etc., though the reports about them are individual. This shows that the collective accumulation of such reports produces certainty of the general phenomenon.

Key Terms
معجزات حسية (sensory miracles)
طريق الآحاد (individual report)
ترادف (numerous successive reports)
تواطؤ على الكذب (collusion in lying)
نقض العادة (breach of custom)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ahad narrations are completely unreliable and cannot establish any knowledge.
Correction: While a single ahad report may not yield certainty, numerous ahad reports from independent, trustworthy sources can collectively produce general certainty.

Checkpoint
Under what condition do ahad narrations about miracles yield certainty according to Nasafi?
A) When they are recorded in books.
B) When they are numerous from people who cannot conspire to lie.
C) When they are accepted by historians.
D) When they are mentioned by poets.

Key Takeaway
Many ahad miracle reports, though individually uncertain, can collectively yield general certainty when they are numerous and from irreproachable sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that many ahad reports can give certainty about the Prophet's miracles. Is your own certainty about his prophethood built on such cumulative evidence, or have you simply accepted what you were taught? What would happen if you tried to trace the evidence for just one miracle story back to its sources? Will you do that starting today?
?
The author compares miracle reports to stories of legendary generous figures like Hatim. Think of a person you know of only through repeated stories. Why do you believe those stories? Now consider your belief in the Prophet's miracles: is it based on the same kind of accumulated testimony, or is it weaker? If it is weaker, what will you do to strengthen it?
?
Imagine you are asked by a skeptic why you believe miracles occurred. Could you explain the argument from accumulated ahad reports? If not, why not? Are you content to have a faith that you cannot defend with reason? Commit to learning this argument well enough to share it—this lesson is the first step.

The Impossibility of False Prophets Performing Miracles
Proof that false prophets cannot perform true miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the combination of perfect attributes in the Prophet constitutes a miracle and how it proves that false prophets cannot perform true miracles.

Core Idea
The Prophet's perfect attributes are a miracle that false prophets cannot possess.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents a powerful argument that the very character and physical perfection of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) is itself a miracle. He argues that if a false prophet could possess such a combination of perfections, then they would be even more likely to perform explicit miracles, but since miracles are impossible for false prophets, so is this perfection. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify its structure
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author references a Quranic verse and then presents a logical argument.
The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum.
2
Understand 'breaking custom' (naqd al-ʿādah)
The author says the combination of attributes in the Prophet is outside the continuous custom (khārij ʿan al-ʿādah al-mustamirrah). This is the definition of a miracle. Ask yourself: why is this combination considered a miracle?
3
Trace the logical implication
The author says if such a combination were possible for a false prophet, then explicit miracles would be even more permissible for him. Since explicit miracles are impossible for false prophets, the combination must also be impossible. This is the core proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا: وإلى هذا المعنى يرجع قوله تعالى فيما أمر نبيه عليه السلام بمخاطبة قومه به على سبيل الاحتجاج لنفسه: ﴿ وَمَا أَسْلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَجْرٍ (1) الآية - (وهذا تأويل حسن)(۲)(۳)، والله أعلم.
ثم اجتماع هذه المعاني التي اجتمعت في بدنه وأخلاقه خارج عن العادة المستمرة وإن (٤) كان وجود أفرادها على ما عليه العادة جائز من أفراد الأشخاص وأعيان الخلق، فكان ذلك من باب نقض العادة، ولن يظن أن الله تعالى مع كمال يجمع هذا كله فيمن يعلم أنه يتقول عليه ويدعي أنه أرسله إلى عباده إفكا منه وتحرصا ، ولو كان هذا جائزاً لكان إظهار المعجزة الناقضة للعادة على يدي المتنبئ الكاذب في دعواه أجوز ، وقد مر امتناع ذلك، فكذا هذا.
They said: And to this meaning goes back His statement, exalted is He, regarding what He commanded His Prophet, peace be upon him, to address his people with, by way of argument for Himself: "And I do not ask you for any reward for it" (Quran 26:180) — and this is a good interpretation, and God knows best. Then the combination of these attributes that have been gathered in his body and his character is outside the continuous custom, even if the existence of their individual instances according to custom is permissible for individual persons and beings. So that is from the category of breaking the custom. And it is not to be thought that God, exalted is He, with His perfection, would gather all this in someone He knows is lying about Him and claiming that He sent him to His servants, as a falsehood from him and a means of seeking gain. And if this were permissible, then the manifestation of a miracle that breaks the custom at the hand of a false claimant would be even more permissible, and the impossibility of that has already been mentioned. So likewise this.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a proof that false prophets cannot perform true miracles. The author argues that the combination of perfect attributes in the Prophet is itself a miracle breaking custom. If such a combination were possible for a false prophet, then it would be even more possible for him to perform explicit miracles. Since it is impossible for a false prophet to perform miracles (as established previously), it is also impossible for him to have such a combination of attributes.

Key Terms
معجزة
نقض العادة
متنبئ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is possible for a false prophet to perform miracles or have miraculous attributes.
Correction: God only supports true prophets with miracles; a false prophet cannot have genuinely miraculous attributes because that would contradict God's wisdom.

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument regarding the impossibility of a false prophet having miraculous attributes?
A) Because God knows who is truthful
B) Because if it were possible, then explicit miracles for false prophets would be even more likely, which is impossible
C) Because the Prophet's attributes are actually ordinary
D) Because the Quran prohibits it

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's perfect attributes constitute a miracle that false prophets cannot possess.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's perfect attributes are a miracle from God. When you look at your own character, do you see the same level of dedication to embodying truthfulness and excellence? What one specific habit can you change today to better reflect the Prophet's character?
?
The passage argues that God would never honor a liar with a miracle. Does this truth strengthen your conviction that the Prophet was sent by God? How does that certainty challenge you to obey his commands even when they are difficult?
?
If the combination of virtues in the Prophet is beyond ordinary human capacity, then you cannot achieve it on your own. Are you relying on divine help to purify your character, or are you content with mediocrity? What is one prayer you can make today to seek God's assistance in this?

The Cumulative Tawatur of the Prophet's Miracles
Argument that multiple ahad reports collectively yield certain knowledge of miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how multiple ahad reports about the Prophet's miracles can collectively yield certain knowledge through cumulative tawatur.

Core Idea
Many ahad reports together can give certain knowledge just like stories of famous heroes.

Having established the general proof of prophethood, we now turn to the specific miracles of Prophet Muhammad. While many miracle reports are individually transmitted as ahad, their sheer number and variety from different sources combine to produce certain knowledge that miracles indeed occurred. This passage explains this cumulative argument using analogies from well-known figures of generosity and bravery.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the entire Arabic passage carefully, noting the mention of countless miracles and the ahad/tawatur distinction.
Focus on the examples of Hatim, 'Antarah, etc.
2
Analyze the analogy
The author uses the analogies of generosity and bravery to show how individual ahad stories yield collective certainty. Identify how this applies to miracles.
Notice the phrase 'في حيز الآحاد' and 'في حيز التواتر'.
3
Understand the usuli principle
The passage concludes with a principle from usul al-fiqh: particulars combine to yield a necessary universal. Reflect on how this is applied to the Prophet's miracles.
Consider why the splitting of the moon etc. are mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكمته
ولنبينا محمد عليه السلام من المعجزات الحسية ما لا يحصى كثرة، ذكرها
نقلة الحديث وخلدوها في كتبهم وأعرضت عن ذلك مخافة التطويل.
ثم وإن كان فيما ذكر أصحاب التواريخ ونقلة الأخبار والآثار أشياء نقلت على طريق الآحاد ، وذلك لا يوجب العلم لكل فرد أنه حق لا محالة إلا أن ترادفها من أناس لا يتصور عليهم التواطؤ على الكذب، يكون دليلاً على ظهور ما هو الناقض للعادة في الجملة على يديه، وإن لم يقع العلم بكل فرد كحكاية الأفراد عن () (۷) وجود حاتم ( ) وكعب بن مامة (٦) وأبي داوود الإيادي (٧) وهرم بن سنان (۸) المري
والأجواد العشرة في صدر الإسلام، والبرامكة ومع ابن زائدة وغيرهم من الأجواد. وشجاعة عامر بن الطفيل (۱) وعتيبة (۲) بن الحارث بن (۳) شهاب، وبسطام بن قيس(4)
وعنترة بن شداد ()، وعمرو بن معد يكرب(٦)، وربيع بن عباد البكري، وحكمة أكثم بن صيفي وعامر بن الظرب (۱) وغير ذلك.
فإن حكاية كل فرد معنى من هذه المعاني عن المحكى عنه إن كان لا يوجب العلم بصحة (۸) تلك الحكاية بعينها فإنه يوجب العلم بكونه (۹) موصوفا بما وصف به في الجملة، فكانت كل حكاية في حق تلك الصورة التي وردت عنها في حيز الآحاد وهي بكليتها في حق أصل الجود والشجاعة في حيز التواتر الموجب للعلم حتى إن أحدًا لم
yتردد في قلبه شك في جود من تقدم ذكره من الموصوفين بالجود، وكذا في شجاعة من مر ذكره، وكذا العلم والحكمة لما فكذا كل فرد من الأخيار في حق صورة ذلك
المروى بعينه في حيز الآحاد ومجموعها في حق أنه كانت تظهر على يده المعجزات
الناقضات للعادة في حيز التواتر الموجب للعلم بذلك.
وهذا معنى قول أهل الأصول إن الجزئيات المجوزة يتركب من مجوعها كلي موجب، ولسنا نعني أن كلا الشاة وشكاية الناقة وحنين الأسطوانة، وما ذكرنا نحن من قبيل هذا، بل كل واحد مما ذكرنا ثبت برواية قوم لا يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب،
Its wisdom. And our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, has sensory miracles that are countless in number; the transmitters of hadith have mentioned them and recorded them in their books, and I have refrained from that out of fear of length. Then, even if among what the historians and transmitters of reports and traditions have mentioned there are things transmitted by way of ahad (single-chain reports), and that does not necessitate certain knowledge for every individual that it is absolutely true, unless they are consecutive from people whose collusion upon falsehood is inconceivable, it becomes evidence for the appearance of what breaks the custom in general at his hand, even if certain knowledge of every individual does not occur. Like the stories of individuals about the existence of Hatim, and Ka'b ibn Mamah, and Abu Dawud al-Iyadi, and Harm ibn Sinan al-Murri, and the ten generous people in early Islam, and the Barmakids, and Ma'n ibn Za'idah, and other generous people. And the bravery of 'Amir ibn al-Tufayl, and 'Utaybah ibn al-Harith ibn Shihab, and Bistam ibn Qays, and 'Antarah ibn Shaddad, and 'Amr ibn Ma'dikarib, and Rabi' ibn 'Abbad al-Bakri, and the wisdom of Aktham ibn Sayfi and 'Amir ibn al-Zarib and others. For the story of each individual of these meanings from the one it is reported about, if it does not necessitate certain knowledge of the correctness of that story in particular, it does necessitate certain knowledge that he is characterized by what he is described with in general. So each story regarding that particular image from which it came is in the realm of ahad, but they collectively, regarding the principle of generosity and bravery, are in the realm of tawatur (consecutive transmission) that necessitates knowledge, such that no one hesitates in his heart with doubt about the generosity of those mentioned among those described with generosity, and similarly about the bravery of those mentioned, and likewise knowledge and wisdom. So likewise, every individual report from the chosen ones (the prophets?) regarding the particular image of that which is reported itself is in the realm of ahad, but their totality regarding the fact that miracles breaking the custom appeared at his hand is in the realm of tawatur which necessitates knowledge of that. And this is the meaning of the statement of the people of usul: "The particular permissibles combine from their totality to yield a necessary universal." And we do not mean the splitting of the moon and the complaint of the she-camel and the yearning of the pillar, and what we have mentioned is of this type; rather, every single one of what we have mentioned is established by the transmission of a people whose collusion upon falsehood is inconceivable.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage explains the epistemological basis for believing in the Prophet's miracles. The author states that the Prophet's sensory miracles are too many to count. Although many of the reports about them are transmitted as ahad (single-chain), the accumulation of such reports from many different sources and events makes the occurrence of miracles in general a matter of tawatur (consecutive transmission) that yields certain knowledge. He uses the analogy of famous generous and brave people: individual stories about Hatim's generosity or 'Antarah's bravery are ahad, but no one doubts their character. Similarly, the many miracle reports together give certainty that the Prophet performed miracles. The author cites the principle of usul: 'particular probables combine to yield a necessary universal.' He clarifies that these are not like the splitting of the moon, etc., but each report is established by a group whose collusion upon falsehood is inconceivable.

Key Terms
آحاد
تواتر
معجزات
علم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only reports that are individually mutawatir (mass-transmitted) can yield certain knowledge.
Correction: This passage shows that multiple ahad reports, when combined from independent sources, can produce cumulative tawatur and thus certain knowledge of a general fact, such as the occurrence of miracles.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to explain how multiple ahad reports give certain knowledge?
A) The miracles of Moses
B) The generosity of Hatim and bravery of 'Antarah
C) The splitting of the moon
D) The wisdom of Luqman

Key Takeaway
The many ahad reports about the Prophet's miracles, taken together, create a cumulative tawatur that produces certain knowledge of his miraculous nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson shows that many weak reports can together give certain knowledge. What 'weak' spiritual habits or doubts in your life have been building up without you noticing? Will you let them accumulate and become certain disbelief, or will you actively replace them with certainties of faith?
?
You are certain about the generosity of Hatim based on stories, but how certain are you about the Prophet's miracles? Does your level of certainty reflect the weight of evidence, or is it influenced by the world's skepticism? What will you do to bridge that gap?
?
The principle says 'particular permissibles combine to a necessary universal.' Your small acts of worship—are they adding up to a certain evidence of your faith, or are they scattered and aimless? If they were put together, would they prove you are truly devoted to Allah? What one change can you make today to ensure your 'particulars' lead to a 'necessary universal' of sincere belief?

How Individual Reports Create Certainty: The Pre-Islamic Arab Examples
Author uses pre-Islamic Arab examples to illustrate how ahad reports collectively yield certain knowledge of general traits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how individual reports (akhbar ahad) about general traits like generosity and bravery can collectively yield certain knowledge.

Core Idea
Many uncertain reports together produce certain knowledge.

Before discussing miracles, the author illustrates a key epistemological principle using well-known pre-Islamic Arab figures known for generosity, bravery, and wisdom. No single report about a specific act gives certainty, but the multitude of reports leaves no doubt about the person's overall character.

Guided Path
1
Read the examples of generous and brave Arabs
Read the list of famous individuals known for generosity, bravery, and wisdom. Notice that each report is about a specific trait.
These examples are well-known in Arab tradition.
2
Understand the claim about certainty
The author states that each individual report does not give certain knowledge of that specific act, but the totality of reports about the same person gives certain knowledge of the trait in general.
This is the key insight: a + a + a = A (certain).
3
Reflect on the analogy for miracles
Consider how this principle will be applied to miracles in the next lesson.
The same logic applies: many ahad reports about miracles give certain knowledge that miracles occurred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأجواد العشرة في صدر الإسلام، والبرامكة ومع ابن زائدة وغيرهم من الأجواد. وشجاعة عامر بن الطفيل وعتيبة بن الحارث بن شهاب، وبسطام بن قيس وعنترة بن شداد، وعمرو بن معد يكرب، وربيع بن عباد البكري، وحكمة أكثم بن صيفي وعامر بن الظرب وغير ذلك. فإن حكاية كل فرد معنى من هذه المعاني عن المحكى عنه إن كان لا يوجب العلم بصحة تلك الحكاية بعينها فإنه يوجب العلم بكونه موصوفا بما وصف به في الجملة، فكانت كل حكاية في حق تلك الصورة التي وردت عنها في حيز الآحاد وهي بكليتها في حق أصل الجود والشجاعة في حيز التواتر الموجب للعلم حتى إن أحدًا لم يتردد في قلبه شك في جود من تقدم ذكره من الموصوفين بالجود، وكذا في شجاعة من مر ذكره، وكذا العلم والحكمة لما فكذا كل فرد من الأخيار في حق صورة ذلك المروى بعينه في حيز الآحاد ومجموعها في حق أنه كانت تظهر على يده المعجزات الناقضات للعادة في حيز التواتر الموجب للعلم بذلك. وهذا معنى قول أهل الأصول إن الجزئيات المجوزة يتركب من مجوعها كلي موجب، ولسنا نعني أن كلا الشاة وشكاية الناقة وحنين الأسطوانة، وما ذكرنا نحن من قبيل هذا، بل كل واحد مما ذكرنا ثبت برواية قوم لا يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب، فكان كل فرد من ذلك ثابتا بطريق التيقن كأنا عايناه، ولثبوته برواية من لا يتصور منهم التواطؤ على الكذب، وبالله التوفيق.
And the ten generous ones in early Islam, and the Barmakids, and Ibn Za'ida and other generous ones. And the bravery of 'Amir ibn al-Tufayl, and 'Utayba ibn al-Harith ibn Shihab, and Bistam ibn Qays, and 'Antara ibn Shaddad, and 'Amr ibn Ma'di Karib, and Rabi' ibn 'Abbad al-Bakri, and the wisdom of Aktham ibn Sayfi and 'Amir ibn al-Zarib and others besides. For the report of every individual meaning from these meanings about the one reported of, if it does not necessitate knowledge of the soundness of that specific report, it nevertheless necessitates knowledge that he is described with what was described in general. Thus every report regarding that specific instance which was transmitted about it is in the category of ahad, but in its totality regarding the origin of generosity and bravery it is in the category of tawatur that necessitates knowledge, so much so that not a single person has any doubt in his heart about the generosity of those previously mentioned who are described with generosity, and similarly about the bravery of those mentioned, and likewise knowledge and wisdom. Likewise, every individual report about the miracles in the case of that specific transmitted event is in the category of ahad, but their totality regarding the fact that miracles breaking the customs appeared at his hand is in the category of tawatur that necessitates knowledge of that. And this is the meaning of the statement of the scholars of usul: 'The individual permissible parts combine from their totality into a necessary universal.' And we do not mean that each of the complaint of the sheep, the complaint of the camel, and the weeping of the pillar, and what we have mentioned is of this type. Rather, each one of what we have mentioned is established by the transmission of a group (qawm) concerning whom collusion upon falsehood cannot be imagined. Thus every individual report of that is established by the method of certainty as if we had seen it, and due to its being established by the transmission of those concerning whom collusion upon falsehood cannot be imagined. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a proof that individual reports (akhbar ahad) about miracles, when taken together, yield certain knowledge (tawatur). The author begins with examples from pre-Islamic Arabia: famous generous individuals (like the ten generous ones, the Barmakids) and brave individuals (like 'Amir ibn al-Tufayl, 'Antara). The point is that no single report about a specific act of generosity or bravery gives certain knowledge of that particular act, but all the reports together give certain knowledge that the person was characterized by generosity or bravery in general. Similarly, each report of a specific miracle (like the speaking of the sheep, the complaint of the camel, the weeping of the pillar) is ahad and does not individually necessitate certainty about that exact event, but the totality of such reports from the Prophet (peace be upon him) yields certain knowledge that miracles occurred at his hand. The author likens this to the principle in usul al-fiqh: 'The individual permissible parts combine from their totality into a necessary universal' — i.e., many uncertain reports can together produce certainty. He clarifies that he does not mean each specific miracle story (like the sheep's complaint) is proven by tawatur individually, but rather the collective mass of reported miracles from reliable transmitters, who cannot conspire to lie, gives certain knowledge that miracles happened. Thus, the existence of prophetic miracles is known with certainty, even if the details of some specific miracles are not individually certain.

Key Terms
آحاد
تواتر
يقين
جزئيات مجوزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Each individual report about a specific act of generosity or bravery gives certain knowledge of that exact act.
Correction: The author argues that individual reports are ahad and do not give certainty about the specific act; rather, the aggregate gives certain knowledge of the general trait.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does no one doubt the generosity of the ten generous ones?
A) Because each report about their generosity is individually certain.
B) Because the totality of reports about their generosity yields certain knowledge.
C) Because they were well-known to everyone at the time.
D) Because the reports come from the same source.

Key Takeaway
Individual reports about a person's character, though uncertain individually, collectively yield certain knowledge about that character.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about the stories you have heard about the character of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). Do you treat each story as just an isolated report, or do you allow them to build a certain conviction of his beautiful character? Where is your level of certainty now, and what would it take to reach the level of no doubt?
?
This lesson teaches that many small, uncertain reports together produce certain knowledge of a trait. Where in your own life have you allowed a collection of small doubts to build into a certain negative judgment about someone? How can you use this principle to seek the truth about others' character rather than assuming the worst?
?
Are there qualities you have heard reported about yourself from multiple sources? Do you accept that collective testimony as certain, or do you dismiss it? How can you use this principle to recognize and cultivate virtues you may be blind to, and what change will you commit to today based on that?

From Individual Miracles to Certain Knowledge: The Usul Principle
Author applies the previous logic to miracles and states the usul principle with clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the principle that 'individual permissible parts combine into a necessary universal' applies to reports of miracles, yielding certain knowledge that miracles occurred.

Core Idea
The totality of miracle reports from reliable transmitters gives certain knowledge of prophethood.

The author now applies the same logic to miracles. Each specific miracle story like the speaking of the sheep or the weeping of the pillar is ahad, but the collective mass of such stories from reliable sources yields certain knowledge that the Prophet performed miracles. He also clarifies a key usul principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the application to miracles
Read how the author extends the analogy to miracles: each miracle report is ahad, but collectively they are tawatur regarding the occurrence of miracles.
The same logic as the pre-Islamic examples.
2
Understand the usul principle
Learn the principle: 'The individual permissible parts combine from their totality into a necessary universal.' This is a foundational idea in usul al-fiqh.
This principle explains how many uncertain reports can yield certainty.
3
Note the clarification
The author clarifies that he does not mean each specific miracle story (like the sheep's complaint) is proven by tawatur individually; rather, each is established by a group that cannot conspire to lie, giving certainty as if seen.
This prevents misunderstanding that every detail is certain.

Commentary
This passage is a proof that individual reports (akhbar ahad) about miracles, when taken together, yield certain knowledge (tawatur). The author begins with examples from pre-Islamic Arabia: famous generous individuals (like the ten generous ones, the Barmakids) and brave individuals (like 'Amir ibn al-Tufayl, 'Antara). Misconception & Correction

?

?

?

In your own life, where are you failing to see Allah's signs because you focus on individual weaknesses or doubts? What step will you take this week to look at the bigger picture and increase your certainty in Allah's truth?

Categories of the Prophet's Intellectual Miracles
Author enumerates the categories of the Prophet's intellectual miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the comprehensive classification of the Prophet's intellectual miracles as outlined by Imam al-Nasafi.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intellectual miracles go far beyond the Qur'an, covering his life, reports, and legacy.

Imam al-Nasafi provides a detailed taxonomy of the Prophet's intellectual miracles. He begins by listing the broad categories, then delves into subcategories, particularly for his reports. This systematic enumeration sets the stage for deeper proofs in later chapters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping, then the English translation. Notice how the author organizes the material with repetition of 'minha' and divisions.
The passage is a classified list, not a flowing argument.
2
Identify the main categories and subcategories
Look for the initial four categories (state, lineage, call, reports) and then the subdivisions of reports. Also note the additional categories after death, place, time, book, and shari'a.
Make a mental or written tree diagram.
3
Reflect on the purpose of this classification
Ask yourself why the author begins with this classification. What does it show about the nature of intellectual miracles? Consider how each category independently points to prophethood.
This connects to the core idea.

معجزاته عليه السلام العقلية وأقسامها: وأما معجزاته العقلية فمنقسمة إلى أقسام فمنها ما هو راجع إلى حالة ومنها ما هو راجع إلى نسبه، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى دعوته، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى أخباره، وهذا ينقسم إلى قسمين: أحدهما ما ورد مع البشارات به في الكتب المتقدمة والأمم الماضية. والثاني: إخباره عن الكائنات، وهذا القسم الأخير ينقسم إلى قسمين: أحدهما: إخباره عن أمور ماضية. والثاني: إخباره عن أمور توجد في المستقبل ومنها معجزات ظهرت بعد وفاته عليه السلام، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى مكانه، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى زمانه، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى كتابه الذي أتى به، ومنها ما هو راجع إلى شريعته التي اختص بها. ونبين في كل فصل من هذه الفصول ما يوجب ثلج الصدر، ويسوق إلى القلوب برد اليقين، وإن ضاق عن ذلك صدر المتعنتين، ورغم أنف الملحدين الذين وصفهم الله تعالى في كتابه بقوله تعالى: فَإِنَّهُمْ لَا يُكَذِّبُونَكَ وَلَكِنَّ الظَّالِمِينَ بِآيَاتِ اللَّهِ يَجْحَدُونَ.
His (peace be upon him) intellectual miracles and their divisions: As for his intellectual miracles, they are divided into sections. Some of them relate to his state, some relate to his lineage, some relate to his call, and some relate to his reports. And this (i.e., the reports) is divided into two parts: one of them is what came with the glad tidings of him in the previous scriptures and past nations. The second is his reports about future things. And this last part is divided into two parts: one of them is his reports about past matters, and the second is his reports about matters that occur in the future. And among them are miracles that appeared after his death (peace be upon him), and among them are what relate to his place, and among them are what relate to his time, and among them are what relate to his book which he brought, and among them are what relate to his shari'a which was uniquely his. And we will explain in each chapter of these chapters what causes the breast to be tranquil and brings to the hearts the coolness of certainty, even if the breasts of the obstinate are straitened by that, and despite the noses of the atheists whom Allah the Exalted has described in His Book with His saying: 'For indeed they do not deny you, but the wrongdoers reject the verses of Allah.'
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the intellectual miracles (mu'jizat 'aqliyya) of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author lists several categories. First, miracles relating to the Prophet's state (hala), his lineage (nasab), his call (da'wa), and his reports (akhbar). The reports category is further subdivided: (a) prophecies about him in earlier scriptures, and (b) his reports about future events. The latter is again subdivided into reports about past matters (i.e., accurate historical information) and reports about future matters (predictions). Then additional categories are mentioned: miracles that appeared after his death, miracles relating to his place (e.g., the city of Medina), his time (the era of his prophethood), his book (the Qur'an), and his shari'a (the Islamic law). The author promises to explain each of these in detail in subsequent chapters, aiming to bring tranquility and certainty to the reader, while it may distress the obstinate and anger the atheists, who are described in the Qur'an as rejecting Allah's verses while not actually denying the Prophet himself.

Key Terms
معجزات عقلية
دعوة
أخبار
بشارات
شريعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The only intellectual miracle of the Prophet is the Qur'an.
Correction: This passage shows that intellectual miracles include many aspects: his state, lineage, reports (prophecies, historical accuracy), after-death miracles, place, time, book (Qur'an), and shari'a.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The intellectual miracles of the Prophet encompass multiple dimensions, each providing evidence for his prophethood.

The Miracles of His State: His Unlettered People
Author begins explaining the first subcategory of miracles related to the Prophet's state, namely his people.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's illiterate background itself constitutes a miracle and why the first division of his state-related miracles focuses on his people.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unlettered people became the stage for the miracle of the Qur'an.

When we consider the Prophet's state, one of the most striking aspects is his background. He came from a people who did not read or write—a nation of oral tradition. The author begins by classifying the miracles related to the Prophet's personal state into four divisions, and the first one highlights this very fact about his people. This passage sets the stage for understanding how his illiteracy and that of his community was not a weakness but a proof of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage in Arabic and English
Read the Arabic text carefully, then the translation. Notice the structure: the author gives a classification and then describes the first division.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the four divisions mentioned (though only the first is given here) and note what makes the first division remarkable: the Prophet's people were unscripted.
3
Reflect on the miraculous aspect
Ask yourself why being from an illiterate people is considered a miracle. The Qur'an's eloquence, coming from such a background, points to divine origin.
This connects to the broader argument for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعجزات الراجعة إلى حاله وأقسامها: وأما ما هو راجع إلى حاله فمنقسم إلى أقسام أربعة: أحدها: ما هو راجع إلى قومه فإنه كان من قوم لا يعرفون الكتب
The miracles relating to his state and their divisions: As for what relates to his state, it is divided into four divisions: One of them is what relates to his people, for he was from a people who did not know the scriptures.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a definition and explanation of the first subcategory of the Prophet's intellectual miracles, specifically those relating to his personal state (hala). The author states that this category is divided into four parts. The first part concerns his people (qawm): the Prophet was from a people—the Arabs of the time—who were unlettered and did not possess scriptures. This is presented as a miraculous aspect because, despite this background, he brought the Qur'an, which is of unparalleled eloquence and contains knowledge of the unseen. The author will likely elaborate on how this very fact points to the divine origin of his message.

Key Terms

قومه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Prophet's illiteracy and his people's ignorance of scriptures was a deficiency or weakness.
Correction: It was a miraculous sign because it showed the Qur'an could not have been humanly produced.

A) His lineage
B) His people
C) His call
D) His reports

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's illiterate background and his people's lack of scripture turned into a powerful proof of the divine origin of the Qur'an.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Proof from the Prophet's Unlearned Knowledge of the Unseen
Continuation of the first proof: the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen despite his environment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's upbringing and environment demonstrate the divine origin of his knowledge of the unseen.

Core Idea
The Prophet's knowledge came from Allah, not from human teachers.

In this passage, the theologian continues the first proof of prophethood by focusing on the Prophet's biography. Despite living among illiterate Bedouins and having no access to scriptures or scholars, the Prophet brought news of the unseen that he could not have learned naturally. This argument uses the known facts of his life to show that his message could only be from God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it, then read the translation. Notice how the author builds the argument step by step.
The passage begins mid-sentence; it continues a previous line of reasoning.
2
Identify the conditions of the Prophet's environment
The author lists several factors: the town was in the desert, only illiterate Bedouins visited, the Prophet was only briefly absent for a trade journey, and no learned scholars came to Mecca to teach him. These establish that he had no human means of acquiring the knowledge he later brought.
These conditions are crucial to the argument.
3
Note the Qur'anic verses cited as evidence
The passage quotes several verses (e.g., 'That is from the news of the unseen...', 'Or did they not recognize their Messenger...', 'And you did not recite before it any scripture...', 'I have remained among you a lifetime before it...'). Each verse reinforces that the Prophet could not have learned this knowledge from any human source.
The Mubahala challenge (invoking mutual imprecation) shows the Prophet's certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودراستها، وكانت بلدتهم في البراري لا يشهدها إلا الأعراب الأميون الذين كان الغالب عليهم الجهل، ثم هو لم يغب عنهم إلا مدة يسيرة في سفره إلى الشام مع العير، ولم يغب عنهم، ولم يقدم عليهم مكة أحد من أحبار أهل الكتاب والعلماء بشرائع الأمم المتقدمة يختصه ممن هو دونه ويعتكف على تعريفه ما في الكتب السالفة، ثم إنه علم أنباء الغيب الذي لم يكن يعلمها هو ولا أحد من قومه، وبلغ في ذلك الثقة به والطمأنينة إليه إلى أن قال عند مجادلتهم إياه: تَعَالَوْا نَدْعُ أَبْنَاءَنَا وَأَبْنَاءَكُمْ وقال تعالى: تِلْكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الغَيْبِ نُوحِيهَا إِلَيْكَ مَا كُنتَ تَعْلَمُهَا أَنتَ وَلَا قَوْمُكَ ولم ينسبه أحد منهم إلى تعلم قد تفرد به وأنفق عمره في تحصيله، وقال تعالى: أَمْ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا رَسُولَهُمْ فَهُمْ لَهُ مُنكَرُونَ وقال: وَمَا كُنتَ تَتْلُوا مِن قَبْلِهِ، مِن كِتَبٍ وَلَا تَخُطُّهُ بِيَمِينِكَ إِذًا لَارْتَابَ الْمُبْطِلُونَ وقال: فَقَدْ لَبِثْتُ فِيكُمْ عُمُرًا مِّن قَبْلِهِ، أَفَلَا تَعْقِلُونَ
And his study? And their town was in the desert, where none visited except the illiterate Bedouins who were mostly ignorant. Then he was not absent from them except for a short period in his journey to Syria with the caravan, and he was not absent from them, and no Jewish or Christian scholar or knowledgeable person of the laws of past nations came to Mecca to single him out from those below him and devote himself to teaching him what is in the previous books. Then he knew the news of the unseen which neither he nor any of his people knew, and he reached such confidence and assurance in that that he said during their argument with him: 'Come, let us call our sons and your sons.' And the Almighty said: 'That is from the news of the unseen which We reveal to you; you did not know it, nor did your people.' And none of them attributed to him that he had learned what he had uniquely done and spent his life acquiring it. And the Almighty said: 'Or did they not recognize their Messenger, so they deny him?' And He said: 'And you did not recite before it any scripture, nor did you write it with your right hand; then the falsifiers would have doubted.' And He said: 'I have remained among you a lifetime before it; will you not then reason?'
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof of prophethood (continued from previous pages). It establishes that the Prophet Muhammad lived in an environment of ignorance, with no access to learned scholars or scripture. He was only briefly absent for a trade journey to Syria. Despite this, he suddenly brought news of the unseen, including the challenge of Mubahala (mutual imprecation) and the revelation of past events. The Qur'anic verses confirm that he was not a reciter or writer before revelation, and his own people acknowledged he lived among them for forty years without any such knowledge. Thus, his knowledge could not have been acquired through human means, proving it is from God. This argument uses the Prophet's known background to demonstrate the supernatural origin of his message.

Key Terms
أنباء الغيب
المباهلة
الأعراب الأميون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Prophet's brief trade journey to Syria provided him with knowledge from the People of the Book.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the journey was short and that no scholars came to teach him; his knowledge could not have been acquired that way.

Checkpoint
What is the primary argument in this passage to prove the Prophet's knowledge is from God?
A) He traveled to learn from scholars
B) The Meccans taught him secretly

D) He was a poet who composed the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unlearned knowledge of the unseen, in the context of his known environment, proves his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have known for years that the Prophet ﷺ was unlettered, yet did you ever truly reflect on what that means for the authenticity of his message? When you read the Qur'an today, do you approach it as a divine revelation that could only come from Allah, or do you passively assume it without awe? How would your recitation change if you internalized that the one who brought it had no human teacher and no books?
?
The Prophet ﷺ lived among his people for forty years before revelation. Consider your own life—what have you spent forty years known for? Yet he was known for honesty and trustworthiness, not for any claim to divine knowledge. Does your daily conduct reflect that you are a follower of a prophet whose entire life was a testament to truth, or do you carelessly ignore the weight of his example?
?
This passage argues from the Prophet's environment and circumstances. Look at your own environment—are you surrounded by influences that could cause you to doubt or forget the origin of this message? The proof here is that from a 'desert' of ignorance, such profound knowledge could only come from Allah. In your life, are you actively seeking reminders that reinforce your faith, or are you letting a 'desert' of heedlessness make you forget the unmistakeable signs of prophethood?

Second Proof: No Prior Training in Oratory
Second proof: the Prophet was not known as a speaker or debater before prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second rational proof for prophethood: the Prophet's sudden emergence of inimitable eloquence despite having no prior training in oratory.

Core Idea
An untrained speaker producing matchless eloquence proves divine origin.

This proof focuses on the Prophet Muhammad's personal history. Before prophethood, he was not known as an eloquent speaker or debater. Yet he suddenly produced the Qur'an, a speech beyond human capacity. This sudden leap from an untaught man indicates divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical flow: premise, premise, conclusion.
2
Identify the two premises
The passage states: (1) The Prophet had no prior reputation as a speaker or debater. (2) If he had, his close associates would have known. Then it adds that human nature requires gradual learning, but his speech came suddenly.
These premises support the conclusion that his speech is not human.
3
Understand the logical conclusion
The conclusion is implied: the sudden production of speech that all humans fail to imitate, from someone untrained, proves it is from Allah. Reflect on why this is convincing.
This argument is a form of miracle, similar to the inimitability of the Qur'an.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني: أنه لم يكن قبل إظهار الدعوة متكلما لما أظهره، ولا خائضا نظم الكلام وتأليفه، ولو كان شرع في شيء من ذلك لظهر لمعاشريه ولما خفى على أهل بطانته، وليس من طباع البشر التصدي لمثل ذلك الخطب الجليل والتعرض لمخالفة العالم فجأة بلا مقدمة ولا القدرة على الإتيان بكلام يعجز عنه الخلق بغتة من غير تدريج
And the second: that before declaring his call, he was not a speaker of what he presented, nor one who engaged in the composition and arrangement of speech. If he had entered into any of that, it would have appeared to his contemporaries and would not have been hidden from his close associates. And it is not in human nature to undertake such a great matter and to expose oneself to opposing the world suddenly without any precedent, nor is it in human capacity to produce speech that creatures are incapable of all at once without gradual training.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage gives the second proof: the Prophet had no prior reputation as an eloquent speaker or debater before his prophethood. He did not train in composing speeches or arguments. If he had, his close companions would have known. Yet he suddenly produced the Qur'an, which all humans are unable to imitate. This sudden emergence of unparalleled eloquence from someone untrained in oratory proves it is not from human effort but from divine revelation. Human nature requires gradual learning; the Prophet's abrupt mastery defies natural explanation.

Key Terms
متكلما
نظم الكلام
إظهار الدعوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the second proof argue about the Prophet's eloquence?
A) He learned from famous poets
B) He gradually improved over years
C) He was not previously known as a speaker, yet produced inimitable speech
D) He copied from earlier scriptures

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's lack of prior oratory training combined with his sudden production of the inimitable Qur'an proves his prophethood is from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

In what area of your life today can you step out in faith, relying on Allah rather than your own training?
?
The proof highlights that the Prophet's close associates would have known if he had practiced oratory. Think about those closest to you: do they see a consistency between your public profession of faith and your private conduct? Is there any secret 'practice' of habits that contradict what you claim to believe? What will you do about that discrepancy starting today?
?
Given that the Prophet's lack of training was widely known and undeniable, this proof challenges any doubt about the divine origin of the Qur'an. If you have ever doubted, what concrete step will you take this week to resolve that doubt—perhaps by reciting the Qur'an with contemplation or studying its inimitability further?

Third Proof: Divine Aid Despite Apparent Weakness
Third proof: the Prophet opposed all while weak, yet succeeded supernaturally.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's triumph while in a state of weakness constitutes a rational proof of prophethood, demonstrating that his mission was divinely supported.

Core Idea
The Prophet's triumph without human means proves his mission was divinely supported.

This passage presents the third proof from Imam al-Nasafi: the Prophet faced the entire world while poor and powerless, yet his message spread irresistibly. This success could not have been achieved by human effort alone; it points directly to divine assistance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the vivid contrast between the Prophet's weakness and his enemies' strength.
2
Identify the key contrast
The passage details two opposing states: the Prophet's weakness (poverty, few helpers) and his enemies' power (wealth, numbers, weaponry). Observe how this contrast is developed.
3
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that the spread of Islam despite the Prophet's lack of human resources can only be explained by divine assistance. Ask yourself: could any purely human strategy achieve this?
This is the core of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث: أنه انتصب في حال ضعفه وفقره وفاقته وقلة أعوانه حربا لجميع أهل الأرض ومتعرضا للملوك والجبارين وذوي القدرة والبسطة، وعاداهم معاداة الدين، وهي أشد أنواع العداوة، وسفه أحلامهم وأحلام آبائهم الذين كانوا يعتادون التفاخر بمآثرهم ومناقبهم، وكان أشد الناس عليه عشيرته الأقربون ورهطه الأدنون، ولم يأخذه في الله لومة لائم، وطلبوا منه أدنى مداهنة ليتابعوه وأيسر مسايلة لينقادوا له، فلم يعطهم ذلك ولم يساعدهم عليه، ثم إنهم مع قوة أبدانهم وكثرة عددهم ووفور عدوهم أتوا بأقصى ما في وسعهم من الجد والاجتهاد واستعمال العدة والعتاد لإطفاء نوره وطمس آثاره فلم يزدد ذلك إلا كثرة الأتباع وقوة الأشياع وانتشار الدعوة وشد الشوكة من غير أن كان ذلك راجعا إلى معونة بشرية على ما عليه أمر طلاب دول الدنيا المعتمدين في ذلك على كثرة الأموال وقوة الأنصار والأعوان، بل كان نشأ يتيما لا تبع له وعائلا لا مال له، وهذا من أول الدلائل على أن أمره كان مبنيا على المعونة الإلهية والتأييد السماوي، ولهذا كان نصره بالرعب وكان يخاف منه مسيرة شهر.
And the third: that he stood up, in a state of weakness, poverty, neediness, and few helpers, as a war against all the people of the earth, exposing himself to kings, tyrants, and those of power and authority. He opposed them with religious enmity, which is the severest type of enmity, and he belittled their intellects and the intellects of their fathers, who used to boast of their exploits and merits. And the most severe of people against him were his closest clan and nearest relatives. And he let no blame of a blamer affect him in [the cause of] God. They asked him for the slightest compromise to follow him and the easiest concession to submit to him, but he did not give them that and did not assist them. Then, with the strength of their bodies, their great numbers, and the abundance of their enemies? They exerted their utmost in effort and diligence and the use of equipment and weaponry to extinguish his light and obliterate his traces. That only increased the number of followers, the strength of partisans, the spread of the call, and the firmness of his power, without that being due to any human assistance, unlike the case of seekers of worldly power who rely on abundance of wealth and strength of supporters and helpers. Rather, he grew up an orphan with no followers and a dependant with no wealth. This is among the clearest indications that his affair was based on divine assistance and heavenly support. For this reason, he was aided with awe and was feared from a distance of a month's journey.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof: the Prophet single-handedly confronted the entire world while in a state of extreme weakness - poor, orphaned, with few initial followers. He opposed the powerful, including his own relatives, with uncompromising religious enmity. They offered him wealth and power to stop, but he refused. Despite their full military and economic effort to destroy him, his movement only grew stronger. This growth cannot be attributed to human means because he lacked wealth, armies, and political support. Instead, it came from divine aid. A sign of this is that he was given victory through being feared from afar, a supernatural effect.

Key Terms
ضعف
قهار
معونة إلهية
نصر بالرعب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet had no followers or support at all initially.
Correction: The passage says 'few helpers', not none. He had some followers, but not enough to explain the eventual success through human means.

Checkpoint
According to the third proof, what explains the spread of Islam despite the Prophet's weakness?
A) He acquired wealth from trade
B) He formed alliances with powerful tribes
C) Divine assistance and heavenly support
D) The Meccans were not serious in opposing him

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's success against all odds is a clear sign of divine support.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there an area in your life where you feel weak, outnumbered, or without resources? Will you still stand for the truth like the Prophet did, refusing to compromise even when pressure mounts? What is one thing you will do today to act on that conviction?
?
You often rely on your own plans, wealth, or connections to succeed. But this lesson shows that the Prophet's triumph came through divine aid, not human means. Are you willing to let go of your reliance on your own strength and truly depend on God for success? What would that look like in your current biggest challenge?
?
The Prophet's own relatives opposed him fiercely. Whose approval are you afraid to lose? Are you holding back from full obedience to God because of fear of family, friends, or society? Name one relationship where you need to prioritize God's pleasure over human approval, and commit to a specific step to correct it.

Fourth Proof: The Prophet's Unwavering Perseverance
Fourth proof: the Prophet's unwavering perseverance through immense suffering beyond human capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's extraordinary endurance of hardships and rejection of worldly temptations serves as a proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unmatched patience proves his mission is from Allah.

The fourth proof presented by Imam al-Nasafi focuses on the Prophet's conduct during his mission. Despite immense suffering, he never wavered. He even rejected offers of wealth and power. This steadfastness, far beyond human capacity, indicates that his call was supported by divine will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key terms: مشاق (hardships), وتيرة واحدة (consistent course), صبر (patience).
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the proof structure
The passage presents a premise: the Prophet endured unbearable hardships consistently, rejected worldly temptations, and remained patient. The conclusion is that such behavior is a miracle proving prophethood.
This is a form of argument from unusual character.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this is considered a proof. If the Prophet sought personal gain, he would have accepted wealth. His refusal shows sincerity.
4
Answer the checkpoint
The checkpoint tests your understanding of the main point: rejection of worldly gain proves divine motive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرابع أنه عليه السلام تحمل في إظهار دعوته المشاق التي لا خفاء بمكانها، والمتاعب التي ليست في الجملة البشرية احتمالها فدام في ذلك كله على وتيرة واحدة لا يسأم عن شأنه ولا يمل عن دعوته، وعرضت عليه المطامع من الثروة والرياسة ليترك دعوته فلم يجبهم إلى ذلك بل قال: وَمَا أَسْأَلُكُمْ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَجْرٍ وصبر على تلك المشاقات مترددا في البؤس والفاقة منصرفا في الضراء واللداء
And the fourth: that he, peace be upon him, bore in manifesting his call the hardships whose position is no secret, and the troubles that are not within the capacity of human nature to bear. He continued in all of that on one consistent course, not tiring of his matter nor getting bored with his call. And temptations of wealth and leadership were presented to him to abandon his call, but he did not respond to them; rather he said: 'And I do not ask you for any reward for it.' And he patiently endured those hardships, persisting in misery and poverty, turning away in adversity and distress.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof: the Prophet endured extreme hardships for the sake of his mission, far beyond normal human endurance. He never wavered or grew weary, despite continuous suffering. He was offered great worldly benefits—wealth and power—to stop, but he refused, saying he only seeks reward from God. His steadfastness in poverty and distress, without any personal gain, indicates that his motivation was purely divine. Such consistent perseverance, free from material desires, is evidence that his call is true and supported by God.

Correction: The passage explicitly states that he rejected offers of wealth and leadership, showing his motives were purely for God's sake.

A) He already had enough wealth
B) He was not motivated by worldly gain
C) He was afraid of his enemies
D) He wanted more power later

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unwavering patience and rejection of worldly gain demonstrate that his mission was divinely ordained.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet endured troubles 'not within human capacity' without tiring. What troubles have you given up on because they were too hard? Will you commit to persevere for Allah's sake starting today?
?
You are offered worldly gain to abandon a religious duty. Can you say with the Prophet, 'I ask no reward'? Examine your intentions: are you serving Allah or your own desires? Repent and realign.
