The Establisher of the Sunnah in the Psalms
Interpretation of a Psalm verse as a prophecy about Muhammad clarifying Jesus' humanity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Psalm prophecy about the 'establisher of the Sunnah' and how it corrects the misconception about Jesus' divinity.

Core Idea
David prayed for a prophet who would teach people that Jesus is human.

The author cites another Psalm verse where David prays for a 'establisher of the Sunnah' so that people may know that he (the Messiah) is human. He interprets this as a prophecy that Muhammad would come to clarify the true humanity of Jesus, countering those who would later deify him.

Guided Path
1
Read the Psalm quote
Read the short quote: David asks God to send the 'establisher of the Sunnah' so that people may know he is human.
2
Understand the interpretation linking to Muhammad and Jesus
The author explains that 'he' refers to Jesus, and the one who makes people know Jesus is human is Muhammad.
3
Reflect on the purpose: to refute claims of divinity
David foresaw that some would claim divinity for Jesus, so he prayed for a prophet to correct this.

Do you not see that if someone says to another: Bring me a man from the brothers of Banu Bakr bin Wa'il, he would have to bring him a man from Banu Taghlib, not a man from Banu Bakr. And among them is what is mentioned in the Psalms: 'Gird your sword, O mighty one, for your law and your statutes are accompanied by the majesty of your right hand, and your arrows are sharpened, and nations fall under you.' And the one who girded the sword among the prophets is only our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, and he is the one under whom nations fell, and his laws were accompanied by majesty. And among them is what David said in the Psalms: 'O God, send the establisher of the Sunnah so that people may know that he is human,' and this is news about the Messiah and about Muhammad, peace be upon them both; he intended: send Muhammad so that people may know that Jesus is human. Thus David knew that a people would claim for the Messiah what they claimed. And among them are many expressions in the Gospel by the name 'Faraqlit' (Paraclete), such as that the Paraclete is the Spirit of Truth whom He sends in my name, He will teach you everything. The scholars have mentioned in their books these expressions and many things from the books of the earlier prophets, peace be upon them, containing mention of him, and mention of his companions, and mention of Mecca, the Kaaba, the sanctuary, the stone, and other things. The people of the two Books do not deny the establishment of that, but they distort words from their places and interpret all of that with unnatural, corrupt interpretations to other than what is intended.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage collects scriptural prophecies from the Torah, Psalms, and Gospel that foretell the coming of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The author begins with a verse from the Torah describing God's appearance at Sinai, Seir, and Paran, interpreting Paran as Mecca and thus indicating the revelation of the Qur'an in Mecca. He then cites the prophecy in Deuteronomy of a prophet from the brothers of Israel, arguing that 'brothers' means the Ishmaelites, not Israelites, and that only Muhammad fits the description of a law-giving prophet like Moses. Logical analogies are given to support this interpretation. Next, he quotes Psalm verses about girding a sword and peoples falling under him, applied to Muhammad as the warrior prophet. Another Psalm verse about 'the establisher of the Sunnah' is interpreted to mean that people will learn from Muhammad that Jesus was human, countering later Christian claims of divinity. Finally, he references Gospel mentions of the Paraclete, identified as Muhammad. The passage concludes by noting that Jews and Christians do not deny these texts but distort their meanings.

السنة
المسيح

Misconception: Christians believe Jesus is divine.
Correction: The author shows that a Psalm prophecy anticipates a prophet who will teach that Jesus is human.

D) To build the temple

Key Takeaway
David's prayer for the 'establisher of the Sunnah' is a prophecy that Muhammad would affirm Jesus' humanity.

?

The Paraclete Prophecy in the Gospel
Identifying the Paraclete as Muhammad from Gospel passages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Gospel's mention of the Paraclete (Faraqlit) is a prophecy about Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
The Paraclete promised by Jesus is Muhammad, the Spirit of Truth.

The author concludes his list of prophecies with references from the Gospel to the 'Faraqlit' (Paraclete) – the Spirit of Truth whom Jesus says will be sent by the Father and will teach all things. The author asserts that this is a prophecy of Muhammad's coming, and that scholars have documented many such references. He ends by noting that Jews and Christians do not deny these texts but distort their meanings.

Guided Path
1

Read the passage about the Paraclete and note that the author identifies it with Muhammad.
2
Understand the claim that the Paraclete is Muhammad
The author says the Paraclete is the 'Spirit of Truth' who will teach all things, sent in Jesus' name. He sees this as Muhammad.
3
Note the concluding remark about distortion
The author states that Jews and Christians do not deny these texts but corrupt their interpretations.

Rational Proof from the Prophet's Claim in Scriptures
Rational argument using the opponent's lack of refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that the Prophet Muhammad's claim to be foretold in previous scriptures is corroborated by the fact that his opponents did not refute it despite having the opportunity.

Core Idea
A bold claim left unrefuted is evidence of its truth.

The author presents a compelling rational argument that cuts through lengthy debates. Instead of enumerating scriptural proofs, he focuses on a simple fact: the Prophet claimed to be mentioned in the Torah and Gospel, and his opponents—who had every incentive to disprove him—remained silent. This lesson unpacks that argument and its logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the author's concise style and the Quranic verses he cites.
Pay attention to the rhetorical question at the end.
2
Identify the Prophet's claim
Find where the author states that Muhammad claimed to be mentioned in earlier scriptures. Note the Quranic verses that support this claim.
The verses are from the Quran, not from the Torah/Gospel directly.
3
Understand the rational argument
The author argues that if the claim were false, the opponents would have easily refuted it. Why did they not? Reflect on this pragmatic reasoning.
Consider why the opponents' silence is significant.
4
Consider the implications
How does this argument strengthen the case for prophethood? It uses the opponent's own lack of refutation as proof.
This is a unique approach compared to direct scriptural evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ذكر ذلك أئمة أهل الكلام، وأبطلوا تأويلاتهم الفاسدة، وأعرضت عن ذكر ذلك مخافة الإطالة واكتفيت من ذلك كله بمعقول لا اعتراض للخصوم عليه ولا انفصال لهم عنه وهو أن محمدًا ادعى أنه مذكور في كتبهم وأنه مبشر به على لسان المسيح على ما ذكر الله تعالى في كتابه بقوله: ( الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُمِّيَّ الَّذِي يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوبًا عِندَهُمْ فِي التَّوْرَاةِ وَالْإِنْجِيلِ ) وقال تعالى خبرًا عن عيسى عليه السلام: إِنِّي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ إِلَيْكُم مُّصَدِّقًا لِمَا بَيْنَ يَدَيَّ مِنَ التَّوْرَاةِ وَمُبَشِّرًا بِرَسُولٍ يَأْتِي مِنْ بَعْدِي اسْمُهُ أَحْمَدُ ( وقال تعالى: يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ لِمَ تَكْفُرُونَ بِآيَاتِ اللَّهِ وَأَنْتُمْ تَشْهَدُونَ * يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ لِمَ تَلْبِسُونَ الْحَقَّ بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتَكْتُمُونَ الْحَقَّ وَأَنْتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ ) . وقال : الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَاهُمُ الْكِتَابَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ ) وفي آيات كثيرة يطول تعدادها وقد كان يدعوهم إلى اتباعه وتصديقه، وقد أقام على صحة دعواه من الدلالات الكافية التي قطعت أعذار الجاحدين، فكيف كان يحتج عليهم بباطل ويحيل ذلك إلى ما عندهم وفي أيديهم ويقول علامة ثبوتي ودليل صدقي أنكم تجدونني مكتوبًا وهو يعلم أنهم لا يجدونه، ويعلم أن ذلك مما يزيدهم نفارًا وعما يدعوهم إليه بعدًا، وقد كان غنيًا عن ذلك بما أقام من الدلالات، أيفعل ذلك عاقل؟
And the imams of the theologians have mentioned that, and they invalidated their corrupt interpretations. I have refrained from mentioning that for fear of prolixity, and I suffice with a rational argument against which the opponents have no objection and from which they have no escape. And it is that Muhammad claimed that he is mentioned in their books and that he is given glad tidings of by the tongue of the Messiah, as God Almighty mentioned in His book saying: "Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered Prophet, whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel." And God Almighty said, reporting from Jesus, peace be upon him: "I am the messenger of God to you, confirming what was before me of the Torah, and giving glad tidings of a messenger who will come after me, whose name is Ahmad." And God Almighty said: "O People of the Book, why do you disbelieve in the verses of God while you bear witness? O People of the Book, why do you clothe the truth with falsehood and conceal the truth while you know?" And He said: "Those to whom We gave the Book recognize him as they recognize their sons." And there are many verses whose enumeration would be lengthy. And he (Muhammad) used to call them to follow him and believe him, and he established for the correctness of his claim sufficient proofs that cut off the excuses of the deniers. So how could he argue against them with falsehood and refer that to what is with them and in their hands, saying: "The sign of my establishment and the proof of my truthfulness is that you find me written (in your books)" while he knows that they do not find him, and he knows that that would increase their aversion and distance from what he calls them to? And he was independent of that by the proofs he established. Would a rational person do that?
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents a rational argument for the truth of the Prophet Muhammad's claim to be foretold in earlier scriptures. The author begins by noting that earlier scholars have refuted the distorted interpretations of Jews and Christians, but he avoids lengthy discussion and instead offers a concise rational proof that is irrefutable. The argument is: Muhammad claimed openly that he is mentioned in the Torah and Gospel, and that Jesus himself gave glad tidings of him (as per Quranic verses). He called the People of the Book to witness this and to follow him. He supported his prophethood with many clear proofs. If his claim to be written in their scriptures were false, he would be staking his credibility on something easily falsifiable. Yet his opponents did not produce evidence to refute his claim; rather, they remained silent or resorted to distortions. A rational person would not make such a claim if it were false, especially since he had other independent proofs. Therefore, his claim must be true.

Key Terms
معقول
دلالات
تأويلات
الخصوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The rational argument is circular because it assumes the Prophet's claim is true to conclude it is true.
Correction: It is not circular; it is a pragmatic proof based on the opponent's lack of refutation. If the claim were false, the opponents would have had every reason to disprove it, but they did not. Their silence is evidence of the claim's truth.

Checkpoint
What is the core rational argument the author presents?
A) The Prophet performed miracles that prove his truthfulness.
B) The Prophet claimed to be in previous scriptures, and if false, his opponents would have refuted him easily, but they did not.
C) The Prophet was illiterate, so he could not have fabricated the prophecies.
D) The Prophet's moral character proves his truthfulness.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's claim to be in earlier scriptures is validated by the fact that his opponents, who would have refuted him if false, did not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a claim about Islam that is easily verifiable, do you seek to verify it, or do you let your preconceptions silence it? How would the rational argument used here apply to your own life?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) risked public refutation by making a claim that could be easily checked. Do you have the same courage in your own faith to put your beliefs to the test, or do you avoid examining them for fear of being wrong?
?
If you were among the People of the Book at that time, would you have been among those who concealed the truth? What in your heart today prevents you from fully accepting the truth when it is clear?

The Paraclete Foretold in the Gospel
Imam Nasafi presents the Gospel's Farqalit prophecy and the distortion by the People of the Book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Gospel's mention of the Paraclete is used as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood, and how the People of the Book distort these texts.

Core Idea
The Gospel’s mention of a Paraclete points to Muhammad, though distorted by later interpreters.

Imam al-Nasafi begins by pointing to specific references in the Gospel to a figure called the Paraclete. These references, along with many others in earlier scriptures, are consistent with the description of the Prophet Muhammad. However, the People of the Book do not deny the existence of such passages; rather, they distort their meaning. In this lesson, we examine these scriptural prophecies and the response of early Muslim scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the Farqalit passage
Carefully read the Arabic passage where Imam Nasafi mentions the Farqalit in the Gospel and the scholars' citations.
Notice that the author states the People of the Book do not deny these texts, only distort them.
2
Understand the distortion
Reflect on the fact that the People of the Book twist the interpretations of these prophecies. Why would they do that?
The author says their interpretations are 'repugnant and corrupt'.
3
Note the author's approach
Imam Nasafi refrains from lengthy discussion of these distortions and instead moves to a rational argument. This sets the stage for the next lesson.
He says he will suffice with a 'rational argument' that the opponents cannot refute.

سيدعون للمسيح ما ادعوا. ومنها ألفاظ كثيرة في الإنجيل باسم فارقليط من ذلك أن الفارقليط روح الحق الذي يرسله أي باسمي هو يعلمك كل شيء. ذكر العلماء بكتبهم هذه الألفاظ وأشياء كثيرة من كتب الأنبياء المتقدمين عليهم السلام فيها ذكره وذكر أصحابه وذكر مكة والكعبة والحرم والحجر وغير ذلك. لا ينكر أهل الكتابين ثبوت ذلك غير أنهم يحرفون الكلم من مواضعه ويصرفون ذلك كله بتأويلات مستكرهة فاسدة إلى غير ما هو المراد، وقد ذكر ذلك أئمة أهل الكلام، وأبطلوا تأويلاتهم الفاسدة، وأعرضت عن ذكر ذلك مخافة الإطالة واكتفيت من ذلك كله بمعقول لا اعتراض للخصوم عليه ولا انفصال لهم عنه وهو أن محمدًا ادعى أنه مذكور في كتبهم وأنه مبشر به على لسان المسيح على ما ذكر الله تعالى في كتابه بقوله: (الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُمِّيَّ الَّذِي يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوبًا عِندَهُمْ فِي التَّوْرَاةِ وَالْإِنجِيلِ)، وقال تعالى خبرًا عن عيسى عليه السلام: إِنِّي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ إِلَيْكُم مُّصَدِّقًا لِّمَا بَيْنَ يَدَيَّ مِنَ التَّوْرَاةِ وَمُبَشِّرًا بِرَسُولٍ يَأْتِي مِن بَعْدِي اسْمُهُ أَحْمَدُ، وقال تعالى: ﴿ يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ لِمَ تَكْفُرُونَ بِآيَاتِ اللَّهِ وَأَنتُمْ تَشْهَدُونَ * يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ لِمَ تَلْبِسُونَ الْحَقَّ بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتَكْتُمُونَ الْحَقَّ وَأَنتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾، وقال: الَّذِينَ آتَيْنَاهُمُ الْكِتَابَ يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُمْ، وفي آيات كثيرة يطول تعدادها. وقد كان يدعوهم إلى اتباعه وتصديقه، وقد أقام على صحة دعواه من الدلالات الكافية التي قطعت أعذار الجاحدين، فكيف كان يحتج عليهم بباطل ويحيل ذلك إلى ما عندهم وفي أيديهم ويقول علامة ثبوتي ودليل صدقي أنكم تجدونني مكتوبًا وهو يعلم أنهم لا يجدونه، ويعلم أن ذلك مما يزيدهم نفارًا وعما يدعوهم إليه بعدًا، وقد كان غنيًا عن ذلك بما أقام من الدلالات، أيفعل ذلك مجنون؟ فضلاً عمن طبقت حكمته الأرض، وفاق على زعم الخصوم جميع أهل الأرض دهاء وذكاء وأبذ على كافة الفصحاء في البلاغة والفصاحة، ولم أسلم والحال كما زعموا من كذبه في دعواه وجود ذكره والبشارة به في الكتب المتقدمة - من أسلم من علمائهم وأحبارهم كعبد الله بن سلام وتميم الداري وكعب وهم عالمون بكذبه فيما يدعي؟ هذا مما لا يكون، فكان هذا من أوضح الدلائل على ثبوت ذكره، والبشارة به في الكتب المتقدمة، وروي أحاديث كثيرة عن العلماء بالكتب المتقدمة في وجه ذكره فيها أعرضنا عن ذلك مخافة التطويل
They will claim for the Messiah what they claim. And among these are many words in the Gospel under the name 'Farqalit' (Paraclete), such as: 'The Farqalit is the Spirit of Truth whom He sends, that is, in My name He will teach you everything.' The scholars have mentioned in their books these words and many things from the books of the earlier prophets (peace be upon them) including mention of him, his companions, Mecca, the Ka'ba, the sanctuary, the stone, and other things. The People of the Two Books do not deny the existence of that, except that they distort the words from their places and misinterpret all of that with repugnant and corrupt interpretations to other than what is intended. The imams of the People of Kalam have mentioned that and refuted their corrupt interpretations. I have refrained from mentioning that for fear of prolixity and suffice with a rational argument that the opponents have no objection to and no escape from, and that is that Muhammad claimed that he is mentioned in their scriptures and that he was given glad tidings through the tongue of the Messiah, as Allah Almighty said in His Book: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered Prophet, whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel...' And He Almighty said as a report from Jesus (peace be upon him): 'I am the messenger of Allah to you, confirming what came before me of the Torah and giving glad tidings of a messenger who will come after me, whose name is Ahmad.' And He Almighty said: 'O People of the Book, why do you disbelieve in the verses of Allah while you bear witness? O People of the Book, why do you mix truth with falsehood and conceal the truth while you know?' And He said: 'Those to whom We gave the Book recognize him as they recognize their own sons.' And there are many verses whose enumeration would be lengthy. And he was calling them to follow and believe him, and he had established the soundness of his claim with sufficient proofs that cut off the excuses of the deniers. How then could he argue with falsehood and refer them to what is in their hands and say: 'The sign of my establishment and the proof of my truthfulness is that you find me written' while he knows that they do not find him written, and he knows that that would increase their aversion and distance from what he calls them to? He was needless of that by what he established of proofs. Would a madman do that? Far be it from one whose wisdom covered the earth, and who, according to the claim of the opponents, surpassed all the people of the earth in cunning and intelligence and excelled all the eloquent in eloquence. And did not, while the situation is as they claim (that he was lying in his claim that he is mentioned and given glad tidings in the previous scriptures), some of their scholars and rabbis like 'Abdullah ibn Salam, Tamim al-Dari, and Ka'b accept Islam, while they know he is lying in what he claims? That is impossible. So this is among the clearest proofs of the establishment of his mention and the glad tidings of him in the previous scriptures. And many hadiths have been narrated from the scholars of the previous scriptures regarding the manner of his mention in them, which I have omitted for fear of making it long.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood from the foretelling in previous scriptures and the conversion of learned Jews and Christians. The author begins by mentioning that the Gospel contains references to the 'Farqalit' (Paraclete) and that scholars have collected many such passages. He then notes that the People of the Book do not deny that these prophecies exist but they distort them. To avoid lengthy discussion, the author presents a rational argument (معقول) that cannot be refuted: Muhammad claimed to be mentioned in their scriptures. He then poses a rhetorical question: if this claim were false, why would learned Jewish and Christian scholars like 'Abdullah ibn Salam, Tamim al-Dari, and Ka'b convert to Islam, knowing that the Prophet was lying? This is impossible. Therefore, this is a clear proof that the Prophet was indeed foretold in the previous scriptures. The author omits lengthy hadith narrations on this topic to keep the discussion concise.

Key Terms
الفارقليط
تحريف
بشارة
الكتب المتقدمة
أهل الكتاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that the People of the Book deny the existence of prophecies about Muhammad in their scriptures.
Correction: The passage clarifies that they do not deny the existence of such texts; they only distort their interpretation. Thus, the proof from previous scriptures is not merely textual but also rational.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Nasafi, what do the People of the Book do with the prophecies about Muhammad in their scriptures?
A) They deny that they exist
B) They distort the words and interpret them wrongly
C) They accept them as genuine prophecies
D) They ignore them completely

Key Takeaway
The Gospel contains clear prophecies about Muhammad, but they are distorted; Muslim scholars have refuted these distortions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the People of the Book distort clear words to avoid acknowledging the truth, what subtle forms of self-deception do you use to avoid acting on what you already know is true about Islam?
?
The prophecy of the Paraclete is a clear sign for those who seek the truth. What fear holds you back from presenting this evidence to someone who questions Muhammad's prophethood, even when the proof is in their own scripture?
?
If you were among the People of the Book and read this prophecy, would you have accepted it or twisted it to maintain your current beliefs? What does your answer reveal about your own attachment to comfort over truth?

The Conversion of Learned Scholars as a Rational Proof
Imam Nasafi presents a rational proof from the acceptance of Islam by learned scholars of the People of the Book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the conversion of learned Jewish and Christian scholars serves as a decisive rational argument for the truth of Muhammad's claim to be foretold in previous scriptures.

Core Idea
If Muhammad were lying about being foretold, learned scholars would not have embraced Islam.

After referencing scriptural prophecies, Imam al-Nasafi presents a rational argument that is independent of textual interpretation. He argues that the fact that knowledgeable Jewish and Christian scholars converted to Islam, despite their expertise in the scriptures, proves that Muhammad was indeed mentioned in those scriptures. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the rational argument
Read the passage starting from 'وأعرضت' to the end. Notice how the author builds his case: he states Muhammad's claim, cites Quranic verses, and then poses a rhetorical question.
The argument is called 'معقول' (rational) and is meant to be irrefutable.
2
Understand the rhetorical question
The author asks: would a madman claim something that would increase people's aversion? Muhammad was known for wisdom and intelligence, so he would not make a false claim that would push people away.
This shows the reasonableness of Muhammad's claim.
3
Reflect on the conversion of scholars
The author mentions 'Abdullah ibn Salam, Tamim al-Dari, and Ka'b as examples of knowledgeable scholars who accepted Islam despite knowing the scriptures.
If Muhammad were lying, these experts would have known and not converted.
4
Conclude the proof
Thus, the fact that they converted is among the clearest proofs that Muhammad was indeed foretold in the previous scriptures.
This rational argument bypasses the need for lengthy discussion of distortions.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Prophecies of the Prophet in Persian and Yemeni Traditions
Imam Nasafi presents evidence of the Prophet's mention in Persian and Yemeni prophecies and histories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how non-Islamic traditions (Persian and Yemeni) also foretold the coming of the Prophet Muhammad, adding to the cumulative proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
Even pre-Islamic Persian and Yemeni records contain prophecies about the Prophet Muhammad.

This passage from Imam Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla expands the evidence for prophethood beyond the familiar scriptural proofs. It shows that the Prophet's coming was foretold not only in the Torah and Gospel but also in the historical records and dreams of the Persians and in the poetry of the Yemeni king Tubba'. By examining these traditions, we see how God prepared different nations to recognize His final messenger.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and its translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the evidence presented.
2
Identify the two sources of foretelling
Notice that the passage first mentions Persian reports and dreams, then moves to Yemeni kings, specifically Tubba' and Sayf ibn Dhi Yazan.
3
Examine Tubba's poem
Read the poem attributed to Tubba' carefully. What does it say about Ahmad? What does Tubba' wish for?
The poem is a direct testimony to the Prophet's status before his birth.
4
Consider the story of Sayf ibn Dhi Yazan
The author references a well-known story without recounting it. Reflect on why this story is relevant and what it indicates about prior knowledge of the Prophet.
This story adds to the cumulative evidence from Yemeni tradition.
5
Synthesize the cumulative proof
Think about how these non-scriptural sources strengthen the overall argument for the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.
These sources show that the prophecy was not limited to one community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا وجد ذكره في أخبار الفرس ومنامات لهم أنذروا فيها بزوال ملكهم على يده، وكانوا يخافون ذلك وكذا في سير ملوك اليمن وغيرهم حتى حكوا في حكاية فيها طول عن تبع بن حسان بن تبع أنه قال في النبي عليه السلام: شهدت على أحمد أنه رسول من الله باري النسم، فلو مد عمري إلى عمره لكنت وزيرًا له وابن عم. وقصة سيف بن ذي يزن مع عبد المطلب مشهورة لا خفاء بها على من له أدنى علم بالتواريخ وسير الملوك، والله الهادي.
Likewise, his mention was found in the reports of the Persians and their dreams in which they were warned of the end of their kingdom at his hands, and they were afraid of that. Similarly, in the histories of the kings of Yemen and others, they narrated a lengthy story about Tubba' ibn Hassan ibn Tubba' that he said concerning the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'I bear witness that Ahmad is a messenger from God, the Creator of souls; if my life were extended to his lifetime, I would be his minister and cousin.' And the story of Sayf ibn Dhi Yazan with 'Abd al-Muttalib is well-known, not hidden from anyone with the slightest knowledge of histories and the lives of kings. And God is the Guide.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents additional non-scriptural evidence for the foretelling of the Prophet Muhammad. The author first cites Persian traditions: reports and dreams among the Persians warned them that their kingdom would end at the hands of the Prophet, and they feared that. He then turns to the Yemeni royal tradition, quoting a poem attributed to Tubba' (a Himyarite king) in which he declares: 'I bear witness that Ahmad is a messenger from God, the Creator of souls; if my life were extended to his lifetime, I would be his minister and cousin.' The author also references the well-known story of Sayf ibn Dhi Yazan and 'Abd al-Muttalib, which is familiar to anyone with knowledge of history. He concludes with 'And God is the Guide' (والله الهادي). This adds to the cumulative case for prophethood from various cultural traditions beyond the scriptural ones.

أخبار الفرس
ملوك اليمن
تبع
باري النسم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophethood proofs rely solely on Islamic sources.
Correction: The author shows that non-Islamic traditions also contain confirmations of the Prophet's coming.

Checkpoint

Non-Islamic traditions from Persia and Yemen also contained prophecies and accounts that pointed to the coming of the Prophet Muhammad.

Proof from Foretelling in Previous Scriptures
Al-Nasafi argues that the Prophet's mention in earlier scriptures is a clear proof of his prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses the conversion of Jewish and Christian scholars, along with pre-Islamic traditions, as a proof of the Prophet's prophethood.

Core Idea
The conversion of scripture experts proves the foretelling was genuine.

Al-Nasafi presents a multifaceted proof for the Prophet's prophethood: the fact that learned Jewish and Christian scholars, who knew their scriptures intimately, converted to Islam even while the opponents accused the Prophet of lying. This, he argues, would be impossible if the prophecies were false. He then adds supporting evidence from Persian and Yemenite traditions that also mention the coming Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rhetorical question
Read the opening argument carefully: Al-Nasafi asks how it could be that scripture scholars like Abdullah ibn Salam submitted if they knew the Prophet was lying about his mention in their books. This is a logical challenge to the opponents.
The phrase 'This is something that cannot happen' is the punchline.
2
Grasp the logical force
The argument is that the conversion of experts who knew the scriptures demonstrates that the prophecies were indeed present. If they were false, such experts would not have converted.
This is not about all Jews and Christians, but about the learned.
3
Consider the extra-scriptural evidence
Al-Nasafi cites Persian dreams warning of the loss of their kingdom, and Yemenite traditions including Tubba's poem and the story of Sayf ibn Dhi Yazan. These are independent confirmations.
These traditions predate Islam and show anticipation of the Prophet.
4
Reflect on the cumulative case
The combination of scriptural and non-scriptural sources builds a strong case that the Prophet's coming was foretold. Al-Nasafi presents this as an 'obvious proof'.
He concludes with 'And Allah is the Guide.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عمن طبقت حكمته الأرض، وفاق على زعم الخصوم جميع أهل الأرض دهاء وذكاء وأبذ على كافة الفصحاء في البلاغة والفصاحة، ولم أسلم والحال كما زعموا من كذبه في دعواه وجود ذكره والبشارة به في الكتب المتقدمة - من أسلم من علمائهم وأحبارهم كعبد الله بن سلام وتميم الداري وكعب وهم عالمون بكذبه فيما يدعي ؟ هذا مما لا يكون، فكان هذا من أوضح الدلائل على ثبوت ذكره، والبشارة به في الكتب المتقدمة، وروي أحاديث كثيرة عن العلماء بالكتب المتقدمة في وجه ذكره فيها أعرضنا عن ذلك مخافة التطويل، وكذا وجد ذكره في أخبار الفرس ومنامات لهم أنذروا فيها بزوال ملكهم على يده، وكانوا يخافون ذلك وكذا في سير ملوك اليمن وغيرهم حتى حكوا في حكاية فيها طول عن تبع بن حسان بن تبع أنه قال في النبي عليه السلام: شـهدت على أحمـ أحمــ ـد أنـ فلو مد عمري إلى عمره رسول من الله باري النسم لكنت وزيرًا له وابن عم وقصة سيف بن ذي يزن مع عبد المطلب مشهورة لا خفاء بها على من له أدنى علم بالتواريخ وسير الملوك، والله الهادي.
From Him whose wisdom covered the earth, and who surpassed, according to the claim of the opponents, all the people of the earth in cunning and intelligence, and surpassed all the eloquent in eloquence and rhetoric, and (yet) they did not submit while the situation was as they claimed from his lie in his claim, (a situation) which requires the existence of his mention and glad tidings of him in the previous books - (if) some of their scholars and rabbis like Abdullah ibn Salam, Tamim al-Dari, and Ka'b had submitted while they knew his lie in what he claims, (could) this (possibly) happen? This is something that cannot happen. So this was among the clearest proofs of the establishment of his mention and glad tidings of him in the previous books. And many hadiths were narrated from the scholars of the previous books regarding the manner of his mention in them, which we have refrained from (citing) for fear of length. Likewise, his mention was found in the reports of the Persians and in their dreams in which they were warned of the removal of their kingdom by his hand, and they used to fear that. Likewise, in the biographies of the kings of Yemen and others, until they narrated a lengthy story from Tubba' ibn Hassan ibn Tubba' that he said regarding the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'I testify concerning Ahmad that if my lifetime extended to his lifetime, (he would be) a messenger from Allah, the Creator of souls, then I would be a minister for him and a cousin.' And the story of Sayf ibn Dhi Yazan with Abd al-Muttalib is famous, not hidden from anyone who has even the slightest knowledge of histories and biographies of kings. And Allah is the Guide.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the Prophet Muhammad's prophethood based on his mention in previous scriptures and historical traditions. Al-Nasafi argues that given the hostility and denial of the opponents, it is implausible that people like Abdullah ibn Salam, Tamim al-Dari, and Ka'b would have submitted to him if they truly knew he was lying about being foretold in their scriptures. Their conversion despite knowing the Scriptures indicates that the prophecies were indeed there. This is presented as an obvious proof. He then mentions that there are many narrations about this, which he omits for brevity. Further evidence comes from Persian stories and dreams warning of the loss of their kingdom at his hands, and from Yemenite traditions, including the poem of Tubba' acknowledging Ahmad as a prophet. The well-known story of Sayf ibn Dhi Yazan and Abd al-Muttalib is cited as another witness. He concludes with 'And Allah is the Guide.'

الكتب المتقدمة
أحبار
دهاء
ذكاء

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument requires that all Jews and Christians recognized the Prophet's foretelling.
Correction: The argument specifically points to the conversion of learned scripture scholars, not the entire community. Their submission despite knowledge of the scriptures proves the prophecies were genuine.

Proof from Knowledge of Past Events
Al-Nasafi argues that the Prophet's accurate knowledge of past events, without learning, proves divine revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses the Prophet's knowledge of past events as evidence for divine revelation.

Core Idea
Perfect knowledge from an unlettered man proves revelation.

This lesson presents a key proof of prophethood from the Maturidi tradition. Al-Nasafi argues that the Prophet's accurate recounting of past events, which he could not have learned through normal means, demonstrates that his knowledge came directly from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Al-Nasafi builds his argument step by step.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the key conditions
Find the conditions Al-Nasafi lists: the Prophet's unlettered state, his isolation from scholars, and his perfect agreement with previous scriptures.
These conditions show the knowledge could not have been acquired normally.
3
Understand the conclusion
Al-Nasafi concludes that such knowledge is from the unseen and only possible through divine revelation. Notice how he ties the conclusion to the conditions.
The phrase 'من باب علم الغيب' marks the category.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
Ask yourself why this argument is considered 'clear'. Consider the alternative explanations and why they fail.
This argument is a classic proof in Maturidi theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما هو راجع إلى إخباره عن الكائنات الماضية الجزئية فيما تضمن الكتاب من أخبار أنبياء بني إسرائيل وغيرهم مما لم يكن علم شيء من ذلك عند أهل بلدته، وهو لم يختلف إلى أحد ممن له علم بذلك وأخبر على نحو ما علمه أحبار اليهود وعلماء النصارى من غير زيادة ولا نقصان وعلم ذلك من مثله من الأميين الذين لم يقرأوا الكتب المتقدمة ولا أخذوا ذلك من علمائهم وأحبارهم، من باب علم الغيب لا يعلم إلا بالله تعالى، فحيث علم هو مع ما بينا من حاله دل أنه علم بأخبار الله تعالى إياه، وهذا واضح بحمد الله.
And as for what pertains to his informing about past particular events, including what the Book contains of the stories of the prophets of the Children of Israel and others, concerning which there was no knowledge of anything of that among the people of his town, and he did not frequent anyone who had knowledge of that, and he informed in a manner matching what the Jewish rabbis and Christian scholars knew, without increase or decrease, and that is known from someone like him, from the unlettered who have not read the previous books nor taken that from their scholars and rabbis, (this) is from the category of knowledge of the unseen, not known except by Allah the Exalted. So since he knew it, along with what we have explained of his condition, it indicates that he knew it through Allah's informing him. And this is clear, praise be to Allah.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood based on the Prophet's knowledge of past events, specifically the detailed stories of previous prophets and nations as found in the Qur'an. Al-Nasafi notes that the people of Mecca had no such knowledge, and the Prophet never studied with anyone who knew these stories. Yet he reported them exactly as the Jewish and Christian scholars knew them, without any error. This, coming from an unlettered man, could only be from divine revelation. He concludes that this is clear evidence of his prophethood.

Key Terms

أميين
الكتب المتقدمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the argument is merely that the Prophet knew history, but the key is his unlettered state and his perfect agreement with previous scriptures without any teacher.
Correction: Al-Nasafi's argument relies on three conditions: the Prophet's unlettered state, his isolation from scholars, and the exact match of his knowledge with previous scriptures. This combination makes the knowledge miraculous and proves revelation.

Checkpoint

D) He learned from traveling merchants.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate knowledge of past events, despite being unlettered and isolated, proves that his knowledge came from divine revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

This proof shows that the Prophet's accuracy is a miracle. Does this reality humble you and increase your certainty in his message? If not, what is holding you back?

Proof from Predictions in the Qur'an
Al-Nasafi classifies and exemplifies Qur'anic predictions as proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses fulfilled predictions in the Qur'an as a proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
Fulfilled predictions in the Qur'an are a miracle proving the Prophet's truthfulness.

Al-Nasafi now presents a powerful proof of prophethood: predictions of future events that came true exactly. He classifies these predictions into two categories—those in the Qur'an and those in hadith—and then provides three clear examples from the Qur'an. This lesson will walk through the classification and examples to see how they constitute a miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation. Notice the structure: classification first, then examples.
The passage is dense with Qur'anic citations.
2
Identify the two types of predictions
Al-Nasafi states there are two types: those in the Book (Qur'an) and those in hadith. He only elaborates on the Qur'anic type here.
3
Examine the first two examples
Look at the verses about the defeat of the polytheists (Q54:45) and the promise of one of the two parties (Q8:7). Note how each was fulfilled exactly as predicted.
The 'sin' prefix in 'suyuhzamun' proves it is a future prediction, not a present report.
4
Study the third example and its implication
The verse about calling the Bedouins to fight a people of severe might (Q48:16) is linked to historical events. Al-Nasafi also notes it indicates the caliphate of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Ali.
This example also serves as a proof of the imamate, which he will discuss later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما هو راجع إلى إخباره عن الكائنات في المستقبل فنوعان: أحدهما: ما وجد في الكتاب. والآخر ما وجد في الخبر. فأما ما كان من ذلك في الكتاب فكقوله تعالى: سَهزَمُ الْجَمْعُ وَيُولُونَ الدُّبُرَ ) والسورة مكية يعني بذلك المشركين يوم بدر فكان كما أخبر، ولا شك أنه إخبار عما يكون في المستقبل بدلالة حرف السين الموضوعة لتمحض الاستقبال وقطع احتمال الحال التي وضعت لها الصيغة وقوله تعالى: وَإِذْ يَعِدُكُمُ اللَّهُ إِحْدَى الطَّائِفَتَينِ أَنَّهَا لَكُمْ ) وقد كانت لهم وهي العسكر لا العير، وقوله تعالى: ﴿ قُل لِّلْمُخَلَّفِينَ مِنَ الأعْرَابِ سَتَدْعَوْنَ إِلَى قَوْمٍ أُوْلِي بَأْسٍ شَدِيدٍ وقد دعوا لأن المراد من قوله "أولي بأس شديد عند بعضهم هم بنو حنيفة، وقد دعا إلى قتالهم أبو بكر الصديق الله، وعند بعضهم المراد من ذلك هم أهل فارس، وقد دعا إلى ذلك عمر بن الخطاب، وفي الآية دلالة على خلافة أبي بكر وعمر وعلي على ما نبين إذا انتهينا إلى إثبات الإمامة - إن شاء الله تعالى.
And as for what pertains to his informing about future events, there are two types: one: what is found in the Book. And the other: what is found in the hadith. As for what is from that in the Book, it is like His statement, the Exalted: 'The assembly will be defeated, and they will turn their backs' (al-Qamar 54:45), and the surah is Meccan, meaning by that the polytheists on the day of Badr, and it happened as he informed. There is no doubt that it is an informing about what will be in the future, indicated by the letter 'sin' which is placed for pure futurity and removing the possibility of the present tense for which the form was placed. And His statement, the Exalted: 'And when Allah promised you one of the two parties that it would be yours' (al-Anfal 8:7), and it was for them, and it is the army, not the caravan. And His statement, the Exalted: 'Say to those who remained behind of the Bedouins, "You will be called to a people of severe might"' (al-Fath 48:16), and they were called, because the meaning of 'people of severe might' according to some is the Banu Hanifa, and Abu Bakr al-Siddiq called to fighting them, and according to others the meaning is the people of Persia, and Umar ibn al-Khattab called to that. And in the verse there is an indication of the caliphate of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Ali, as we will explain when we reach the proof of the imamate, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood based on the Prophet's predictions of future events, specifically those found in the Qur'an. Al-Nasafi first classifies these predictions into two types: those in the Qur'an and those in hadith. He then gives three examples from the Qur'an. First, the verse 'The assembly will be defeated' was revealed in Mecca predicting the defeat of the polytheists at Badr, which happened exactly. He notes that the Arabic letter 'sin' indicates pure future tense, confirming it is a prediction. Second, the verse about Allah promising one of the two parties (the caravan or the army) to the Muslims, and it was the army that they got. Third, the verse calling the Bedouins to fight a people of severe might, which was fulfilled either by the wars against Banu Hanifa (under Abu Bakr) or against the Persians (under Umar). He adds that this verse also indicates the caliphate of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Ali, a point he will elaborate later. These fulfilled predictions are presented as clear proofs of prophethood.

الكتاب
الخبر
حرف السين
الاستقبال
دلالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any prediction coming true proves prophethood.
Correction: The argument relies on specific, detailed predictions about future events that came true exactly as stated, which is a miracle beyond human ability.

C) The verse is a command.
D) The verse mentions the day of Badr.

Key Takeaway
Fulfilled predictions in the Qur'an demonstrate that the Prophet's knowledge was from Allah, confirming his prophethood.

Quranic Predictions of Future Events
Al-Nasafi enumerates Quranic verses containing future predictions and notes their fulfillment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses specific Quranic verses that accurately predicted future events—such as the Roman victory, the conquest of Mecca, and the succession of the Companions—as evidence for the truth of prophethood.

Core Idea
Accurate future predictions in the Quran are a powerful proof that its message is from Allah.

Al-Nasafi presents a series of Quranic verses that foretold specific future events with precision. These predictions could not have been made by human guesswork. By examining these examples, we see a pattern of fulfilled prophecy that confirms the divine origin of the Quran and the truth of the Prophet Muhammad.

1

3

Think about why this would be impossible for a human to guarantee.

بكر إذ لا يجوز أن يكون المستخلف مقهورا. وكقوله تعالى في شأن اليهود قُلْ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ هَادُوا إِن زَعَمْتُمْ أَنَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَاءُ لِلَّهِ مِن دُونِ النَّاسِ إلى أن قال: وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُ أَبَدًا وكان كما أخبر، ولم يتمن أحد منهم الموت، وفي الآية دليل أنهم كانوا يعلمون صحة رسالته، وكانوا وجدوا ذكره في كتبهم حيث لم يتجاسروا على التمني علمًا منهم أنهم لو تمنوا لماتوا لولا ذلك لفعلوا إظهارًا لخلفه. وكقوله تعالى في اليهود: ضُرِبَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الذِّلَّةُ أَيْنَ مَا ثُقِفُوا إِلَّا بِحَبْلٍ مِّنَ اللَّهِ ومصداق هذا في اليهود بين في كل عصر ومصر؛ إذ لم ترفع لهم راية منذ يومئذ، ولا ثبت لهم سلطان، وكانت أمارة الذل والصغار والمسكنة عليهم بادية، وعلامة السخط واللعنة ظاهرة وإن كانوا يرجعون إلى ثروة من المال وكثرة من العدة والعتاد. وأما ما هو راجع إلى الإخبار عن الكائنات في المستقبل غير الكتاب فمنه قوله عليه السلام: زويت لي الأرض فأريت مشارقها ومغاربها وسيبلغ ملك أمتي ما زوى لي منها وكان كما أخبر إذ لم يرد بذلك جميع المشارق والمغارب، وإنما أراد ما ينطلق في عرف الناس عليه اسم المشرق والمغرب لانصراف مطلق الكلام إلى ما هو المستعمل في مخاطبة المتعارف في مفاوضاتهم. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعدي بن حاتم الطائي: كيف بك إذا خرجت الظعينة من أقصى قصور اليمن إلى قصور الحيرة لا تخاف إلا الله؟ قال عدي: قلت يا رسول الله، فكيف بطيئ ومقامها؟ قال: يكفيها الله طيئا. وهذا إخبار عن الأمر الذي يكون بعدهم لأنهم كانوا خائفين في حياته، فكان كما أخبر في زمن عمر فكانت المرأة تخرج من قبيلة طيئ باليمن وتجاوز البادية، ولا يعترض لها أحد
And like His saying, the Exalted: 'Alif, Lam, Meem. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and after their defeat they will be victorious.' And it was as He informed. And like His saying, the Exalted: 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and in themselves.' The intended meaning is something in the future by the indication of the letter 'sin', and He has shown them the signs indicating their origination and the existence of the Wise Maker for them in themselves and in the horizons, so the verse was not confined to that, and the intended meaning was what the people of interpretation said: that the signs in the horizons meant the conquest of Persia, and in themselves the conquest of Mecca, and it was as He informed. And like His saying, the Exalted, to His Messenger: 'Indeed, He who imposed upon you the Qur'an will bring you back to a place of return' meaning Mecca, and He returned him to it. And like His saying, the Exalted: 'He is the one who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to manifest it over all religion' and He manifested it. And like His saying, the Exalted: 'Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession in the land' the verse, and the intended meaning from that is the Companions, by the indication of His saying, the Exalted: 'And He will surely substitute for them, after their fear, security' and they were the fearful ones in early Islam and before the Hijra, and He granted them succession, and in the verse is evidence for the caliphate of Abu Bakr, since it is not permissible that the one given succession be subdued. And like His saying, the Exalted, concerning the Jews: 'Say, O you who are Jews, if you claim that you are allies of Allah, excluding the people' until He said: 'And they will never wish for it' and it was as He informed, and none of them wished for death, and in the verse is evidence that they knew the truth of his message, and they had found his mention in their books, where they did not dare to wish, knowing that if they wished they would die, otherwise they would have done so showing that His word is false. And like His saying, the Exalted, concerning the Jews: 'Humiliation is imposed upon them wherever they are found, except through a rope from Allah' and the fulfillment of this regarding the Jews is evident in every age and place, for no flag has been raised for them since that day, nor has any authority been established for them, and the mark of humiliation, lowliness, and misery is apparent on them, and the sign of wrath and curse is manifest, even if they possess wealth and abundant equipment and matériel. And as for what pertains to informing about future beings other than the Book, among it is his saying, peace be upon him: 'The earth was folded for me, so I was shown its easts and wests, and the dominion of my community will reach what was folded for me' and it was as he informed, for he did not mean by that all easts and wests, but rather he meant what, in common parlance, is called the east and west, because of the general expression being directed to what is customary in the speech of people in their conversations. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to Adi ibn Hatim al-Ta'i: 'How will you be when the litter-bearing camel goes out from the farthest castles of Yemen to the castles of Hira, fearing none but Allah?' Adi said: 'I said, O Messenger of Allah, what about Tayyi and its position?' He said: 'Allah suffices for it against Tayyi.' And this is an informing about a matter that would occur after them, because they were fearful in his lifetime, and it was as he informed in the time of Umar, for the woman would go out from the tribe of Tayyi in Yemen and cross the desert, and no one would intercept her.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This is a cumulative proof-by-example passage. Al-Nasafi presents a series of fulfilled predictions (إخبارات) from the Quran and hadith to demonstrate the truth of prophethood. Each example shows that the Prophet (or the Quran) foretold future events with precise accuracy, something impossible except by divine revelation. The passage follows a clear order: first Quranic predictions, then a hadith prediction. 

1. Quranic examples:
   - Romans' defeat and subsequent victory (Surah al-Rum): predicted soon after defeat, fulfilled later.
   - Signs in horizons and themselves (Surah Fussilat): the future tense indicates later fulfillment in conquests.
   - Return to Mecca (Surah al-Qasas): fulfilled by the conquest of Mecca.
   - Dominance of Islam (Surah al-Saff): fulfilled historically.
   - Succession and security for the Companions (Surah al-Nur): fulfilled, with implication for Abu Bakr's caliphate.
   - Jews' challenge to wish for death (Surah al-Jumu'ah): they never did, proving their knowledge of the Prophet's truth.
   - Humiliation upon Jews (Surah Al 'Imran): evident throughout history.

2. Hadith examples:
   - The earth folded for the Prophet: the Muslim empire spread to regions shown.
   - The safe journey of a woman from Yemen to Hira (hadith to Adi ibn Hatim): fulfilled in the time of Umar, indicating security.

Al-Nasafi uses each fulfillment as evidence (دليل) that the informant (Allah or the Prophet) was truthful. The passage underscores the principle that accurate predictions of future unseen matters (إخبار عن الكائنات المستقبلية) are a miracle and a sign of prophethood.

Key Terms
إخبار عن الكائنات
أمارة
استخلاف
أدنى الأرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These predictions could have been coincidental or guessed by a human.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows each prediction was specific and historically fulfilled precisely, which rules out coincidence.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, which Quranic prediction does he use to argue for Abu Bakr's caliphate?
A) The Romans will be victorious.
B) The promise of succession for the believers.
C) The return to Mecca.
D) The dominance of Islam.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's accurate predictions of future events are a clear sign of its divine origin and the truth of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
These predictions were fulfilled exactly as revealed. Does your level of certainty in the Quran match what this evidence demands? If not, what stands between you and full conviction?
?
Al-Nasafi uses these fulfilled predictions to prove that the Quran is from Allah. Have you personally verified this evidence in your own heart, or do you rely on blind acceptance? What would change in your life if you truly internalized this proof?
?
The promise of succession and security was given to the Companions. Are you living in a way that qualifies you for Allah's help and victory? What specific fear or insecurity are you holding onto that contradicts this divine promise?

Prophethood
intermediate

Predictions About the Jews and Prophetic Hadith Miracles
Al-Nasafi presents predictions about Jews and hadith prophecies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses the Jews' failure to wish for death and their perpetual humiliation, along with prophetic hadith about the Muslim community's expansion and safety, as evidence for prophethood.

Core Idea
Even the Jews' own inaction and historical state fulfill prophecies, proving Muhammad's truth.

Al-Nasafi continues his proof-by-example with two striking Quranic verses about the Jews: one challenging them to wish for death, which they never did, and another predicting their perpetual humiliation. Then he cites hadith predicting the expansion of Islamic rule and a woman's safe journey from Yemen to Hira. Each fulfillment corroborates the truth of the Prophet's message.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Jews
Read the Arabic and translation for the Quranic verses about the Jews.
Focus on the challenge to wish for death and the humiliation prophecy.
2
Understand the Jews' reaction
Al-Nasafi argues that the Jews did not wish for death because they knew Muhammad was true. Why would that be?
They had found his description in their scriptures.
3
Analyze the hadith examples
Read the hadith about the folded earth and the woman's safe journey. Both were fulfilled.
The hadith about Adi ibn Hatim is particularly striking.

وكقوله تعالى: ( الم ۚ غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ فِي أَدْنَى الْأَرْضِ وَهُم مِّن بَعْدِ غَلَبِهِمْ سَيَغْلِبُونَ ) وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى: ﴿ سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَاتِنَا فِي الْآفَاقِ وَفِي أَنفُسِهِمْ ﴾ والمراد منه معنى في المستقبل بدلالة حرف السين وقد أراهم الآيات الدالة على حدوثهم وثبوت الصانع الحكيم لهم في أنفسهم وفي الآفاق فلم تكن الآية منصرفة إلى ذلك، وكان المراد ما قال أهل التأويل أن المراد بالآيات في الآفاق فتح الفرس، وفي أنفسهم فتح مكة، وكان كما أخبر. وكقوله تعالى لرسوله: إِنَّ الَّذِي فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْآنَ لَرَادُّكَ إِلَىٰ مَعَادٍ أي مكة. وقد رد إليها. وكقوله تعالى: هُوَ الَّذِي أَرْسَلَ رَسُولَهُ بِالْهُدَىٰ وَدِينِ الْحَقِّ لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ كُلِّهِ وقد أظهره. وكقوله تعالى: وَعَدَ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ الآية والمراد من ذلك الصحابة بدلالة قوله تعالى: وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُم مِّن بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمْنًا وكانوا هم الخائفين في صدر الإسلام وقبل الهجرة وقد استخلفهم، وفي الآية دلالة على خلافة أبي بكر إذ لا يجوز أن يكون المستخلف مقهورا. وكقوله تعالى في شأن اليهود قُلْ يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ هَادُوا إِن زَعَمْتُمْ أَنَّكُمْ أَوْلِيَاءُ لِلَّهِ مِن دُونِ النَّاسِ إلى أن قال: وَلَا يَتَمَنَّوْنَهُ أَبَدًا وكان كما أخبر، ولم يتمن أحد منهم الموت، وفي الآية دليل أنهم كانوا يعلمون صحة رسالته، وكانوا وجدوا ذكره في كتبهم حيث لم يتجاسروا على التمني علمًا منهم أنهم لو تمنوا لماتوا لولا ذلك لفعلوا إظهارًا لخلفه. وكقوله تعالى في اليهود: ضُرِبَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الذِّلَّةُ أَيْنَ مَا ثُقِفُوا إِلَّا بِحَبْلٍ مِّنَ اللَّهِ ومصداق هذا في اليهود بين في كل عصر ومصر؛ إذ لم ترفع لهم راية منذ يومئذ، ولا ثبت And like His saying, the Exalted: 'Alif, Lam, Meem. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land, and after their defeat they will be victorious.' And it was as He informed. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Jews could have wished for death but chose not to, which is not miraculous.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Nasafi, why did the Jews not wish for death when challenged in the Quran?
A) They did not believe in the afterlife.
B) They knew that if they wished, they would die, proving Muhammad's prophethood.
C) They were afraid of the Roman authorities.
D) They had forgotten the challenge.

The fulfillment of predictions about the Jews and hadith about the community's expansion confirm the truth of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jews avoided wishing for death because they knew the truth of Muhammad's message and feared it would be proven. What truth about your own life are you avoiding facing because you fear it might demand change? Are you willing to let that fear keep you from the certainty that comes with embracing the truth?
?
The Prophet foretold a time when a woman could travel safely across a dangerous region without fear. That prophecy was fulfilled. What parts of your life today do you live in fear of, not trusting that Allah's promise of security is as real as that fulfilled prophecy? How can you begin to live in the confidence of that promise starting this week?
?
The fulfillment of these prophecies leaves no room for doubt that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. If you truly believed that every word he spoke about the unseen will come to pass, what would you change in your daily priorities and actions right now? Identify one specific habit you will adjust today to align with that certainty.

Prophethood

Prophetic Proofs from Predictive Miracles
Al-Nasafi enumerates prophetic predictions as proofs of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how predictive prophecies from the Quran and Hadith serve as proofs of prophethood, and see specific examples from the Prophet's lifetime.

Core Idea
Predictive miracles confirm prophethood because only Allah can unveil the future.

Al-Nasafi presents a powerful argument for the truthfulness of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) by listing several accurate predictions he made about future events. These predictions range from the humiliation of the Jews foretold in the Quran to specific predictions about individuals and historical events. Each one came true exactly as stated, demonstrating that the Prophet spoke from divine knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repeated phrase 'ومن ذلك' which introduces each new example.
2
Identify the Quranic prophecy
Find the first example from the Quran (the verse about the Jews) and note how Al-Nasafi explains its fulfillment in every age.
3
List the non-Quranic predictions
Go through each 'ومن ذلك' example and write down what was predicted and how it was fulfilled.
There are about eight examples; some are closely related.
4
Reflect on accuracy
Ask yourself: Could these predictions be mere coincidences? How does the fulfillment strengthen belief in prophethood?
The passage argues that only a true prophet can foretell the unseen with such precision.
5
Consider the overall argument
Synthesize: How do these examples together build a cumulative case for prophethood?
The more examples, the stronger the proof.

علمًا منهم أنهم لو تمنوا لماتوا لولا ذلك لفعلوا إظهارا لخلفه. وكقوله تعالى في اليهود: {ضُرِبَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الذِّلَّةُ أَيْنَ مَا ثُقِفُوا إِلَّا بِحَبْلٍ مِّنَ اللَّهِ} ومصداق هذا في اليهود بين في كل عصر ومصر؛ إذ لم ترفع لهم راية منذ يومئذ، ولا ثبت لهم سلطان، وكانت أمارة الذل والصغار والمسكنة عليهم بادية، وعلامة السخط واللعنة ظاهرة وإن كانوا يرجعون إلى ثروة من المال وكثرة من العدة والعتاد. وأما ما هو راجع إلى الإخبار عن الكائنات في المستقبل غير الكتاب فمنه قوله عليه السلام: "زُوِيَتْ لِيَ الْأَرْضُ فَأُرِيتُ مَشَارِقَهَا وَمَغَارِبَهَا، وَسَيَبْلُغُ مُلْكُ أُمَّتِي مَا زُوِيَ لِي مِنْهَا" وكان كما أخبر إذ لم يرد بذلك جميع المشارق والمغارب، وإنما أراد ما ينطلق في عرف الناس عليه اسم المشرق والمغرب لانصراف مطلق الكلام إلى ما هو المستعمل في مخاطبة المتعارف في مفاوضاتهم. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعدي بن حاتم الطائي: "كيف بك إذا خرجت الظعينة من أقصى قصور اليمن إلى قصور الحيرة لا تخاف إلا الله؟" قال عدي: قلت يا رسول الله، فكيف بطيئ ومقامها؟ قال: "يكفيها الله طيئ" (وهذا إخبار عن الأمر الذي يكون بعدهم لأنهم كانوا خائفين في حياته، فكان كما أخبر في زمن عمر فكانت المرأة تخرج من قبيلة طيئ باليمن وتجاوز البادية، ولا يعترض لها أحد بمكروه). ومن ذلك أنه نعى النجاشي وخبر أصحابه بموته وصلى عليه، فتتابعت الأخبار أنه مات في ذلك اليوم. ومن ذلك قوله لعمار: "تقتلك الفئة الباغية" فقتل يوم صفين مع علي. ومنها قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "أشقى الناس عاقر الناقة، والذي يخضب من هذا هذه" يعني الذي يضربك على رأسك فيخضب لحيتك من دم رأسك فضرب علي على رأسه حين قتل. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "إنك تقتل الناكثين والمارقين والقاسطين". ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام: "اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر" فأعلمنا بهذا أن الخليفة بعده أبو بكر وبعد أبي بكر عمر رضي الله عنهما. ومن ذلك قوله: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة ثم يؤتي الله الملك من يشاء" وكانت خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين ثلاثين سنة.
Knowing from them that if they wished for death they would die, otherwise they would have done it to show their defiance. And like His saying, the Exalted, regarding the Jews: 'Humiliation has been stamped upon them wherever they are found, except by a rope from Allah' and the verification of this among the Jews is clear in every age and region; for no banner has been raised for them since that day, nor has any authority been established for them, and the mark of humiliation, lowliness, and abasement upon them is evident, and the sign of wrath and curse is manifest, even if they possess wealth and abundant equipment and weaponry. As for what pertains to informtation about future beings other than the Book, from that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'The earth was folded for me, so I was shown its eastern and western parts, and the dominion of my community will reach what was folded for me of it.' And it was as he informed, for he did not intend by that all the easts and wests, but rather he intended what, in the customary usage of people, is called the east and the west, because absolute speech is directed to what is customary in addressing the conventional in their conversations. And from that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Adi ibn Hatim al-Ta'i: 'How will it be with you when a woman traveling in a litter sets out from the furthest forts of Yemen to the forts of al-Hirah, fearing none but Allah?' 'Adi said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, how about the banditry of Tayyi' and their encampments? He said: 'Allah will suffice her against Tayyi'' (And this is information about a matter that would occur after them, because they were afraid during his lifetime, and it happened as he informed in the time of 'Umar, as women would set out from the tribe of Tayyi' in Yemen and cross the desert, and no one would accost them with harm). And from that is that he announced the death of al-Najashi and informed his companions of his death and prayed over him, and the reports followed that he died on that day. And from that is his saying to 'Ammar: 'The rebellious faction will kill you' and he was killed on the day of Siffin with 'Ali. And from that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will dye this from this' meaning the one who will strike you on your head and dye your beard with the blood of your head, and 'Ali was struck on his head when he was killed. And from that is his saying, peace be upon him, to 'Ali: 'You will kill the oath-breakers, the apostates, and the deviators.' And from that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow the two after me, Abu Bakr and 'Umar' so he informed us by this that the caliph after him is Abu Bakr and after Abu Bakr is 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both. And from that is his saying: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years, then Allah gives the kingdom to whom He wills' and the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs was thirty years.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophethood through predictive miracles. Al-Nasafi presents two broad categories: prophecies from the Quran (the verse about the Jews) and prophecies from the Prophet (peace be upon him) about future events. He begins with the Quranic prophecy that humiliation will be upon the Jews wherever they are found, except through a covenant from Allah. Al-Nasafi notes that this is evidently fulfilled in every age: the Jews never raised a banner or established a lasting state, and the signs of humiliation and wrath are apparent despite their wealth and armaments. Then he turns to non-Quranic predictions. He lists several: (1) The earth was folded for him, and he saw its east and west; his community's dominion would reach those lands. This was fulfilled, but not literally every place—only what people customarily call 'east' and 'west'. (2) He told 'Adi ibn Hatim that a woman traveling alone from Yemen to al-Hirah would fear no one but Allah, and indeed during 'Umar's caliphate it happened, as the banditry of Tayyi' ceased. (3) He announced the death of the Negus on the day he died, and companions received confirmation. (4) He told 'Ammar that 'the rebellious faction would kill you', and 'Ammar was killed at Siffin fighting with 'Ali. (5) He told 'Ali that the most wretched person after the one who hamstrung the she-camel is the one who would strike his head and dye his beard, and 'Ali was struck on the head when he was killed. (6) He told 'Ali he would kill the oath-breakers, apostates, and deviators, which 'Ali did in his wars. (7) He said to follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar after him, informing that they would be caliphs. (8) He said the caliphate after him would be thirty years, which matched the reigns of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Each example shows that the Prophet's foreknowledge came true exactly, proving his truthfulness.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these predictions are mere coincidences or allegorical.
Correction: The passage insists they are literal fulfillments, proving prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which prophetic prediction concerned the duration of the caliphate after the Prophet's death?
A) It will last until the Day of Judgment
B) It will be thirty years
C) It will be a hundred years
D) It will be passed to the Umayyads

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate predictions about future events, including the duration of the caliphate, the death of the Negus, and specific events, constitute undeniable proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet foretold that a woman would travel safely from Yemen to Syria, and indeed it happened exactly. What fear or obstacle in your own life are you clinging to that Allah has already promised to remove? Why do you hesitate to trust His promise fully?
?
‘Adi ibn Hatim, a former Christian, doubted the Prophet’s claim until he saw the literal fulfillment of this prophecy. Is there any area of your faith where you are withholding full acceptance because you have not yet seen the outcome? What would it take for you to surrender that doubt today?
?
The Prophet told ‘Ali that the most wretched person would strike his head and dye his beard. That happened despite the seeming impossibility of killing a companion of such standing. Take a moment: if you knew that every word the Prophet spoke would come true, how would you change your relationship with his Sunnah right now?

Prophethood

Predictive Miracles: The Negus, Ammar, and Ali
Al-Nasafi enumerates four prophecies about individuals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's predictions about specific individuals demonstrate his prophethood.

Core Idea
Fulfilled prophecies prove divine knowledge.

Al-Nasafi begins his argument by citing concrete instances where the Prophet foretold events that later occurred exactly as reported. These examples serve as clear evidence that his knowledge came from Allah, not from human speculation.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of examples
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the repeated phrase 'wa min dhālika' introducing each prophecy.
Each example is a self-contained proof.
2
Identify the four prophecies
Find the four distinct predictions: Negus's death, Ammar's killing, Ali's head wound, and Ali's victory over three groups.
3
Reflect on their fulfillment
Consider that all these events happened exactly as foretold. This consistency is the evidential force.
The examples are chosen from well-known historical events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك أنه نعى النجاشي وخبَّر أصحابه بموته وصلى عليه، فتتابعت الأخبار أنه مات في ذلك اليوم. ومن ذلك قوله لعمار: "تقتلك الفئة الباغية" فقتل يوم صفين مع علي. ومنها قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "أشقى الناس عاقر الناقة، والذي يخضب من هذا هذه" يعني الذي يضربك على رأسك فيخضب لحيتك من دم رأسك فضرب علي على رأسه حين قتل. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعلي: "أنك تقتل الناكثين والمارقين والقاسطين." ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام: "اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر" فأعلمنا بهذا أن الخليفة بعده أبو بكر وبعد أبي بكر عمر رضي الله عنهما. ومن ذلك قوله: "الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة ثم يؤتي الله الملك من يشاء" وكانت خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين ثلاثين سنة. ومن ذلك حديث ليلة الإسراء وما أخبر من أخبار عير قريش، وكان كما أخبر. ومن ذلك أنه ضلت له عليه السلام ناقة فأقبل يسأل الناس عنها فقال المنافقون: هذا محمد يخبركم خبر السماء وهو لا يدري أين ناقته، فصعد المنبر وحمد الله وأثنى عليه، وحكى قولهم ثم قال: إني لا أعلم إلا ما أعلمني ربي وقد أخبرني أنها في وادي كذا متعلق زمامها بشجرة فبادر الناس فوجدوها كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله لخالد بن الوليد حين بعثه إلى أكيدر بدومة الجندل: "أما أنكم ستأتونه فتجدونه يصيد البقر" فوجدوه كذلك. ومن ذلك قوله عليه السلام للعباس حين أسره: "افد نفسك وابني أخيك" يعني عقيل بن أبي طالب ونوفل بن الحارث فإنك ذو مال فقال: لا مال عندي. قال: فأين المال الذي وضعته بمكة عند أم الفضل وليس معكما أحد، فقلت: إن أصبت في سفري فللفضل كذا ولعبد الله كذا ولفلان كذا؟ فقال العباس: والذي بعثك بالحق نبيا ما علم بهذا أحد غيري، وإنك لرسول الله وأسلم هو وعقيل. ومن ذلك ما كان يخبر أهل النفاق بما كانوا يقولون فيما بينهم ويبيتون ما لا يرضى من القول حتى كانوا من شدة تعنتهم يحذرون أن ينزل عليه سورة تنبئهم بما في قلوبهم، وأمثال ذلك كثير، وكتابنا هذا يضيق عن ذكر عشر ذلك فضلاً عن كله، والله الموفق. ثم إن جميع ما أخبر من الأخبار الكائنة في المستقبل خرج على ما أخبر من غير تمكن كذب أو حلف في شيء من ذلك لا كمثل أخبار الكهنة والمنجمين.
And among that is that he (the Prophet) announced the death of the Negus and informed his companions of his death and prayed over him, and reports followed that he died on that day. And among that is his saying to Ammar: 'The rebellious group will kill you,' so he was killed on the day of Siffin with Ali. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'The most wretched of people is the one who hamstrung the she-camel, and the one who will dye this from this' — meaning the one who strikes your head and dyes your beard from the blood of your head — so Ali was struck on his head when he was killed. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'You will kill the oath-breakers, the renegades, and the deviators.' And among that is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar,' so he informed us by this that the caliph after him is Abu Bakr and after Abu Bakr, Umar, may God be pleased with them both. And among that is his saying: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years, then God gives sovereignty to whom He wills,' and the caliphate of the rightly-guided caliphs was thirty years. And among that is the hadith of the night of Isra' and what he informed of the news of the Quraysh caravan, and it was as he informed. And among that is that his, peace be upon him, she-camel was lost, and he began asking people about her, so the hypocrites said: 'This Muhammad tells you news of the heaven but does not know where his she-camel is.' So he ascended the pulpit, praised God and extolled Him, and recounted their words, then said: 'I do not know except what my Lord has taught me, and He has informed me that she is in such-and-such valley, her halter entangled in a tree.' So the people hastened and found her thus. And among that is his saying to Khalid ibn al-Walid when he sent him to Ukaydir of Dumah al-Jandal: 'Indeed, you will come to him and find him hunting cows,' and they found him thus. And among that is his saying, peace be upon him, to al-Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself and your brother's sons' — meaning 'Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith — 'for you are wealthy.' So he said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Then where is the wealth you placed in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl, with no one else with you, and you said: If I am struck in my journey, then such-and-such is for al-Fadl, such-and-such for 'Abdullah, and such-and-such for so-and-so?' Then al-Abbas said: 'By Him who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knows this except me, and you are indeed the Messenger of God,' and he and 'Aqil embraced Islam. And among that is what he used to inform about the people of hypocrisy, what they said among themselves and secretly plotted of speech that is not pleasing, until from the intensity of their obstinacy they feared that a chapter would be revealed to him informing them of what was in their hearts. And such examples are many, and this book of ours is too narrow to mention a tenth of that, let alone all of it, and God is the granter of success. Then, all that he informed of news occurring in the future came out as he informed, without any possibility of falsehood or mistake in any of that, not like the news of soothsayers and astrologers.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a cumulative proof of prophethood through predictive miracles (i'jāz al-ikhbār bi-al-ghayb). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, lists several verified predictions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) that demonstrate his truthfulness. The argument proceeds by enumeration: each example is introduced with 'wa min dhālika' (among that is), building a chain of evidence. The examples include: (1) the death of the Negus of Abyssinia, announced while the Prophet was in Medina; (2) the prophecy that Ammar ibn Yasir would be killed by the rebellious party, fulfilled at the Battle of Siffin; (3) the prophecy that the most wretched person would strike Ali's head, fulfilled by Ibn Muljam; (4) the prophecy that Ali would kill the oath-breakers (nakithūn), renegades (māriqūn), and deviators (qāsitūn); (5) the instruction to follow Abu Bakr and Umar, indicating the order of succession; (6) the prophecy that the caliphate after him would last thirty years, which matched the reign of the four rightly-guided caliphs; (7) the details of the Isra' night and the Quraysh caravan, which came true; (8) the incident of the lost she-camel, where the Prophet accurately described its location; (9) the prophecy that Khalid ibn al-Walid would find Ukaydir hunting cows; (10) the revelation of the hidden wealth of al-Abbas, which led to his conversion; (11) the exposure of the hypocrites' secret conversations. After listing these, the author states that there are many more such examples, but his book cannot contain them all. Finally, he draws the conclusion: all these future reports came to pass exactly as predicted, without any falsehood or error—unlike the predictions of soothsayers (kahana) and astrologers (munajjimun), who often err. This distinction establishes that the Prophet's knowledge is from divine revelation, not from human guesswork.

Key Takeaway
The fulfillment of specific prophecies about individuals confirms that the Prophet's knowledge comes from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
These prophecies were fulfilled precisely. Is your trust in the Prophet's knowledge merely intellectual, or does it translate into obedience in areas where his teachings seem difficult or counter to your desires?
?
The Prophet knew about events after his death, including the fates of individuals. If you truly believe that, how does it change the way you approach his commands regarding the unseen—like the punishment of the grave or the Day of Judgment?
?
Consider the prophecy about Ali being struck on the head. The Prophet named the most wretched person. Do you ever reflect on your own potential to be among the wretched if you persist in a sin or doubt that you know is wrong? What will you change today to avoid that?

Prophecies About Succession and the Caliphate
Al-Nasafi cites prophecies about succession and the Isra' event.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's predictions about leadership and future events prove his prophethood.

Core Idea
Predictions about political events also prove divine origin.

Al-Nasafi continues with prophecies about the caliphate and the night journey. These examples show that the Prophet's knowledge extended to political and historical events that later unfolded exactly as described.

Guided Path
1
Read the three prophecies
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how each prophecy is about future leadership or events.
The prophecies are: order to follow Abu Bakr and Umar, 30-year caliphate, and details of Isra'.
2
Analyze the fulfillment
Check that Abu Bakr and Umar indeed succeeded, the rightly-guided caliphate lasted 30 years, and the caravan news from Isra' matched.
These are historical facts.
3
Connect to the argument
Understand that these predictions could not have been guessed, so they indicate divine revelation.
