The Fourth Benefit: Returning to Service with Humility
Definition of the fourth benefit of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth benefit of Hajj: after receiving forgiveness, the pilgrim returns to normal life with humility, gratitude, and a renewed sense of servitude.

Core Idea
Forgiveness in Hajj leads to humble service, not continued asceticism.

After completing the essential rites of Hajj and attaining forgiveness, the pilgrim does not remain in a state of austerity. Instead, he resumes adornment and cleanliness, but now with a deeper awareness of his dependence on Allah. This lesson explores the fourth benefit of Hajj as articulated by Imam Nasafi, highlighting the transformation that occurs in the pilgrim's heart.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the fourth benefit
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the sequence: after forgiveness, the pilgrim removes austerity and returns to adornment.
2
Identify the three states mentioned
The passage mentions three things: removing austerity, dishevelment disappearing, and returning to adornment and cleanliness. Identify these and reflect on their meaning.
These show a return to normal life but with a transformed attitude.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Why does the pilgrim return to adornment? The passage says it is to show gratitude and neediness to Allah. Consider how this contrasts with worldly pride.
The goal is to fulfill servitude and the rights of self in serving Allah.

والرابع أن العبد إذا فعل تلك الثلاثة وفاز بحسن موعوده له بالرضا عنه والتجاوز عن خطاياه أن يسكن إليه، ويزيل عن نفسه التقشف وينقضي عن هيئته الشعث، ويعود إلى خدمته على صورة من نال عفو ملكه وسعد بمرضاته، فيعاود الزينة ويراجع الوضاءة، ويباسط مولاه بمسألة حوائجه، ويظهر افتقاره إليه ليكون قد قضى أمر العبودية وتمم حقوق نفسه في خدمة ربه، وواقع تحت الحج وتواعبه، ثم لما كان الحج عبادة لا يتوصل إلى أدائها إلا من له فضل قوة في الجسم وسعة في المال وبسطة في الحال والجاه – وهذه المعاني من دواعي الكبر والسطوة والجبرية - جعل الله تعالى هيئة أداء هذه العبادة على صورة مضادة لأحوال الجبابرة، وفي الطرف الأبعد من هيئات المتكبرين، وهو هجران الزينة رأسًا، والسعي في المواطن عدوا وتحريك الأطراف بلا سبب، ورمي الأحجار لا إلى أحد، وتقبيل حجر ولا ينفع، وتعظيم مواطن لا تجدي نفعا ولا تمنع؛ ليعترف به الجبابرة لمر الخضوع ويذعن الأشراف لخالص العبودية، وتصير الأقدام سواسية في ذات الله تعالى، فمن نال في الدنيا ملكًا عظيمًا أو جاها وشرفًا وسعة في الأموال متى لابس عملاً لا يلائم صورة المتكبر به، وينافي أفعال الجبابرة رأسًا من الإقبال على حجر أصم بالتقبيل وعلى مواضع ميتة بالإجلال يصير ذلك أبلغ سبب في ارتفاض الكبر، وأتم رياضة لطرح الأنفة، فإن من أطاعته نفسه لوجه الله تعالى في توقير شيء لا ينفع ولا يؤذي، ولا يعلم ولا يشعر فهو إلى توقير من هو نظيره من العباد أسرع، وإلى هجران ما استشعر من الجبرية أوحى، والله الموفق.
And the fourth: that the servant, when he does those three [acts] and succeeds in the good promise to him of contentment with him and overlooking his sins, should settle into it, and remove from himself austerity, and the dishevelment of his appearance disappears, and he returns to his service in the form of one who has obtained the pardon of his king and is blessed with his pleasure, so he resumes adornment and returns to cleanliness, and he is open with his master in asking for his needs, and he shows his neediness to Him, so that he may have fulfilled the matter of servitude and completed the rights of himself in the service of his Lord, and fallen under the Hajj and its duties. Then, since Hajj is an act of worship that can only be performed by one who has strength of body, wealth, and status and prestige – and these meanings are among the causes of pride, tyranny, and haughtiness – Allah Most High made the manner of performing this worship in a form contrary to the states of tyrants, and at the farthest extreme from the states of the arrogant: namely, abandoning adornment entirely, running in the places of worship, moving limbs without reason, throwing stones at no one, kissing a stone that brings no benefit, and venerating places that yield no benefit and do not prevent harm; so that the tyrants might acknowledge the bitterness of submission, and the nobles yield to pure servitude, and feet become equal in the essence of Allah Most High. So whoever has obtained in this world great kingship or prestige and honor and wealth, when he engages in an act that does not suit the image of the arrogant and contradicts the actions of tyrants entirely – such as turning to a deaf stone for kissing and to dead places for veneration – that becomes the most effective cause for the lowering of pride and the most complete training for casting off haughtiness. For if a person subdues his ego for the sake of Allah Most High in honoring something that neither benefits nor harms, and neither knows nor feels, then he is quicker to honor one who is like him from among the servants, and more inclined to abandon what he perceives of haughtiness. And Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the fourth benefit (الرابع) of Hajj. The author states that after the pilgrim performs the three previous actions (mentioned earlier: ihram, standing at Arafat, and the circuit/sa'y?) and attains forgiveness, he should return to normal life but with a transformed character. He removes the rough ascetic appearance and resumes clean adornment, but now with a sense of gratitude and dependence on Allah. Then the author explains the wisdom behind the specific rituals of Hajj: because Hajj requires strength and wealth, which can lead to pride, Allah prescribed the rituals in a form opposite to the behavior of tyrants. These include abandoning adornment, running (sa'y), throwing stones, kissing a stone that provides no worldly benefit, and venerating places that do not help or harm. This humbles the proud, as a person who can humble himself before an inanimate object for Allah's sake will more readily humble himself before fellow humans. The passage concludes with a supplication: 'And Allah is the Giver of success.'

Key Terms
التقشف
الشعث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the pilgrim do after receiving forgiveness?
A) He continues to live in austerity and dishevelment.
B) He removes austerity and returns to adornment and cleanliness.
C) He abandons all worldly life and becomes a recluse.
D) He immediately performs another Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The fourth benefit of Hajj is that after forgiveness, the pilgrim returns to normal life with humility and gratitude, not with continued asceticism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After receiving Allah's forgiveness in Hajj, do you feel you must maintain an artificial austerity to prove your piety, or are you willing to return to your normal life with the same humility and open-heartedness in asking for your needs? What would that look like for you tomorrow?
?
The passage says the servant 'returns to his service in the form of one who has obtained pardon and is blessed with pleasure.' Is your daily service to Allah characterized by that joy and confidence, or do you often serve with a sense of burden? How can you change that today?
?
If you truly believed that your sins were overlooked, would you be more open in presenting your needs to Allah? What keeps you from being as 'open with your master' as this passage describes?

The Wisdom of Hajj Rituals: Counteracting Pride
Explanation of the wisdom behind Hajj rituals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the profound wisdom behind the specific rituals of Hajj: they are deliberately designed to humble the proud and counteract the arrogance that wealth and status can bring.

Core Idea
Hajj rituals are purposely opposite to the behavior of tyrants to instill humility.

Hajj requires strength, wealth, and status, which can easily lead to pride. But Allah, in His wisdom, prescribed the rituals of Hajj in a form that completely contradicts the ways of the arrogant. This passage explains how actions like abandoning adornment, running, throwing stones, and kissing the Black Stone serve to humble the soul and remind every pilgrim that all are equal before Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the wisdom of the rituals
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the contrast: Hajj requires means that could cause pride, yet the rituals are the opposite of tyrants' behavior.
2
Identify the specific rituals and their opposites
The passage lists several rituals: abandoning adornment, running, throwing stones, kissing a stone, venerating places. Consider how each is contrary to the actions of the proud.
For example, kissing a stone that neither benefits nor harms is the opposite of seeking useful connections.
3
Reflect on the purpose: humbling the proud
The author states that these actions make tyrants acknowledge submission, nobles yield to servitude, and feet become equal. Think about how this transforms the pilgrim.
This lesson guards against seeing Hajj rituals as meaningless.

The Certainty of Muhammad's Truthfulness
Concludes that all previous arguments confirm Muhammad's truthfulness, unless hindered by stubbornness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the evidence for Muhammad's prophethood is so compelling that only moral failings can obstruct acceptance.

Core Idea
Only moral corruption, not lack of evidence, prevents acceptance of Muhammad's truth.

This concluding passage ties together all previous arguments for Muhammad's prophethood. It emphasizes that the evidence is sufficient to produce certainty, and the only barriers are negative human traits like stubbornness and bigotry.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's concluding tone come through.
Note the unclear phrase 'الا الله' - the translator marks it with [?].
2
Identify the obstacles to certainty
Find the list of traits that can contradict the clear knowledge: obstinacy, conceit, bigotry, tribalism, and pride. These are moral/spiritual failings, not intellectual ones.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider that the proof is complete and knowledge is certain unless one is hindered by such traits. This shows the strength of the evidence.
The passage is not merely repeating; it is a strong conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل ما سبق يؤكد صدق دعوة محمد وبالوقوف على ما تقدم عرف أنه الا الله [؟] كان صادقًا فيما ادعاه من رسالة ربه معرفة لا يشوبها شك ولا يعتريها ما يزيلها لو لم يعارضها ما مر ذكرها من المعاني الصادرة عن ذلك - أعني العناد والمكابرة للتعصب – والجنسية أو الأنفة
All that has preceded affirms the truth of the call of Muhammad. And by standing on what has come before, he knows that he [؟] was truthful in what he claimed of the message of his Lord, a knowledge not mixed with doubt nor affected by anything that would remove it, were it not contradicted by the meanings that have been mentioned stemming from that – I mean obstinacy and conceit due to bigotry – and tribalism or pride.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is the concluding affirmation of the book's central thesis: the arguments presented throughout confirm the truth of Muhammad's prophethood. The author states that by reflecting on all that has preceded, one knows with certainty that Muhammad was truthful in his claim of prophethood, a knowledge free from doubt. However, this certainty is only undermined by the negative traits mentioned earlier: obstinacy (العناد), conceit (المكابرة) arising from bigotry (التعصب), tribalism (الجنسية), and pride (الأنفة). Thus, the only obstacles to accepting the truth are moral failings, not lack of evidence.

Correction: It actually emphasizes that the evidence produces certain knowledge, and only moral failings can block acceptance. It is a powerful conclusion, not a simple repetition.

Key Takeaway
The cumulative evidence for Muhammad's prophethood yields certain knowledge, and only negative traits like stubbornness and tribalism prevent its acceptance.

?

Confirming Muhammad's Prophethood Through Proofs and Refuting Objections
Author concludes previous proofs confirm Muhammad's truthfulness and refutes objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the preceding miracles establish certain knowledge of Muhammad's prophethood and how the author refutes objections that claim his message merely reiterates reason.

Core Idea
Truth is clear; denial reveals inner barriers, not lack of evidence.

The author now draws the conclusion from all the preceding proofs. He affirms that true knowledge of the Prophet's message can be certain and unshaken, unless one's own negative traits—like stubbornness or pride—block acceptance. He then tackles a specific intellectual objection, showing it stems from misunderstanding reason's limits.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then read the literal English translation. Let the author's concluding tone come through before analyzing.
Notice the dense structure: conclusion, obstacles, refutation.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states that by standing on the previous proofs, one gains certain knowledge that Muhammad was truthful. This knowledge is free from doubt unless opposed by certain factors.
3
List the obstacles to acceptance
The author enumerates several negative traits that prevent acceptance: stubbornness, partisanship, racial fanaticism, pride, habit, and laziness. Note how each opposes rational acceptance.
These are psychological and social barriers, not intellectual failings.
4
Examine the refutation of the objection
The author addresses the claim that the Prophet only brought what reason already knows. He argues this claim is based on ignorance of what reason can and cannot accept.
The refutation hinges on defining the limits of reason.
5
Reflect on the overall purpose
This passage seals the argument from miracles: the proofs are sufficient, and denial only arises from internal obstacles or ignorance.
The author concludes the discussion of miracles and proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كل ما سبق يؤكد صدق دعوة محمد . وبالوقوف على ما تقدم عرف أنه الا الله كان صادقًا فيما ادعاه من رسالة ربه معرفة لا يشوبها شك ولا يعتريها ما يزيلها لو لم يعارضها ما مر ذكرها من المعاني الصادرة عن ذلك - أعني العناد والمكابرة للتعصب – والجنسية أو الأنفة المانعة عن اتباع الغير أو الإلف والعادة أو الكسل عن لوازم التكليف وبه يبطل قول من يقول: إنه عليه السلام أتى بما في العقول دفعه وإنكاره ، وظهر أنه زعم ما زعم عن الجهل بما يقبله العقل وما لا يقبله، هذا هو الكلام من حيث المعجزات والدلالات.
All that precedes confirms the truthfulness of Muhammad's call. And by standing upon what has preceded, it is known that he [؟] was truthful in his claim of his Lord's message — a knowledge not mixed with doubt nor affected by anything that would remove it — had it not been opposed by the meanings that issued from that — namely stubbornness and obstinacy due to partisanship — [and] racial fanaticism or the pride that prevents following others, or familiarity and habit, or laziness regarding the duties of responsibility. And by this is invalidated the statement of one who says: 'He (peace be upon him) produced what is in the intellects, its repudiation and denial.' And it becomes clear that he claimed what he claimed out of ignorance of what the intellect accepts and what it does not accept. This is the discussion from the perspective of miracles and proofs.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage serves as a concluding argument from the previous evidence regarding miracles. The author states that all previous proofs confirm the truth of Muhammad's prophethood. By studying them, one can attain certain knowledge that he was truthful — knowledge free from doubt and immune to anything that could remove it — unless it is opposed by certain negative traits emanating from the person: stubbornness, partisanship, racial fanaticism, pride, habit, or laziness. These factors prevent one from accepting the truth. The author then refutes a specific objection: someone who claims that the Prophet merely brought what is already known by reason, and that he was denied. This claim is invalidated because it stems from ignorance of what reason can and cannot accept. The passage ends by noting that this concludes the discussion of miracles and proofs.

الجنسية

المعجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet only presented what reason already knows, and his denial was justified because reason could reject it.
Correction: The author shows this claim arises from ignorance of what the intellect accepts and does not accept; the Prophet brought miracles beyond reason, and denial stems from inner obstacles, not intellectual deficiency.

Key Takeaway
The preceding miracles provide certain knowledge of Muhammad's truthfulness; any denial must stem from internal barriers or ignorance, not from a lack of proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The refutation shows that claiming the Prophet only brought what reason knows is actually ignorance. Where in your life have you assumed you already knew enough, preventing you from deeper submission? What will you say to Allah if He asks you about your neglect of a truth you knew was clear?

Properties of Prophethood: Two Main Divisions
Author divides properties of prophethood into two categories: establishing foundation and nurturing strength.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main divisions of the properties of prophethood and their distinct purposes.

Core Idea
The properties of prophethood work in two complementary ways: building the foundation and nurturing its power.

This lesson introduces a fundamental classification in the discussion of prophethood's special characteristics. Imam al-Nasafi divides these properties into two categories, each serving a distinct role in the effectiveness of prophethood. Understanding this division helps us appreciate the comprehensive nature of prophethood's functions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation to grasp the author's concise classification.
2
Identify the two types
Notice that the author explicitly names two types: one for preparing and strengthening the foundation, and one for nurturing powers.
These are not separate but complementary.
3
Reflect on the complementarity
Consider why both types are necessary for prophethood to be fully effective. The commentary explains that they are two aspects of a single mission.
Avoid thinking they are unrelated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في خواص النبوة وأقسامها . وأما الكلام من حيث خواص النبوة فنقول: هي إلى قسمين قسم منها لتمهيد أمرها وتوطيد أساسها، وقسم منها لتربية قواها.
On the properties of prophethood and its divisions. As for the discussion from the perspective of the properties of prophethood, we say: They are of two types: one type is for preparing its affair and strengthening its foundation, and one type is for nurturing its powers.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a brief classification. The author introduces a new topic: the properties or special characteristics (khawāṣṣ) of prophethood and their divisions. He states that these properties are of two types. The first type serves to prepare the ground for prophethood and establish its foundation firmly. The second type serves to nurture and develop the strengths and powers of prophethood. This is a general overview before detailing each division.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The two types of properties are independent and unrelated.
Correction: They are complementary: one establishes the foundation while the other nurtures its strength, both necessary for prophethood to be effective.

Checkpoint
What are the two main divisions of the properties of prophethood?
A) External and internal
B) Essential and accidental
C) For establishing the foundation and for nurturing its powers
D) Legal and spiritual

Key Takeaway
The properties of prophethood are divided into two complementary categories: one that establishes and strengthens its foundation, and another that nurtures its powers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author divides the properties of prophethood into 'preparing the foundation' and 'nurturing the powers.' Which of these two aspects is currently weaker in your own faith life? What one concrete step will you take today to address that weakness?
?
Are you treating your relationship with the Prophet ﷺ as merely a historical foundation, or are you actively nurturing its power in your daily decisions and character? What would change if you truly did both?
?
If you had to choose only one—strengthening your foundational beliefs or nurturing your spiritual growth—which would you pick, and does that choice reveal a dangerous imbalance? How will you restore balance starting now?

Prophethood: Divine Selection and Bestowal of Gifts
Author enumerates two sub-divisions of the first property of prophethood: racial selection and bestowal of gifts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two sub-divisions of the first property of prophethood: racial selection and bestowal of gifts, and how they manifest in the prophets.

Core Idea
God chooses prophets from the best of their kind and grants them special gifts.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla lays out the first division of the proofs of prophethood, focusing on how God selects prophets. The author explains two sub-types: first, that God chooses the most excellent individual from a given race or community; second, that He then bestows upon that chosen one additional gifts and perfections. Together, these establish a foundation for understanding prophethood as a divine gift, not a human attainment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the author's style and the two sub-divisions he presents.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the two types are clearly introduced.
2
Identify the two sub-divisions
The author explicitly states that the first section is divided into two. Find both: racial selection and bestowal of gifts. Note how each is defined.
3
Understand racial selection
The author argues by analogy and quotes the Quran to show that God chooses the most suitable person from a community. Reflect on the wisdom behind this.
This is not about ethnic superiority but suitability.
4
Reflect on bestowal of gifts
The second sub-division introduces that God gives extra gifts to the chosen prophet. Though the passage cuts off, consider why this is necessary.
Perfection belongs only to God, so human prophets need divine gifts.
5
Connect to the Quranic verse and Prophet Muhammad
Note the verse 'Allah knows best where to place His message' and how the author says this was especially true for Prophet Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما القسم الأول منها فقسمان: أحدهما: الاختيار الجنسى فإن الحكمة تقتضي أن من أراد إنفاذ رسول إلى موضع أن يختار من أصحابه من هو أصلح، فالله تعالى إذا قدر أن يختار لتلك الرتبة السنية والدرجة العلية واحدًا من عباده فإنه يختار فاضل الجنس الذي منه في عقله وفهمه وصلاحه وعامة أفعاله، ولا يختار واحدًا من الجهلة الأشرار ليكون معدنا لوحيه وموضعا لاختلاف الملائكة إليه، ولذلك قال تعالى: أَعْلَمُ حَيْثُ يجعلُ رِسَالَتَهُ وهذه الخاصية كانت ثابتة لنبينا محمد عليه السلام فوق ما كانت لغيره من الرسل عليهم السلام على ما مر ذكره في بيان أخلاقه الكريمة وشيمه الشريفة. والقسم الثاني من القسم الأول: هو موهبة الزيادات واللطائف والرجحان في الأخلاق والمذاهب، فإنه ليس الكمال إلا الله تعالى والحكمة تقتضي أن من اختار من
As for the first section [of the properties], it is of two types: One of them is racial selection (al-ikhtiyār al-jinsī). For wisdom requires that whoever intends to send a messenger to a place should choose from his companions the one who is most suitable. So Allah, when He decrees to choose for that high rank and lofty degree one of His servants, He chooses the most excellent of the race from which [the prophet] comes, in his intellect, understanding, righteousness, and all his actions. And He does not choose one of the ignorant evil ones to be a mine for His revelation and a place for the angels to descend to. Therefore He said: 'Allah knows best where to place His message.' And this characteristic was established for our Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) more than for other messengers (peace be upon them), as mentioned earlier in the explanation of his noble character and honorable traits. The second type of the first section is the bestowal of increases, subtleties, and preeminence in character and conduct. For perfection belongs only to Allah, and wisdom requires that whoever He chooses from
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the first main division of the properties of prophethood (the one for establishing the foundation). The author divides it into two sub-types. The first is 'racial selection' (al-ikhtiyār al-jinsī). He draws an analogy: when someone wants to send a messenger, he chooses the best person from his circle. Similarly, Allah chooses from among humanity the most excellent in intellect, understanding, righteousness, and actions. He does not choose an ignorant evil person to be the receptacle of revelation. He quotes the Quranic verse 'Allah knows best where to place His message' (6:124). This quality was present in Prophet Muhammad to a greater degree than in other prophets, as mentioned earlier. The second sub-type is the bestowal of extra gifts, subtleties, and moral superiority. The author states that perfection is only for Allah, and wisdom requires that when He chooses someone, He endows him with special qualities. The passage is incomplete but sets the stage for further explanation.

Key Terms

موهبة الزيادات
اللطائف
الرجحان
إعْلَمُ حَيْثُ يَجْعَلُ رِسَالَتَهُ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That racial selection implies ethnic superiority or racism.
Correction: It is about choosing the most suitable individual from a community based on intellectual and moral qualities, not ethnic or racial superiority.

Checkpoint
What is the first sub-division of the first section of the properties of prophethood according to the passage?
A) Miracles
B) Racial selection (al-ikhtiyār al-jinsī)
C) Mystical states
D) Divine attributes

Key Takeaway
God selects prophets from the best of their kind and then bestows upon them extra gifts, establishing prophethood as a divine bestowal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage says Allah does not choose the ignorant and evil for revelation. Since you claim to follow the Prophet, what does that require of your own character? Are there any ignorant or evil habits you are tolerating that contradict the path of the chosen? Identify one and commit to leaving it.
?
If perfection belongs only to Allah and prophets are recipients of His gifts, do you ever feel envy or resentment towards the prophets' status? How can you transform that into gratitude for being given such guides, and what will you do this week to emulate their noble traits without pride?

The Two Main Categories of Prophetic Characteristics and Divine Selection by Genus
The author divides prophetic characteristics and explains selection by genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two overarching categories of prophetic characteristics and the first part of the preparation category: God's selection of the most excellent individual from a human genus.

Core Idea
God's choice of prophets is based on wisdom and inherent excellence, not arbitrariness.

The author begins by classifying the special characteristics of prophethood into two broad types: those that establish prophethood and those that nurture it. He then focuses on the first category, preparation, and introduces its first part: divine selection by genus. This passage explains why God chooses the best from a people and not the wicked, supported by a Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the overall division
Read the first two lines to see that prophetic characteristics are divided into two categories: establishing the affair and nurturing the powers.
2
Understand the first category
Notice that the first category (preparation) itself has two parts. Here we cover the first part: selection by genus.
3
Reflect on the wisdom
Examine the rational argument: wisdom requires choosing the most suitable messenger. Also note the Quranic proof (6:124) and the application to Prophet Muhammad.
This characteristic was even more pronounced in Prophet Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام من حيث خواص النبوة فنقول: هي إلى قسمين قسم منها لتمهيد أمرها وتوطيد أساسها، وقسم منها لتربية قواها.
القسم الأول لتمهيد أمر النبوة
فأما القسم الأول منها فقسمان:
أحدهما: الاختيار الجنسى فإن الحكمة تقتضي أن من أراد إنفاذ رسول إلى موضع أن يختار من أصحابه من هو أصلح، فالله تعالى إذا قدر أن يختار لتلك الرتبة السنية والدرجة العلية، واحدًا من عباده فإنه يختار فاضل الجنس الذي منه في عقله وفهمه وصلاحه وعامة أفعاله، ولا يختار واحدًا من الجهلة الأشرار ليكون معدنا لوحيه وموضعا لاختلاف الملائكة إليه، ولذلك قال تعالى: أَعْلَمُ حَيْثُ يَجْعَلُ رِسَالَتَهُ. وهذه الخاصية كانت ثابتة لنبينا محمد عليه السلام فوق ما كانت لغيره من الرسل عليهم السلام على ما مر ذكره في بيان أخلاقه الكريمة وشيمه الشريفة.
والقسم الثاني من القسم الأول: هو موهبة الزيادات واللطائف والرجحان في الأخلاق والمذاهب، فإنه ليس الكمال إلا الله تعالى والحكمة تقتضي أن من اختار من أصحابه رسولاً أن يزيح علله فيما عرف حاجته ماسة إليه، فالله تعالى إذا قيض عبدًا من عباده لسياسة البلاد والعباد فإنه لا يحرمه الفضائل التي بها تنزاح علله في كفاية ما فوض إليه - أعني به في توفية القوى الفاضلة نفساً وجسماً - ثم السلامة عن العاهات المشوهة للخلقة ثم البراءة عن الآفات المخلة بالأفعال، ثم يبيح له عامة ما علم أنه يحتاج إليه للقيام بما فوض إليه حسب ما أزاح لموسى عليه السلام علته في حل عقدة لسانه والتأييد بأخيه هارون على ما قال تعالى: قَدْ أُوتِيتَ سُؤْلَكَ يَا مُوسَى. وهذه الخاصية أيضا كانت لنبينا محمد عليه السلام على ما ذكره في بيان الدلالة الراجعة إلى بدنه.
As for the discussion regarding the special characteristics of prophethood, we say: they are of two types: a type for establishing its affair and consolidating its foundation, and a type for nurturing its powers. The first type: for establishing the affair of prophethood. As for the first type, it is of two parts: One of them: the selection by genus, for wisdom requires that whoever intends to send a messenger to a place should choose from his companions the one who is most suitable. So God Almighty, when He wills to choose for that high rank and lofty degree one of His servants, He chooses the most excellent of the genus from which he comes in his intellect, understanding, righteousness, and all his actions, and He does not choose one of the ignorant wicked to be a receptacle for His revelation and a place for the descent of angels to him. Therefore He said: 'God knows best where to place His message.' This characteristic was established for our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, more than for other messengers, peace be upon them, as previously mentioned in the explanation of his noble character and honorable traits. The second part of the first type: it is the bestowal of extras, subtle gifts, and preponderance in morals and ways, for perfection belongs only to God Almighty, and wisdom requires that whoever chooses from his companions a messenger should remove his obstacles regarding what he knows he has an acute need for. So God Almighty, when He appoints a servant from His servants to govern the lands and the people, does not deprive him of the virtues by which his obstacles are removed in fulfilling what he has been entrusted with—I mean by this the completion of virtuous powers, soul and body—then safety from disfiguring defects, then freedom from deficiencies that impair actions, then He permits to him generally what He knows he needs to carry out what he has been entrusted with, just as He removed for Moses, peace be upon him, his obstacle in loosening the knot of his tongue and supported him with his brother Aaron, as He said: 'You have been granted your request, O Moses.' This characteristic was also for our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, as mentioned in the explanation of the proof pertaining to his body.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage defines the classification of the special characteristics of prophethood (خواص النبوة). The author states that these characteristics are divided into two main categories: (1) those that serve to establish and consolidate the foundation of prophethood (تمهيد أمرها وتوطيد أساسها), and (2) those that serve to nurture and strengthen its powers (تربية قواها). He then elaborates the first category, which itself has two parts. 

First part: divine selection by genus (الاختيار الجنسى). Wisdom dictates that God chooses the best individual from a human genus in terms of intellect, understanding, righteousness, and all actions. He does not choose a wicked, ignorant person to be the recipient of revelation. This is supported by the Quranic verse: 'God knows best where to place His message' (6:124). 

Second part: bestowal of extras and subtle gifts (موهبة الزيادات واللطائف والرجحان). Since only God is perfect, wisdom requires that God, when choosing a messenger, removes obstacles that would hinder his mission. God grants the prophet virtues—completion of physical and spiritual powers, safety from physical defects, freedom from deficiencies in actions—and permits him all that he needs for his task. An example is Moses' request to remove his speech impediment and the support of Aaron (20:36). 

The author notes that both these characteristics were present in Prophet Muhammad to an even greater degree.

Key Terms
خواص النبوة
التمهيد
الاختيار الجنسى
الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's selection of a prophet is arbitrary and without reason.
Correction: The author emphasizes that selection is based on wisdom and the individual's inherent excellence, not arbitrary.

Checkpoint
What is the first part of the first category (preparation) of prophetic characteristics?
A) Bestowal of extra virtues
B) Divine selection by genus
C) Connection of revelation
D) Warning about slips

Key Takeaway
God's selection of a prophet is not arbitrary but based on choosing the most excellent individual from a human genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God selects the most excellent for prophethood, what does that say about the standard He sets for those who carry His message? Are you actively striving to be among the most excellent in your character, intellect, and actions, or are you content with mediocrity? What specific changes can you make today to align with the excellence that God chooses?
?
The author states that God does not choose the ignorant wicked to be a receptacle for His revelation. How does this challenge your assumption that knowledge and righteousness are secondary to status or popularity? In what area of your life are you seeking God's guidance while neglecting the qualities that make you a worthy vessel?
?
The Prophet Muhammad had this characteristic of selection by genus more than others. What are you doing to emulate his noble character, not just in ritual but in the consistency of your intellect and righteousness? If you were to be evaluated on the criteria of 'excellence of genus' today, would you be selected? What is the one quality you need to work on most urgently?

The Second Part of Preparation: Bestowal of Extras and Subtle Gifts
The author explains the bestowal of extras as the second part of preparation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second part of the preparation category: God bestows extras, subtle gifts, and preponderance upon prophets to remove obstacles and enable them to fulfill their mission.

Core Idea
God perfects His chosen prophets by granting them all necessary virtues and removing their obstacles.

After discussing selection by genus, the author turns to the second part of preparation: the bestowal of extras and subtle gifts. This passage explains that since only God is perfect, wisdom requires that God removes the obstacles of a messenger by granting him additional virtues, safety from defects, and everything needed for his mission. The example of Moses' speech impediment and support from Aaron illustrates this principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of the second part
Read the first sentence defining 'bestowal of extras' and note that it includes subtle gifts and preponderance in morals and ways.
2
Understand the wisdom behind the grants
The passage states that perfection belongs only to God, so wisdom requires that a messenger's obstacles be removed. Identify the specific grants listed.
Grants include completion of virtuous powers, safety from defects, freedom from deficiencies, and permission to use what is needed.
3
Examine the example of Moses
Read how God removed Moses' speech knot and supported him with Aaron, as a case study. Note that this was also true for Prophet Muhammad.

The Second Category of Prophetic Characteristics: Nurturing
Enumerates two subcategories of nurturing prophethood: revelation and warning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two components of the nurturing category of prophetic characteristics: the connection of revelation and divine warning against errors.

Core Idea
Prophets need continuous divine guidance and warning, not just initial empowerment.

This passage unpacks the second major category of prophetic characteristics—those that nurture and sustain the powers of prophethood. The author divides this category into two essential components: the ongoing connection of revelation and divine alerts to prevent mistakes. As you read, notice how the author uses a master-servant analogy to illustrate why even capable prophets need constant support.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main division
The passage begins by stating that the 'nurturing' category itself splits into two parts. Read carefully to find those two parts.
The first part is 'connection of the sources of revelation'; the second is 'alerting him to places of slip'.
2
Understand the analogy
The author compares God delegating prophethood to a master delegating a task to a servant. Why does the master still provide guidance even if the servant is capable? Reflect on this analogy.
This analogy highlights that guidance is not a sign of incapacity but of support.
3
Connect to the Prophet Muhammad
The first part is confirmed for Prophet Muhammad by the Quranic verse 'Your Lord has not forsaken you, nor has He hated you.' Think about why this verse is relevant to the connection of revelation.
4
Grasp the second part
The second part warns against slips. The passage ends with the idea that a master does not abandon his servant. Consider what this implies for prophethood.
Prophetic infallibility is not automatic; it requires divine vigilance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني من القسمين الأولين: وهو الخاصية التي يحتاج إليها لتربية قواها فينقسم أيضًا إلى قسمين:
أحدهما: اتصال مواد الوحي به، فإن كل من قلد غيره عملاً من الأعمال فلابد أن يؤيده فيه بالإرشاد ويتابع لديه بالهداية وإن كان هو في نفسه مستقلاً كافيًا ليكون معونة له على ما يتولاه من خدمته.
والأنبياء عليهم السلام لم يستغنوا عن التبصير والإرشاد، ولا يتم ذلك إلا باتصال الوحي، وهذه الخاصية كانت لمحمد عليه السلام قال الله تعالى: مَا وَدَعَكَ رَبُّكَ وَمَا قَلَى.
والثاني: تنبيهه على مواقع الزلل فإن من قلد عبدًا من عبيده فإنه لا يخليه.
As for the second of the two first categories—which is the characteristic needed for nurturing its powers—it also divides into two parts: 
One of them: the connection of the sources of revelation to him. For whoever delegates a task to another must support him in it with guidance and continue to provide him with direction, even if he himself is independent and sufficient, so that it may be a help to him in what he undertakes of service. The prophets, peace be upon them, are not independent of insight and guidance, and that is only achieved through the connection of revelation. This characteristic was for Muhammad, peace be upon him. God Almighty said: 'Your Lord has not forsaken you, nor has He hated [you].' 
The second: alerting him to places of slip. For whoever delegates a task to one of his servants does not abandon him.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage explains the second main category of prophetic characteristics: those needed for nurturing the powers of prophethood (تربية قواها). This category also divides into two parts. 

First part: the continuous connection of the sources of revelation (اتصال مواد الوحي) to the prophet. The author uses an analogy: when a master delegates a task to a servant, he must support him with guidance and direction, even if the servant is capable. Similarly, prophets need ongoing guidance and insight from God, which is achieved through the uninterrupted flow of revelation. This characteristic is confirmed for Prophet Muhammad by the Quranic verse: 'Your Lord has not forsaken you, nor has He hated you' (93:3). 

Second part: alerting the prophet to places of slip (تنبيهه على مواقع الزلل). When a master delegates a task, he does not abandon the servant; rather, he warns him of potential mistakes. Thus, God guides the prophet to avoid errors in his mission. The text ends abruptly but implies God does not leave the prophet without guidance.

اتصال الوحي
تنبيه الزلل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are infallible on their own without any need for ongoing divine guidance.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that prophets require continuous revelation and divine warnings to avoid slips, even though they are chosen and capable.

Checkpoint
What is the second part of the second category (nurturing) of prophetic characteristics?
A) Connection of revelation
B) Bestowal of extra virtues
C) Alerting to places of slip
D) Divine selection by genus

Key Takeaway
Prophets require ongoing divine revelation and guidance to perform their mission and avoid errors; they are not left independent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If even the Prophet, the best of creation, was not independent of continuous guidance and warning, how can you afford to go a single day without seeking God's direction in the Quran? What does it reveal about your own spiritual pride if you feel you have 'outgrown' the need for regular reminders?
?
The passage teaches that God never abandons His prophet after entrusting him with a mission. What mission has God entrusted to you (e.g., family, community, faith), and how have you been living as if God has left you alone to handle it? In what specific area do you need to start asking for His warning and guidance today?
?
The verse 'Your Lord has not forsaken you' was revealed after a pause in revelation, comforting the Prophet. When have you felt spiritually 'forsaken' or distant from God, and how does this verse confront your feeling of abandonment? Are you willing to believe that the pause was not rejection but preparation for deeper guidance?

The Second Division of Prophetic Characteristics: Revelation and Warning
The author divides the second type of prophetic characteristic into two kinds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two sub-divisions of the prophetic special characteristic needed for nurturing faculties: the connection of revelation and divine correction for slips.

Core Idea
Prophets need both revelation and correction to fulfill their mission.

In this passage, the author continues his discussion of prophetic characteristics by focusing on the special quality needed for nurturing a prophet's faculties. He divides this into two essential aspects: being connected to revelation for guidance, and being alerted to slips for correction. These are illustrated with Quranic examples from the life of Prophet Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then the translation. Notice the division into two sub-kinds.
2
Identify the two sub-kinds
Find the two divisions: 'connection of the means of revelation' and 'alerting him to the places of slipping'. Understand how they are defined.
3
Understand the analogies
The author uses analogies from human delegation to explain why prophets need revelation and correction. Reflect on the reasoning.
4

The passage cites three verses: 93:3, 9:43, 8:67. See how each supports the sub-kind.
5

The author states these characteristics are mentioned for the seeker of guidance, not for the denier. Think about the audience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثاني لتربية قواها. وأما القسم الثاني من القسمين الأولين: وهو الخاصية التي يحتاج إليها لتربية قواها فينقسم أيضًا إلى قسمين: أحدهما: اتصال مواد الوحي به، فإن كل من قلد غيره عملاً من الأعمال فلابد أن يؤيده فيه بالإرشاد ويتابع لديه بالهداية وإن كان هو في نفسه مستقلاً كافيًا ليكون معونة له على ما يتولاه من خدمته. والأنبياء عليهم السلام لم يستغنوا عن التبصير والإرشاد، ولا يتم ذلك إلا باتصال الوحي، وهذه الخاصية كانت لمحمد عليه السلام قال الله تعالى: ﴿ ما ودعك ربك وما قلى ﴾. والثاني: تنبيهه على مواقع الزلل فإن من قلد عبدًا من عبيده فإنه لا يخليه عن التوقف على زلة منه بل ينبهه عليه ليكون سببًا لتثقيفه وأمانًا من الوقوع في مثله، فكذا في حق من أرسله الله تعالى، وهذه الخاصية كانت لنبينا محمد عليه السلام على ما قال عز وجل: ﴿ عفا الله عنك لم أذنت لهم ﴾ وقال: ﴿ ما كان لنبي أن يكون له أسرى ﴾. ثم ثبوت هاتين الخاصيتين وإن لم يقربهما الجاحد لرسالته، ولكن ذكرناهما لبيان تتمة حاله عند المسترشد.
The second section for nurturing his faculties. As for the second of the two first divisions: it is the special characteristic that he needs for nurturing his faculties, and it also divides into two divisions: One of them: the connection of the means of revelation to him. For whoever delegates someone else for a task must support him in it with guidance and follow him with direction, even if he himself is independently sufficient, so that it may be a help for him in what he undertakes of his service. The prophets, peace be upon them, were not independent of insight and guidance, and that is not accomplished except by connection of revelation. And this special characteristic was for Muhammad, peace be upon him. Allah Almighty said: 'Your Lord has not forsaken you, nor has He hated [you].' And the second: alerting him to the places of slipping. For whoever delegates a servant from among his servants does not leave him without watching for a slip from him, but rather alerts him to it so that it may be a cause for his correction and a safety from falling into something similar. Similarly for the one whom Allah Almighty sent. And this special characteristic was for our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, according to what He, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'Allah has forgiven you; why did you give them permission?' And He said: 'It is not for a prophet to have captives.' Then, the establishment of these two special characteristics, even if the denier of his message does not admit them, but we mentioned them to explain the completeness of his state for the seeker of guidance.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the second type of prophetic special characteristic (al-khāṣṣiyya) that a prophet needs for nurturing his faculties. The author divides this second type into two sub-kinds. The first sub-kind is the connection of the means of revelation (ittiṣāl mawādd al-waḥy). He argues that anyone who delegates a task to another must support him with guidance, and prophets are no exception. This connection was granted to Prophet Muhammad, citing Quran 93:3. The second sub-kind is alerting him to slips (tanbīhuhu ʿalā mawāqiʿ al-zalal). The author analogizes that a master watches over his servant and corrects him, so Allah corrects His prophet. This is supported by Quran 9:43 and 8:67. Finally, the author notes that these two characteristics are not conceded by deniers, but they are mentioned for the benefit of the seeker of guidance.

The First Two Special Characteristics: Proof by Tawatur
The author asserts the tawatur-based proof of the first two characteristics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the first two physical characteristics of the Prophet are established by tawatur and serve as a decisive proof for prophethood.

Core Idea
Tawatur provides certain knowledge that makes prophethood undeniable.

In this brief but crucial passage, the author establishes that the first two special characteristics of the Prophet are not based on mere opinion but on uninterrupted transmission (tawatur). This transmission creates certainty, turning these characteristics into an argument that no sincere denier can refute. Understanding this foundation is key to appreciating how prophetic signs function as proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice the concise structure: claim, evidence, conclusion.
2
Identify key terms
Find the terms 'خَاصِّيَّتَانِ أُولَيَانِ', 'التَّوَاتُر', 'حُجَّة', and 'دَلَائِل النُّبُوَّة'. Understand their meanings from the translation.
These terms are central to the argument.
3
Analyze the logic
The passage makes a conditional argument: if these characteristics are mutawatir, they are established; if established, they serve as a proof; and if the proofs of prophethood are established, prophethood is necessarily true.
This is a chain of certainty.
4
Reflect on tawatur
Consider why tawatur yields certainty. It is not a single report but mass transmission that precludes collusion.
5
Summarize the takeaway
The proof of prophethood relies on both rational and transmitted evidence. Tawatur bridges the gap.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الخاصيتان الأوليان فثابتتان بالتواتر، فيكون ثبوتهما حجة على الجاحد. وإذا ثبت في حقه دلائل النبوة وخواصها كانت نبوته ثابتة ضرورة، والله الموفق.
As for the first two special characteristics, they are established by tawatur (uninterrupted transmission), so their establishment is an argument against the denier. And if the proofs of prophethood and its special characteristics are established in his case, his prophethood is established necessarily, and Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the first two (physical) special characteristics of the Prophet are proven, and this proof establishes his prophethood. The author states that these characteristics are established by tawatur (concurrent transmission), which provides certain knowledge. Therefore, their existence serves as a decisive argument against anyone who denies his prophethood. Once the signs of prophethood are established, his prophethood is necessarily known. The passage concludes with a prayer: 'and Allah is the granter of success.'

Signs Binding on the Prophet: Chest Splitting, Gabriel, and Ascension
Listing of special proofs and refutation of Mu'tazila denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the special signs (dalālāt khāṣṣa) of Prophet Muhammad, why they also obligated belief in his own prophethood, and how the Mu'tazila denial of the chest-splitting incident is refuted by widespread transmission and Companions' testimony.

Core Idea
The Prophet's miracles confirm his prophethood not just for others, but for himself as well.

In this passage, the author continues listing miraculous signs unique to Prophet Muhammad. He first establishes a key principle: the same signs that oblige others to believe also oblige the Prophet himself to be certain of his mission. Then he recounts the famous event of the splitting of his chest, the washing of his heart, and the appearance of Gabriel, ending with the Night Journey. The Mu'tazila objection is addressed and refuted.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the full literal translation. Notice the shift from the general principle to specific incidents.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the discussion likely continues on the next page.
2
Identify the general principle
Find the sentence that states that signs binding others also bind the Prophet. Understand why the author mentions this—to show that the Prophet himself needed certainty.
This principle is key to connecting the signs to the Prophet's own belief.
3
List the special signs
From the passage, identify the specific signs: splitting of the chest, extraction/washing of the heart, Gabriel appearing in his true form, the Night Journey.
These are the 'special proofs' (dalālāt khāṣṣa) that distinguish the Prophet.
4
Examine the Mu'tazila objection and the refutation
The Mu'tazila denied the chest-splitting because they saw no wisdom in it. The author refutes them by citing widespread reports (akhbār mustafīḍa) and the Companions' direct observation of the scar.
This shows how theological objections can be overcome by transmitted evidence.
5
Reflect on the broader lesson
Consider how the author uses these signs to affirm the Prophet's status and to defend against deniers. What does this teach about the role of miracles in establishing prophethood?
The passage warns that denying one sign can open the door to denying all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم جميع ما كان من الأعلام والدلالات ملزمًا غيره الإيمان به كان ملزمًا عليه الاعتقاد أيضا أنه رسول، إذ هو يحتاج أيضًا إلى العلم بنبوته ورسالته، كما يحتاج غيره إلى ذلك. ثم كانت له دلالات خاصة من نحو شق بطنه في حال صغره، ونزع قلبه وشقه وغسله ورده إلى موضعه، والمعتزلة لم تعرف جهة الحكمة في ذلك فأنكرت جوازه مع ورود الأخبار المستفيضة به، وكان جحود هذا منهم فتحًا على المنكرين للرسالة باب جحود جميع آياته، وكلهم محجوجون بالنقل المشهور، وبمعاينة الصحابة رضي الله عنهم أثر ذلك في بطنه. ذلك ومن الدلائل الخاصة له ترائي جبريل عليه السلام على صورته وتدليه إليه ودُنُوّه منه وإراؤه الله تعالى إياه ملكوت السماوات ليلة المعراج كما فعل هذا
Then everything that was of signs and proofs binding others to believe in him was also binding on him to believe that he is a messenger, since he also needs knowledge of his prophethood and messengership, just as others need that. Then there were special proofs for him such as the splitting of his belly in his childhood, and the extraction of his heart, splitting it, washing it, and returning it to its place. The Mu'tazila did not know the aspect of wisdom in that, so they denied its permissibility despite the occurrence of widespread reports about it. And their denial of this was an opening for the deniers of the message to the door of denying all of his signs. They are all refuted by the well-known transmission and by the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, witnessing the effect of that in his belly. That, and among the special proofs for him are the appearance of Gabriel, peace be upon him, in his form, and his descending to him, his drawing near to him, and Allah showing him the dominion of the heavens on the night of the Ascension, as He did this...
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a listing and defense of additional special signs (dalālāt khāṣṣa) of Prophet Muhammad. First, the author makes a general principle: signs that oblige belief in the Prophet also oblige the Prophet himself to believe in his own messengership, as he too needs knowledge of it. Then he mentions specific signs: the splitting of the Prophet's chest in childhood, the removal, splitting, and washing of his heart, and its return. The Mu'tazila rejected this incident because they could not perceive its wisdom, despite widespread reports (akhbār mustafīḍa). The author warns that their denial opens the door for deniers to reject all signs. The proof against them is the well-known transmission (naql mashhūr) and the Companions' direct observation of the scar on his belly. Further signs mentioned are the appearance of Gabriel in his true form, descending and drawing near to the Prophet, and Allah showing him the dominion of the heavens on the Night of Ascension. The passage ends abruptly with 'as He did this' (kama faʿala hādhā), implying continuation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The Mu'tazila rejected a miracle because they couldn't see its wisdom. Are there teachings of Islam you resist because they don't immediately make sense to you? Will you trust the transmitted reports over your own reasoning, even when the wisdom is hidden?

The Second Characteristic: Divine Alerting to Mistakes
Describes the second characteristic: the Prophet being alerted to mistakes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second characteristic of prophethood: that prophets are alerted to their mistakes by God for correction and guidance.

Core Idea
Prophets are not flawless; their errors are corrected by divine alerting.

This passage focuses on the second characteristic of the Prophet: divine alerting to mistakes. Through an analogy of a master correcting a servant, the author shows that God corrects His prophets to refine them and protect others from similar errors. The Quranic verses cited provide concrete examples of this in the life of Prophet Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and analogy
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the analogy of the master and servant, which illustrates the rationale behind divine correction.
Notice how the author draws a parallel between human employment and divine selection.
2
Identify the Quranic proofs
Locate the two Quranic verses cited. Understand how they demonstrate God alerting the Prophet to a mistake.
The verses are from Surah At-Tawbah and Surah Al-Anfal.
3
Understand the purpose
Reflect on why the author mentions these characteristics even if disbelievers reject them. The goal is to guide the seeker of truth.
The passage emphasizes the completion (tamām) of the Prophet's state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني: تنبيهه على مواقع الزلل فإن من قلد عبدًا من عبيده فإنه لا يخليه عن التوقف على زلة منه بل ينبهه عليه ليكون سببًا لتثقيفه وأمانا من الوقوع في مثله، فكذا في حق من أرسله الله تعالى، وهذه الخاصية كانت لنبينا محمد عليه السلام على ما قال عز وجل: عَفَا اللَّهُ عَنكَ لِمَ أَذِنتَ لَهُمْ وقال: مَا كَانَ لِنَبِيٍّ أَن يَكُونَ لَهُ أَسْرَى ثم ثبوت هاتين الخاصيتين وإن لم يقربهما الجاحد لرسالته، ولكن ذكرناهما لبيان تتمة حاله عند المسترشد.
And the second: alerting him to places of mistake. For whoever employs a servant from his servants, he does not leave him without stopping him at a slip of his, but rather alerts him to it so that it may be a cause for his correction and safety from falling into its like. So likewise in the case of the one whom God Almighty sent. And this characteristic belonged to our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, as God Almighty said: 'God forgive you, why did you permit them?' and He said: 'It is not for a prophet to have captives.' Then the establishment of these two characteristics, even if the denier of his message does not acknowledge them, but we mention them to explain the completion of his state for the seeker of guidance.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the second characteristic of prophethood: that the Prophet is not free from human error but is alerted by God to his mistakes. The author gives an analogy: a master who employs a servant will not ignore his mistakes but correct him. Similarly, God did the same with Prophet Muhammad, citing two Quranic verses where Allah admonished him for his actions. The author then states that these two characteristics (the one mentioned and another not shown here) are mentioned even if the denier does not accept them, for the benefit of those seeking guidance.

Misconception: Some believe that prophets are infallible in all actions and never make any mistake.
Correction: This passage shows that prophets can have minor errors (zalal) that are corrected by divine alerting, serving as a means of refinement and guidance.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the second characteristic according to the passage?
A) To humiliate the Prophet
B) To correct and protect him from falling into similar mistakes
C) To demonstrate that prophets are sinless
D) To invalidate his prophethood

Key Takeaway
The second characteristic of prophethood is that God alerts the Prophet to his mistakes for correction and protection, as shown by Quranic examples.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time someone corrected you? Did you receive it as a mercy or as an attack? How does knowing that even the Prophet was corrected by God change how you should respond to correction? Will you now see correction as a sign of care?
?

?
Consider an area in your life where you are in authority. Do you allow those under you to correct you? Or do you demand absolute obedience like the master in the analogy? How can you imitate the Prophet's humility in accepting correction from God? What one step will you take this week to invite correction from a trusted advisor?

Tawatur as Proof for Prophethood Characteristics
Proof statement about tawatur and necessary prophethood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the first two characteristics of prophethood are established through mutawatir transmission and why this constitutes a necessary proof.

Core Idea
Widespread transmission makes the characteristics of prophethood undeniable evidence.

In this brief but powerful passage, the author establishes a foundational principle of prophetic proof: the first two characteristics of the Prophet are transmitted through such widespread, continuous reports (tawatur) that they become binding evidence against any denier. This logical step then leads to the necessary conclusion of prophethood. Let's unpack the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic carefully, then the English translation. Notice the logical connectors: 'fa' and 'wa-idha'.
The passage is short but dense; read it twice.
2
Identify the two parts of the argument
The passage has a clear two-step structure: first, the claim about tawatur, second, the conclusion. See how they connect.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'tawatur'
Consider why tawatur makes the evidence strong. Why would a denier be compelled by it?
Tawatur implies consensus through reliable transmission.
4
Understand the necessary conclusion
Notice that once the characteristics are proven, prophethood becomes 'necessarily' established. This is a strong epistemic claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الخاصيتان الأوليان فثابتتان بالتواتر، فيكون ثبوتهما حجة على الجاحد. وإذا ثبت في حقه دلائل النبوة وخواصها كانت نبوته ثابتة ضرورة، والله الموفق.
As for the first two characteristics, they are established by tawatur (widespread transmission), so their establishment is a proof against the denier. And if the proofs of prophethood and its characteristics are established in his regard, then his prophethood is established necessarily. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a proof statement. The author declares that the first two characteristics of the Prophet are transmitted via tawatur (widespread, continuous reports), making them indisputable evidence. He then draws a logical conclusion: if the proofs and characteristics of prophethood are established for the Prophet, then his prophethood is necessarily proven. The phrase 'God is the Grantor of success' is a closing supplication.

Key Terms
خاصيتان
تواتر
حجة
ضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think only miracles (mu'jizat) prove prophethood, but here the characteristics themselves, transmitted via tawatur, are also sufficient proof.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the first two characteristics, when established by tawatur, serve as proof against the denier. This shows that prophethood can be proven through widespread transmission of characteristics, not solely through miracles.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how are the first two characteristics established?
A) By rational argument
B) By tawatur (widespread transmission)
C) By the denier's acceptance
D) By the author's personal opinion

Key Takeaway
The first two characteristics of prophethood are proven by mutawatir transmission, making their establishment a conclusive proof that necessarily entails prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The characteristics of the Prophet ﷺ are established by tawatur—clear, undeniable evidence available to all. Have you truly surrendered to this reality in every area of your life, or do you find yourself still hesitating in some aspects? What is one specific area where you need to submit completely, starting today?
?
The passage calls the establishment of these characteristics a 'proof against the denier.' Are there times when you act like a denier—rejecting clear truths from Allah because they are inconvenient or demanding? Will you now accept the evidence and change your stance?
?
If the Prophet's prophethood is 'necessarily established,' what does that demand from you right now in terms of obedience, love, and following? What concrete step will you take today to align your life with this necessary truth?

Special Miracles: The Prophet's Confirmation and Refutation of Denial
Lists specific miracles and rebuts Mu'tazila denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the special miracles that confirmed the Prophet's messengership and how the Mu'tazila's denial of one miracle undermines belief in all.

Core Idea
The Prophet's own miracles strengthened his heart and proved his message to others.

Imam al-Nasafi lists specific miracles that were unique to the Prophet, such as the splitting of his chest and the greeting of stones. He then addresses the Mu'tazila's objection to the chest splitting, showing how their denial opens the door to rejecting all miracles. This passage teaches us that the Prophet himself needed confirmation, and that miracles serve both to reassure him and to prove his truth to others.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation to get the overall flow.
Notice the principle at the beginning: the Prophet also needed proof.
2
Identify the three special miracles
The passage mentions three specific miracles: the splitting of his chest as a child, the appearance of Gabriel and the Ascension, and the greeting of stones and trees. Find each one in the text.
Each miracle serves to confirm his prophethood.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila objection and refutation
The Mu'tazila denied the chest splitting because they did not see wisdom in it. The author refutes them by citing widespread reports and eyewitness testimony. Note the consequence: denying one miracle opens the door to denying all.
The refutation is based on transmitted knowledge (khabar mutawatir).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم جميع ما كان من الأعلام والدلالات ملزمًا غيره الإيمان به كان ملزما عليه الاعتقاد أيضا أنه رسول إذ هو يحتاج أيضًا إلى العلم بنبوته ورسالته، كما يحتاج غيره إلى ذلك. ثم كانت له دلالات خاصة من نحو شق بطنه في حال صغره، ونزع قلبه وشقه وغسله ورده إلى موضعه والمعتزلة لم تعرف جهة الحكمة في ذلك فأنكرت جواز مع ورود الأخبار المستفيضة به، وكان جحود هذا منهم فتحا على المنكرين للرسالة باب جحود جميع آياته وكلهم محجوجون بالنقل المشهور، وبمعاينة الصحابة رضي الله عنهم أثر ذلك في بطنه. ذلك ومن الدلائل الخاصة له ترائى جبريل عليه السلام على صورته وتدليه إليه ودنوه منه وإراؤه الله تعالى إياه ملكوت السماوات ليلة المعراج كما فعل هذا ومن هذا الجنس ما كان يقع من تسليم الحجر والشجر على النبي عليه السلام بالنبوة، فإذا ثبت بهذا النوع للرسول محل الرسالة ركن قلبه واطمأنت نفسه وارتبط جأشه وقويت منته، فأظهر الدعوة على بصيرة، ونفذ فيها بنشاط وقوة وكان ما يؤيد به بعد ذلك من المعجزات على سبيل إقامة البرهان على قومه بصحة دعوته لهم.
Then all that was of signs and proofs obliging others to believe in him was also obliging upon him to believe that he is a messenger, for he also needs knowledge of his prophethood and his message, just as others need that. Then he had special proofs such as the splitting of his belly in his childhood, and the extraction of his heart, its splitting, washing, and returning to its place. And the Mu'tazila did not know the aspect of wisdom in that, so they denied its occurrence despite the widespread reports about it. And their denial of this opened the door for those who deny the message to deny all his signs. And all of them are refuted by the well-known transmission and by the eyewitness of the Companions, may God be pleased with them, to the effect of that on his belly. That, and among his special proofs was the appearing of Gabriel, peace be upon him, in his form, and his descending near him, and his closeness to him, and God showing him the kingdom of the heavens on the night of the Ascension, as He did this. And of this kind is what used to occur of the greeting of the stone and the tree to the Prophet, peace be upon him, with prophethood. So when by this type the station of messengership is established for the messenger, his heart is steadied, his soul is reassured, his courage is strengthened, and his resolve is fortified. So he proclaims the call with insight, and pursues it with activity and strength. And what follows of miracles supports him by way of establishing proof to his people of the soundness of his call to them.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof of the Prophet's special miracles. The author first states a principle: the same proofs that oblige others to believe also oblige the Prophet himself to know his status. Then he lists specific miracles: (1) the splitting of his chest in childhood, which the Mu'tazila denied due to not seeing wisdom in it, but the author refutes them by citing widespread reports and the Companions' eyewitness testimony. (2) The appearing of Gabriel and the showing of the heavens during the Night of Ascension. (3) The greeting of stones and trees. The author explains the purpose: these miracles strengthen the Prophet's heart and resolve, enable him to call with insight and strength, and later miracles serve as proof to his people.

Key Terms
أعلام
دلالات
شق بطنه
المعتزلة
أخبار مستفيضة
ترائى جبريل
المعراج
تسليم الحجر والشجر
ركن قلبه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet did not need any proof for himself; he already knew he was a prophet.
Correction: The passage states that the Prophet also needed knowledge of his prophethood, and the special miracles served to confirm his heart and strengthen his resolve.

Checkpoint
Why did the Mu'tazila deny the miracle of the splitting of the Prophet's chest?
A) They did not know the aspect of wisdom in it
B) They found it contrary to reason
C) The reports were weak
D) They were not Companions

Key Takeaway
The special miracles of the Prophet served both to confirm his own heart and to provide proof to others, and denying any one miracle undermines the entire prophetic claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the Prophet's chest being split as a child, do you find your heart accepting it fully, or does your mind seek a 'rational' explanation? Why?
?
The Prophet's heart was 'steadied' by these signs. What would it take for your heart to be steadied in your faith such that you call to the truth with the same insight and strength?
?
The Mu'tazila denied a miracle because they could not see its wisdom. In your own life, are there aspects of revelation that you have subtly rejected because they don't fit your sense of 'wisdom'? What will you do about it starting today?

The Greeting of Trees and Stones as a Proof of Prophethood
The author concludes a chapter, citing the greeting of inanimate objects as proof of prophethood and explaining why he wrote at length.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the greeting of inanimate objects served as a dual-purpose miracle: strengthening the Prophet's own heart and providing proof for his community.

Core Idea
Miracles first strengthen the prophet's heart, then prove his message to others.

This passage concludes a chapter on prophethood by highlighting a subtle miracle: the greeting of stones and trees to the Prophet. The author then explains why he devoted so much space to this topic—to counter the rising heresy of his time. Reading this, you will see how miracles serve both the prophet's inner certainty and the external proof of his mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full translation. Notice how the greeting is presented as a form of evidence for prophethood.
Pay attention to the sequence: the greeting establishes the station, then the prophet's heart becomes firm.
2
Identify the dual purpose of miracles
The passage mentions two effects: first, the Prophet's heart becomes firm and tranquil; second, subsequent miracles are used to establish proof for his people. Identify both in the text.
3
Reflect on the author's justification
The author explains why he wrote at length despite promising brevity. Find the reasons (heresy, slander of the impious) and consider the importance of context in theological writing.
This shows that the author's methodology is responsive to the needs of his time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن هذا الجنس ما كان يقع من تسليم الحجر والشجر على النبي عليه السلام بالنبوة، فإذا ثبت بهذا النوع للرسول محل الرسالة ركن قلبه واطمأنت نفسه وارتبط جأشه وقويت منته، فأظهر الدعوة على بصيرة، ونفذ فيها بنشاط وقوة وكان ما يؤيد به بعد ذلك من المعجزات على سبيل إقامة البرهان على قومه بصحة دعوته لهم. فإذا انتهينا إلى هذا فلنختم الباب، وقد خرجنا في هذا الباب عما شرطنا في أول الكتاب من الإيجاز، وطولنا فيه نوع تطويل، وبالغنا نوع مبالغة، وإن كان الاستقصاء في الباب يقتضي استغراق دفاتر، فعلنا ذلك لظهور الإلحاد في زماننا وطعن كثير من الخلعاء في أمر النبوة، فأردت بذلك حسم مادة شرهم، ودفع معرتهم عن ضعفه المسلمين والله خير مؤيد ومعين.
And of this kind is what occurred of the greeting of stone and tree to the Prophet, peace be upon him, with prophethood. So when by this type the station of messengership was established for the Messenger, his heart became firm, his soul tranquil, his composure steady, and his resolve strengthened. Then he proclaimed the call with insight, and carried it out with energy and strength. And what he was supported with thereafter of miracles was by way of establishing proof to his people of the correctness of his call to them. When we have reached this point, let us conclude the chapter. And in this chapter we have departed from what we stipulated at the beginning of the book regarding brevity, and we have lengthened it with a kind of prolongation, and we have gone to excess in a kind of exaggeration—although thoroughness in the chapter would require filling entire notebooks. We did this because of the appearance of heresy in our time and the slander of many of the impious regarding the matter of prophethood. So I intended thereby to cut off the root of their evil and to repel their harm from the weak among the Muslims. And Allah is the best supporter and helper.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is the conclusion of a chapter on prophethood. The author first describes a type of miracle: the greeting of stones and trees to the Prophet, acknowledging his prophethood. This event establishes for the Prophet his station as a messenger. Consequently, his heart becomes firm, his soul tranquil, his composure steady, and his resolve strengthened. With this inner certainty, he proclaims his call with insight and energy. The subsequent miracles serve as proofs for his people, demonstrating the truth of his message. The author then signals the end of the chapter, acknowledging that he has departed from his earlier promise of brevity. He explains that he has gone into lengthy detail because of the prevalence of heresy in his time and the attacks of the impious (khul'ā') on the institution of prophethood. His purpose is to cut off the root of their evil and protect the weaker Muslims from their harm. He concludes by invoking Allah as the best supporter and helper.

Key Terms
تسليم الحجر والشجر
النبوة
الرسالة
معجزات
إقامة البرهان
الإلحاد
الخلعاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are only for proving prophethood to others and have no effect on the prophet's own certainty.
Correction: The passage shows that the greeting of stones and trees first established the station of prophethood in the Prophet's heart, making it firm and tranquil, before being used as a proof for others.

Checkpoint
What effect did the greeting of the stone and tree have on the Prophet according to this passage?
A) It confused him and made him doubt his mission.
B) It strengthened his heart, made his soul tranquil, and increased his resolve.
C) It caused him to delay his public proclamation.
D) It was irrelevant to his inner state.

Key Takeaway
The greeting of inanimate objects to the Prophet serves both to confirm his own heart and to provide a miracle for his community, a sign of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Before you call others to truth, do you seek to strengthen your own heart through Allah's signs—or do you rush ahead relying only on your own strength? What one practice can you adopt this week to increase your inner certainty like the Prophet's heart was firmed?
?
The author wrote extensively to protect the weak from heretical attacks. Who in your life is spiritually vulnerable—a new Muslim, a seeker, or someone with doubts? What specific step will you take this week to shield them from harmful ideas?
?
If even the Prophet—the best of creation—needed miracles to settle his heart, what does that say about your own need for constant reminders of Allah? How will you respond today to the 'greetings' of creation that point to Him, so that your soul may be tranquil?
